Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of which one method is such that you make three cauteries or four, aligning them according to the length of the mouse, as per the figure of the liver cautery we have said before; and do not press your hand against the entire cautery, and let the patient be often on his back. And another method of cautery is such that you heat the cautery with two prongs, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the keur which is at the location of the mouse, or where the wounds of the patient come from the left side, and let the elevations be such that you lift the keur according to the shape, according to the length of the body, and the cauteries should be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After letting the two inflamed nerves burn until the cores are pierced from the other side, then remove the cautery, and thus it will have four. And if you see, cauterize the entire cautery to three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the treatment when it has gotten gangrene over a long time, and this affects even the other wounds mentioned before.
de ydropisie	from dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	The cautery is not effective for dropsy, except in the manner called "asclytes.
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat it according to the methods we have mentioned in divisions, and your treatment is not effective, then you must make four cauteries around the mouth, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the spleen, two behind the back on the spine, and one at the anus; and let the cauteries be close to the skin of the heart.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After let the cautery open to drain pus long enough, and do not leave the treatment of the patient after the cautery; and healing would be hastened, and both intentions would be fulfilled with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery for the belly should be like those we have shown before; and that for the back should be olive-shaped, as described earlier.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in those who are hydropic and are full of yellow bile, you must cauterize on the back of the foot between the thumb and the ring finger; and hold your hand with the cautery without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply, otherwise it would go beyond the yellow bile, and let the cauterization be according to this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After make on two legs two cauterizations in each leg at the point of the scalpel; and let the cauterizations long, one below the knee in front and the other above, between the legs; and leave the cauterizations long without curing, until the bile comes out; after that cure the other wounds as we have said.
de la menoison	of the dislocation
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When the solution of the belly comes from cold and moisture, while the retentive and digestive virtues in the stomach and intestines are weakened and cannot be cured by usual means; and you see the patient suffering greatly with strong virtue, make the great cauterization on the stomach according to what he has spoken about earlier regarding the cauterization of the stomach, at the circular cauterization. And four small cauterizations inside the mouth for each small cauterization, and two cauterizations on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see abundant moisture and the patient suffering, apply the cautery to the handle, and one cautery to each thigh, and two small cauteries on the stomach below the large, for the cure is beneficial when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	for the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are open or internal, one or more, and are old, being large cold and moist humors corrupted, and have been treated as we said in the divisions, if it does not profit, apply cauteries: III on the spine of the back, that which is just above the iliac crest, little by little in a triangular pattern, and one cautery under the navel II twice; and if you think his stomach is cold, and the meat does not cook, and one sees the fauce swelling, then apply the large cautery on the stomach as it was said before, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen for the entire clavicle; and leave the cautery open long enough.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment, let the wound heal until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the carbuncle which is called "thelul
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you treat the carbuncle, heat the cautery to seem like a razor, and then place it completely ablaze over the carbuncle being treated; and let your hand remain there until the vein begins to appear, at which point the flesh will start to blister; do this once or twice, and if there is much carbuncle, cauterize each part as we have said; after that, apply beneficial ointments until it heals; and if you cauterize with a large cautery over abscesses, it will have greater help.
de plaie mal curee	of a wound poorly treated
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure a surgery or incision, as we will discuss in its place, comes a sickness that can only be cured by fire cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When there is an abscess and it is inflamed and filled with rotten moisture, you should probe the entire length of the abscess with a fine probe, and make sure you know the full length of the abscess.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After heating the cautery to the burn, apply it to the abscess according to how far the probe entered, and reapply the cautery until the rotten and corrupted flesh is burned, one or two or three times depending on the amount needed; and be careful not to burn the nerves or large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and the intestine, beware of these signs, and do not make them in living flesh, for they are not permanent; after curing the flesh until it is healed, and if the flesh is hardened and the matter is removed over a long time, then know that the flesh is completely healed; and if the matter is not removed, know that the flesh is torn and corrupted at the root; and in such cases, as we will say in their place.
de la maladie des reins	Of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from cold and great wind comes to the kidneys, and does not affect a woman, then you must make a cautery on the kidneys from one side and the other using the clavile cautery as we have already said; and if we cauterize in the middle, there will be three cauteries in line, and they will provide greater aid.
de la vessie	from the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, causing the patient to retain urine, then you should apply a fire cautery in the lower part above the bladder, where the hairs begin around the navel, both on the right and left. Each cautery should be as long as one inch of your thumb; and you should make the cautery over the back, or where you may need it. Let the cauteries be regular according to the form previously described.
de la marris	of the wart
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the wart is cold and moist, and does not allow conception, and the flowers are corrupted and their termination is delayed; and when they come, great pain is felt: then you should make three cauteries around the vulva, as we have said or those for the bladder, and two cauteries over the back; let the cauteries be regular, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the thick mucus descends to the socket of the hip, and for this reason it dislocates from its place, the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the cause is found in the departure of the joint space. Then you must cauterize the patient on the socket of the hip with a cautery resembling a circle, and mark around the space inside the socket as it turns, so that the socket is within the circle; and the cautery should be such as those used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you do not have such a cautery at hand, make three cauteries from olive oil, and let the cauteries be as perfect as all the rest; and cure him until he is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the socket of the hip, and it is from cold or moisture, and the patient has been treated as we said in the division and the treatment does not work, and the illness is old: then it must be that you purge the patient of the large humors with foul pills or other good pills similar.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	Afterwards, you apply the cautery; and the manner of the cautery is according to two methods: that is to say, with hot medicines together, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is in many ways. Of these, one method is as follows: you apply three triangular cauteries in this form, and they should be of good depth and large, with an interval between each cautery the thickness of two fingers, and let the cauteries be olive oil-based; another time, a cautery is made in the middle on the head of the hip, so there are four according to this form.
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, cauterize with the cautery of the circle that we have already described in the dislocation of the hip; but do it in such a manner that the circle contains all of the hip, and all the parts of the thigh be burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the way we treat sciatica, when the pain remains in the hip and does not extend to the thigh or the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes to the thigh and the leg, then make two cauteries where the patient says the pain is located, and one above the ankle on the left side a little; and let the cautery be either cutaneous or burn the thickness of the thigh; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the toes or near them, cauterize where he feels the pain with three or four cauteries called "poins".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if the skill is, and if the pain be below the knee towards the thigh, then make the cautery with the surgical or circular cautere, and take good care in all thy cauteries that thou leave not too much of the cautere so as to burn the nerves and the great arteries, and that thou do not make more harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who made a cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they left it such that the leg was all swollen, and the foot as well, and the foot was pierced and corrupted altogether.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After an abdominal solution from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pains are in two parts together, make the cautery in one and in the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise men said about the cautery of the hip, as follows: make such an iron and let it be at the end as thick as a finger or a little less, and let them be interwoven and let there be between each interweave the space of one inch; and let the interweaves above two parts, and let them be like nuts, and have the hand made of iron well crafted; and this is its form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated until it is completely red and emits sparks, and then place it on the socket of the painful hip, and turn it over to the healthy side; and apply the cautery once with the cautery hot, and leave it for three days; and then make a plaster with butter, and keep the wound open long enough; after the ointment treatment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use this fire cautery little due to fear of its effect, and we see few who use it; nevertheless, those who can endure it should apply it where it takes effect.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The fire cautery in medicine is such that you make the instrument of tongs in which hangs the wick of the lamp, and it should be made of brass or iron on one side long, and at the height of two fingers, and each should have the thickness of a thumb; and they should be open above and below, and join together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After placing the hip box on the patient lying on their side, press your hand firmly over the hip box; then pour between the two circles of hot coals that are heated by fire to a slight degree, and let it remain for about an hour or so, and allow the patient to feel the heat and the burning from it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is found as a bite or from fire; and when the bite has passed, withdraw your hand with the instrument and lift the hip gently, and leave thus for three days, and apply butter until the blackness of the scalding is removed; and let him lie for three days until corruption is drawn out; and this would be the last aid after the treatment with ointments until he is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has extended to the thigh or to the leg, apply the instrument gently according to what you have done for the hip; and this is the way of warm application, and I have written about it in the treatise on the rectification of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and quicklime, as much of one as the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	or there be a small hole defaced so that the point of a razor might enter; and put over this one another pot well leaded, and put on alkali and wax sweet on it until there be two above the powders which thou wilt have well strained by hand; and let it thus until it descend wax and juice or water and lead, then take all that wax and cast it on alkali and on wax as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then it will be very watery and is administered in many works of medicine and in cauteries of other members. For it makes as much work as fire, and to other medicines with which one cauterizes well the hip thus with terebinth, honey, anacardium, wax with soap; all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a treatment where a noble was cured of the pain in the hip and sciatic vein, and the good lord much, and says that no other treatment was done, and he was cured after only one time when this treatment was done, and he bathed as he instructs hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says that you should take fresh and dry verdigris, grind it a great deal with a little grease, and apply it to the hip and thigh and leg where the pain resides, and cover it; and let it remain for three hours and by the quantity that the patient no longer feels the heat.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter a bath while his body is somewhat warmed, and make him go to bed, and the pain will leave entirely and he will be cured.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use a fire cautery with such medicines if it is not after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with sheep's fat, it helps much; and the cauterization should be done in such a manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take wool and grease it with old oil, and apply it to the hollow between the big toe and the other toe called the fossiculus.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	Afterwards, take dry sheep's fat, and heat it on fire until it becomes hot coals, and place it on the wool, and let it remain until it is extinguished; and do this again, and continue in this manner until you think by sense that it has reached the hip, and the pain has ceased; and this method of cauterization is called "sheep fat cauterization.
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain from the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back from falling or percussion or from too great an evacuation or from similar spread of cold matter, none of these circumstances call for cautery, but only in the case of infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	After that, if the patient is void of foul pills or other similar matters, make three lines signed with enche on the back where the pain resides, and in each line use five cauteries or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can endure; and let the cauteries be made according to the cautery called "poins"; and if you see, make three or four cauteries at the medium clavile according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This sickness often comes to small children, and the signs of the beginning are that they have a tight throat when they wake, and fear; and you find in the last spine of the back and in us the appearance that comes upon the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and it needs to be treated, cauterize it with the circular fire cautery according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cauterization for each part of the spine increases.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, cauterize between the spines with a sharp fire cautery two or three lines wide, and let the points be close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After treating the limb until it is healed as we have said, be sure not to apply a fire cautery in swelling that is due to nerve damage.
de la dolor des jointes	of joint pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain is due to moisture spread throughout each limb of the body, and when pain comes from the feet, which doctors call "podagre" properly, and when it is caused by cold and cannot be cured with treatments or medicines, it is treated as follows: make many fire cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is need to prick the face of the foot, let the cautery be as wide as what we claim "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come down to the knees and other joints, and this happens often, then make a cautery on each knee three or four times from each part, for the entire olive oil cautery; and if you need more, do more, but keep your hand out no longer than until the coals of the heart are extinguished.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and the back, then apply the cautery as we have said in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make punctures two lines apart; and if there remains any pain in the fingers, make punctures on each joint and over the hair of the hand; and if the pains come down to the knees or down to the shoulders, then cauteryize each part, and give good governance to the patient and mild medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you make good governance of it and purge phlegm, it will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the side
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When a rupture comes in the groin, and the bellies descend into the scrotum, this is new and needs care. When you see it needs to be treated, do not let him eat that day; and give him things that release wind from his stomach, so that the contents descend from his abdomen. After that, make him sit on his back between your hands, and instruct him to hold up his scrotum until the bellies are repaired, then lower them with your fingers, and mark over the rupture under the bone of the thigh, and make a sign that resembles half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery as is its form.
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until it is white and gives off scent.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the bowels in their place; and the ministers hold their hand so they do not return. Work well on the thighs for the patient, and put the cook and the squire on the thighs, and the other one on the foot which holds the hands. Then place the cautery at the sign on your whole hand, and keep it straight and hold it until you reach the bone. And if you do not reach the bone the first time, repeat it again another time until you come to the bone. And carefully watch that the bowels do not protrude when you make the cautery; that you do not burn them; and that thereby the patient does not die or suffer other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not come to the bone with the fire cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it must be that the fire cautery for children is subtle according to the measure of their size, and for large people as great according to their measure; after three days, cure the area of the cautery with butter until the scalding is removed; afterwards, apply other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient rest on their back for forty days until the wound is well healed; and it must be that their nourishment is prolonged, so that the boils do not burst when they are taken to rooms.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wants to rise, provide him with a well-made bandage, and let him rest for another forty days; have good rest, and let him work little and avoid too much drinking and eating, and too much loud noise; and when he follows this instruction, he will be completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say after the treatment to shave in his chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not increase, then let them make the fire cautery according to its quantity, and be heated one-third of the chord; after the treatment according to what we have said; and none of the ancients have said that one should cauterize at a III angles in this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but mark the center line first and draw a line along the width above the rupture, and another below it, and hold your hand through all the cautery.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterizations are lighter and more soothing.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any limb, due to falling or injury, and that pain lasts a long time, and the cure of medicine does not help, then it must be cauterized with the cautery called "poins," and the cauterizations should be according to the length of the limb and its size and weakness and its virtue and its location of twists and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If the pain is relieved by the first cauterization, that is well; but if not, you must repeat the other cauterization over it, because such is the custom that it must change to the limb nearest to it, so you must make the cauterizations until the patient is cured.
de meselerie	of leechcraft
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The diseases are often cured once by the fire cautery with great help, especially those that come from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	When you see the wound is to be cauteryed, take care that the disease is in its beginning stage, and if it is cured as we have said in the division, and does not swell or remain, and you doubt that corruption might spread throughout the patient, then make five cauteries on the head: I place one on the forehead near the hairline, and another at the back towards the crown of the head; and II on the two horns of the head, and III behind on the occipital bone; and leave your hand there until the cautery reaches the bone, and until the skin is removed so that the vapors from the gross humors can escape; and make a cautery on the mice according to what is described before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the mezererie is scattered everywhere; and it clearly appears, then you should cauterize with these cauteries that we have said or chief, and the cautery on the nose, and two on the spine of the neck, and six on the spine of the back, and one large one on the breast and another laterally, and two on the ribs, and two on the tendons of the foot, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the palms; and beware of the nerves that are behind the heel, that you do not burn them; and at no time make a cautery on the bone of the elbow, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more you make a cautery, the more you do help, and they profit from it; and know that the sick do not feel pain at the cautery as the healthy do, because their body is already all corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it must be that the cauteries be large and small according to the members and joints, according to those you find in manner of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After the wound is cleansed with flour of wheat and honey and other dressings until it heals.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes to any member and is treated with medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not yet healed, then make cauteries on the member according to the size and smallness of the member; and let the cautery be a little within the thickness of the skin. Then dress with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes a cautery is made with the hand and with the foot and with the back, at the end of the nerve that paralyses the member, and thus the swelling is removed; and in any case, no one should do it unless they are knowledgeable about the members and the outlets of the moving nerves of the body.
de albaras	of leeches
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is mature, and medical remedies are of no use, then cauterize with a slightly hot cautery, according to the thickness of the skin, until the white color is removed and its color changes; then cure with flour of wheat, lentils, rose oil, and plantain leaves, and blood from a donkey and cherry, one part of each; mix all together, apply with a cloth, and keep on the body until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the treatment for a chancre by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a chancre begins to appear, and you see it stop, cauterize around the chancre with a circular cautery.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And truly the wise said that one should make a fire cautery also in the middle of the ulcer; and truly this does not seem good to me, for I fear it may be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already wanted it to happen once; and more suitable is that it be cauterized between, at the cautery called "circule," as we said many times about cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When some have an illness called "adubelati," and it delays death or due to the superfluity it causes or the age of the patient (that is, too old) and he has little blood, or due to the tension; and you see that it should hasten its death: then cauterize around much of the skin with many small cauteries by pricking; after, leave it thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	She will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierce through the entire cautery, heat the cautery with what is of its form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of that disease called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced through the heart, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it on the other side in this manner so that the course of the putrefaction is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the fire cure with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another manner of disease is called "corrodens," and it is nothing more than a corruption of the member, for it eats away at the members as fire does to dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this illness in a patient who can endure cautery with all fire, then heat the clavile cauteries very little and much, according to what is suitable for the patient where the illness is; after the cautery from all sides until you erradicate all the corruption, and let nothing remain of it, that all that is corrupted be removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then let it be for three days, and place endured hot pieces on the cautery wounds with oil until the scalds from the fire are removed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the application of ointments producing flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if after three days flesh healthy does not arise, that is good; and if it does not, then repeat the cautery on what remains corrupted from the wounds.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this mixture has been sometimes cured with medicinal water instead of the fire cautery; but nevertheless, the fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already said the cure of the medicinal water in the division: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of corns that come from the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that from the feet, due to blisters, a disease arises called "clos" according to our understanding, and it is a large, painful lump.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauterization for this disease is done in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	This means cauterization with fire, and cauterization with hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is when you heat the cautery tip as if it were a church spire pen, and it should be made of good iron to fit around the nail in all directions, and have thin edges; then put everything hot on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it reaches the bottom of the nail; and leave it thus for three days until it begins to rot; then apply a plaster of wild mallows crushed with salt, and keep the plaster on overnight, and the nails will fall out and be uprooted from their roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then apply ointment to the wound until it heals.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted by burns on the body, and this happens frequently in hands and feet, you must apply a hot cautery to it; and it is done thus: take a rod of charcoal or iron, or a church spire pen, and place it over the nail and the althea (which refers to porre roots for warts); and put the rod on such that it penetrates all around, then add some hot water, and hold your hand well, pressing your hand as you turn so that the margin of the rod comes to the root of the nail, and may find the hot water deep path down to the root; and let the patient endure a bit the burning from the hot water for an hour; then leave it thus, and it will uproot itself completely from all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Afterwards, do one after another until you cleanse all these that are in the body, then treat the wounds that generate flesh.
li cure dou trembler	the cure for trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some tremble from cold or nerves, or from quartan fever or other fevers, it is fitting that you make four or four cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between each vertebra; one at the feet, and one on the stomach with the olive-shaped cautery. If this does not stop the trembling, speed will be given to the health of the cold disease.
des pustules puans	pus-filled pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes apparent by the smell of the body bathed, or pus-filled pustules, that come from corrupt matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If it is necessary upon the appearance of each head of the pustule to make a cautery: a thin fire cautery from juniper wood, with its point heated over the fire, or from the long root of arnica, or with the lentil-shaped cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And sometimes the cautery is applied at the beginning when they appear in this manner, and it prevents them from growing further, but the excess that causes them is relieved, and they are cured; but it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great hemorrhages from the artery that is cut during the wound, or in incising an abscess, or with the cautery on the member, and similar things; and it is a most grievous thing to stink.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And whenever this happens to anyone, hasten to place your index finger on the wound of the vein, and hold it tightly until the bleeding is appeased beneath your finger, and no more fluid comes out; then put the olive fire cauteries, both small and large, on until they are all red hot; then take I, or a large one or a small one according to the wound and the limb in which the artery runs, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and keep the cautery there until the blood is coagulated.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it leaps out when you remove your finger from above the vein, and the cauteries are still hot, so take quickly another from those on the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this one after another until the blood is coagulated; and guard that you do not burn the nerve which is nearby, and that no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when blood flows from the artery, one cannot properly coagulate it themselves if the artery is large, unless it is by one of the four methods that we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction when it has not been treated, or by strong ligature with thread, or by medicines placed on which have power to coagulate blood; and let it be tied and held immediately.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will treat the stench of lime tightly with cloths or put burning things on it or other similar things, if it does not help much, then do something else.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and they have neither sight nor medicine present, they should place their index finger on the wound from the vein as we have said, and extend it well so that it is filled with stench above the wound and above the vein; and do not move the finger, but frequently rub the flesh with cold water until it is very cold, so that the wind is frozen and engorged and filled with stench; and proceed to make incisions and use cauteries and medicines as needed.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book of wound treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter where it is necessary to use a fire cautery or a burning medicine, and about the ointments and their causes and the instruments and forms of the cauteries; and I placed that chapter from the elbow to the feet, and I will proceed in this chapter by the same way because one finds more easily what one wishes.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And since I begin this one, it is necessary, dear friend, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first on fire cauteries, and for this reason, greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I advise you that you not undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many people come for treatments in various ways.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	If they come so afflicted with their illness that they die lightly from the fever they have contracted, and from the greatness of their wickedness; one must be afraid of these.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And among these there are those who give you their word, saying: "Wait, I am cured"; but the disease is fierce.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting that you consent to those who come to you in this manner, but put more careful consideration into your honor than into your greed, and do not give your word rashly but wisely of what you are certain and have experienced. And use prognosis and indication in the treatments of your patients for whose health this will be helpful; and this will aid you in gaining a good reputation, and glory, and lasting memory.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear child, Our Lord gives you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to inspire from the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered this chapter by speaking of chapters, according to that which was before in the chapter on fire cauteries, that I spoke of from the head down to feet, because you find it more easily what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	from the head full of fluid
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness comes very often to children at birth, and when the midwives grip too tightly the head of the child; and sometimes it comes from the reason given that we do not know.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease occur except in children, and among all those I have seen, death hastened; for this reason, it seems to me that it would be best to abandon the work in partial healing.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I have seen the child whose shoulder was full of fluid, and the head grew larger each day to the point it could no longer bear it; the moisture increased beneath the scapula, between the heart and bone; the work is such that if the moisture is between the heart and bone, and the abscesses are small, you should make a large incision through the head; let it be as long as two of our fingers, as long as the moisture extends; and see here the form of the spatumile:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is greater, and the abscess is larger, make two cuts in a cross-like manner, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and the signs you see are the corners of the mouth open on each side, and a sharp pain shoots out when you press it with your hand from within, and this does not respond: then you must make three cuts in the forehead according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after incising, extract all the moisture out.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After holding the cuts with bandages and powders, and putting wine and oil on them, leave them this way for five days; then remove the bandage, and treat the wound with cloths and ointments, and let the forehead heal evenly. Then give the patient dry meat with little moisture until the limb is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you look for the center of the abscess and the accumulation of pus; for it is sometimes in front; sometimes behind; sometimes on the right; and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut then the skin where the abscess is centered, and where the pus accumulates, making a cut according to what you can do; and beware that you do not cut an artery; and let the blood flow freely, so that the patient dies from the discharge of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of rheumatism
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When someone has a disease called "catarre" in the eyes or the testicles, and the disease is longstanding, and medical treatment does not help, then the last resort is to use the cautery by which one will cauterize the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you see the eyes swollen, the patient should turn his head; afterward, rub the area with a rough cloth until the arteries are visible, then squeeze the patient's neck completely with the cloth; then look where the vein lies, and the lobes of both sides are behind the ears, and they are slightly raised; then mark the lobes with ink, then cut each one with a sharp spatule from two sides, so that the cut reaches the bone, and this should be done by the side of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, place the spatule beneath the artery and cut above, cutting as twice through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, the blood flows out continuously upwards.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to touch, you must measure the length of a thumb three times, then prick and cut until reaching the bone; the amount of blood that should be let out is six denarii, and by chance a bit more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the filling of the artery; then look at the wound: if there remains over the bone point of syphacia, if the cloth that we apply over the abscess does not change, then drain the wound and bind it, and treat with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	And if the artery does not open to touch, you must measure the length of a thumb three times, then prick and cut until reaching the bone; the amount of blood that should be let out is six denarii, and by chance a bit more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the filling of the artery; then look at the wound: if there remains over the bone point of emigrainne, if the cloth that we apply over the abscess does not change, then drain the wound and bind it, and treat with ointment until it is healed.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old migrainne comes and acute catarrh, due to the moisture of tears and the heats in the temples and ancient soreness and similar things, and it is treated with methods of medical cures and all those things do not profit him, then extract the arteries in the temples and use cauteries, as we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extracting them is that the patient pull back the hairs on his temples, and find where the artery opens in the temple, for it opens well through its pulsation, and is little responsive elsewhere except in some very cold people; and if it is responsive, the patient grasps the neck of the artery with some cloth, then rubs the area with a rough cloth, and rinses the area with hot water until the artery appears clearly; then take a splint from which this is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	then scarify the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then draw it up with the forceps and detach well the threads beneath each part; and if the artery is fine, turn it with the point of the curver and incise that part according to the size of the two heads.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	If it is not incised, it will not burst entirely.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out blood from six cuts, up to three; and if the artery is large, you must tie it in two places with a double strong silk thread, so that putrefaction does not occur before the suddenness of the wound, and hemorrhage decorrupts; then incise the excess that is between the two ties at that same hour, and afterward, if you see, cauterize the cut with the knife cautery down to the bone as the heads are cauterized; and this is the major work, if the patient has no fever and is of hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cauteries are helpful to end moistures: because they are of greater help against moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For the extraction of arrows, it is necessary to fill the socket with old cotton and place a well-made tent over it; and when you remove it, it should be treated with dry medicines that promote flesh growth and tents until it is healed; and if there is no cork from the artery as much as you work on it, you must hurry by cautery where you apply the cotton of vitriol and squeeze with your hand to ensure the arrow is extracted; and if you do not have this at hand, place your thumb over the socket so that the arrow is frozen, and wet the socket with cold water until the arrow stops moving, and it should be held as necessary; and what is more moist and lighter in the extraction of the arrow is that you cautery the vein from two parts of this cutting cautery, but the cuttings should be well thick to ward off heat for a longer time.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too cold, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two knives a thickness of about an inch, and then when you signet them to the two leeches, and you heat the iron until it comes just to the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and let them be spaced apart between the two heads because they are not completely cauterized with this cautery from end to end; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When tears from the eyes are flowing down veins that are above the temple of the eye socket, and medicine treatment does not help, and you see the face of the patient turning red, and feel tremors on the forehead; and the eyes are cold and moist so that the hair papers fall out, and the papers are heated and scorched by the heat of the tears, it needs this treatment.
