Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And the ancients called it "cure contuse", and you should do this for the patient who has this disease: if he has any hairs on his forehead, let him have them; then make three equal cuts or incisions along the length of the forehead; and let one of these incisions be as deep as two digits below the forehead, and the other two on either side above the sinews, but avoid incising the arteries that are above the sinews; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the lower jaw bones, and each wound should be the size of three digits in width; and have prepared a piece of sponge and much flannel to wipe the blood, then apply the sharp edge of the spatillum from both sides as it is formed.
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision that is from the temple to the second incision; and cauterize all the cheek which is above the bone between the two cuts. Then do the same from the middle incision to the other second incision, and then withdraw the spatillum.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you place the instrument called "cultellaire" in the first cut, and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side it is rounded, not sharp, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting edge towards the anus at the center, and the rounded edge towards the bone, and keep it there until it reaches the middle cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the veins that descend to the eyes until the incision is continuous down to those that open at the center, and then continue in the middle cut down to the other side; and then extract the blood evenly, express the flesh for the blood taken; then place a tent of old cotton in each cut, and cover with wet cloths in wine and oil and anise, and keep abscesses from forming; on the third day remove the bandage, and apply a large dressing with hot water, then treat with ointment basilicon with rose oil, and other treatments for wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of eye pain
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When someone comes with a sharp cataract accustomedly, and you see the eyes contracted and small, and weakening of vision, and burned papers; and the hair falls out, and where it falls there is pain from water, and the patient sneezes; then know by these accidents that those materials and this cataract come only from many veins, and the matter within, so it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you command the patient to lie on their back, then make a large incision through the forehead, and another one of lesser width.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And start from the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision reach the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when eating. When the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then separate between the two lips of the incision and place old cotton and linen; then cover above with moistened cloth in wine and oil, and beware of warm abscesses. When it is removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat with things that promote healing.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In a manner such: take two parts of flour of wheat, and four parts of colophony, and make a paste; and apply it to the wounds to draw out flesh throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stopping up of ears.
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into ears is one of four things: or grains, or beast, or mineral stone or similar thing such as iron; or seed, such as oats, beans, peas; or fluid-like substances such as water and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls into the ear as a stone or other kind of thing that does not attach to the ear and does not grow in the ear, place the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, if it distils a little bit of violet oil or sesame oil, then administer its extraction; and let the patient sneeze with condisi, and plug the nose with estoup when the sneezing comes, and place pieces of cloth or wool inside the ear; and keep the ear above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times sneezing comes from this treatment; and if it does not come from sneezing, then administer the extraction with subtle forceps, of which the form is described here.
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it sneezes with the forceps, that is good; if not, administer the extraction with a subtle oncine of small weight; and if it does not sneeze with that, make a cotton swab and insert the head of the swab or a hole in the ear firmly, and plug around the swab with soft wax so that the snuff cannot enter with the swab; then draw it to sneeze forcefully, for many times sneezing comes as we have said; and if it does not come in such a manner, take snuff powder and use any instrument that is suitable for this purpose, and put some cotton inside; then press the snuff against the stone or whatever it is, and draw it to sneeze.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not burst from all these things that we have said, hasten to cut the ear as with a boil filled with pus and inflammation; and the manner of cutting is that you first make the patient savor the malady of cephalic origin, and draw out the blood according to the measure of its virtue, then seat the patient in your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear where the fat or flesh hangs down; and let the cut be as narrow as the moon until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your power, and suck it quickly into your mouth; and treat until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is inflamed and swells, administer the extraction; and if it cannot come out, administer the spatumile tenue subtil according to this form.
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not make one when you think the grains are moist due to ear moisture, until you have made many pieces; then extract with fine forceps and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction be gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the ear, when water falls into it, the patient should use sneezing with initial conditions, and enlarge the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let them lie on that same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it drains well through that, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, take many stones according to the length of your thumb and hold them lightly. Heat them slightly over fire. Place one end of the stone in the patient's ear, and place another part of it outside. Strike with another stone on the stone inside the ear; continue striking stone by stone until the water drains completely, and then it will drain completely. If you see this, take a reed, insert one end of the shoulder into the ear, and the other end near the fire until the softer reed is burned. Then repeat with other reeds until the water drains completely, as we have said in the stone method.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is of small size, as with a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large size that one can feel it, use forceps for its extraction; and this is the thing easiest to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and for distillations, and the cure does not help much, then you must look at the ear in the sun: if there are no visible worms, draw them with fine forceps, and if they do not appear, take the wick of cotton described here.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it should be narrow outside and broad inside.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And put in the ear the finest needle according to the amount of pain of the patient, then successively throughout the canal; do this often so that all the pus comes out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out, stop up inside the ear canal as I have said for the stone; and if they do not come out forcefully as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the extraction of worms, and you will find them or treat of distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument, of which its form is as you see.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let it be of silver or thin tin from below the small holes, and above open for distillation; and to press within the distillation with the well-made instrument of tin for this, and if you see use the razor and wrap around the point with suitable cotton; then cast your oil or juice, and what you wish of your medicines into the canal, and let the canal be in the ear; then put within the razor all the cotton, and press your hand firmly until the oil is distilled or movement from the ear; and let the medicines be smelled by the patient, and let the distillations be slightly heated over fire as when one distills into the ear; and keep it from being too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the ear stoppage
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who has no perforation in the ears; and the same thing happens to men due to ear wound obstruction or a clot formed within the ear, and these obstructions sometimes occur so completely that they cannot be seen; and sometimes only part of the perforation is obstructed, and the hole remains visible.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which occurs so completely that it cannot be seen is of great concern for proper treatment, and in such cases, you must place the ear of the patient in the sun; and look inside: if you see the obvious obstruction, then the work has been thoroughly completed.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be sharp and cutting both in front and behind completely clean, so that it does not damage the ear; if the extraction is from flesh or cartilage of the ear, hold it with fine forceps, and remove it gently, until all the flesh is taken out.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the extraction is in the ear, take the fine scissors gently and heat them a little with fire, then place them on the cartilage of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you sense that the extraction causes pain in the patient's ear, pierce gently, and make sure not to damage the nerves of the ear; then place a wick in the ear according to the size of the hole, and fill it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Make this for any day while the wound is sewed up, or take a tent and marrow in rose-colored water, and powder mixed with ground vitriol; and if you see the ear swollen, it must be treated by removing the tent and using another moistened tent made of rosine oil and wax until the swelling is gone; then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if hemorrhaging of blood comes, dip a sponge and cloth in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other dressings that remove the hemorrhage which are or treat with distillations.
de la char des papieres	from the juice of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This althelul that comes from papers of eyes when they are moist and are dried, it must be that you spread them with tongs and forceps, and the peel of a spatule made from its roots; then put on the eye ground vitriol.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without decortic和平版本：而且如果未经去皮，就用细长形烙铁对静脉进行灼烧，然后在切口后使其移动；很多时候会复发，因为它们的根部没有留下任何东西；当它们被火灼烧时，那些根会被烧毁且不再再生。
de la gresle	And if without decortic和平版本：而且如果未经去皮，就用细长形烙铁对静脉进行灼烧，然后在切口后使其移动；很多时候会复发，因为它们的根部没有留下任何东西；当它们被火灼烧时，那些根会被烧毁且不再再生。
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come in the eyes things that seem hailstones in their form and hardness, and because of this, this illness is called "hail," and it is a gathering of moisture large on the surface and underneath; the operations are such: see if the hail moves from one side to another, and this is a light thing to know; then make it wide, then burn each part lightly, then take it with forceps, and scrape it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cope it without piercing a little the paper, it does not hurt the patient at all; and if the cut is large, sew it up with a stitch, and cure it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not apply too much force, for ointments will restore it quickly and promote healing.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the grain is descending into the inner ear towards the upper part, invert the paper, and place the grain with tweezers, and cope and press from both sides; and if the paper is removed by incision, it does not hurt at all; and when the grain is coped, wash the eye with salt water, and cure the head of what promotes healing until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is embedded in the membranes of the papers above, and this happens more to children than to adults, and greatly hurts their eyes. They get catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears rush to their eyes; for this they lie on their faces during the day and sleep face down, with their papers underneath them covered by their moist sorcery that swells and appears from the exinach which opens in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press on the head between your hands and feel the exinach within.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of the work is that the patient places their head on your lap; and then take a linen cloth, and set up a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity of exinach that each part contains, then place it on them. Press from both sides with your hands so that the exinach gather within the circle; then cut through the moisture at the center with a sharp knife making a slit as wide as the wound made for the vein; and scrape the skin thoroughly until you see the exinach. And through many preparations, exinach comes out from the slit in the form of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract then the entire piece of cloth charter between thy two forearms, and turn thy hand to the right and to the left until it is dispersed; and guard that thou dost not join in the fissure, that thou come not to all the spatumile until thou reach the eye, that thou wound it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the spatumile does not open at the beginning of the fissure, widen the fissure slightly until it opens; then extract as we have said, then stuff with soft cloth and water, and place over the eye, and extract with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if such men who grind grain and put it there to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat until he is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess hot comes to the shoulder, treat it with soothing plaster applications until he is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of the paper hairs
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper hairs grow other than as nature intended, and they become mature, they harm the eyes, causing conditions similar to habitual tearing, softening of the papers, and albugine, leading to the destruction of the eyes; and the treatment is according to four methods: either by a fire cautery with all types of fire, or by a medicinal wash as described in the previous chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and suturing or by cantharides, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must place the head of the patient in your sound hand, then turn the paper of the eye with your left hand; if it is rotated correctly, that is good; if not, you should insert a needle along the thread above; and let this be from the margin of the paper where the hair grows among these hairs, and pull the thread above the entire piece of paper, and cut it at the edge with the razor; then make an incision under the paper, under the added hair, to the entire spatumile cutting, from the large eyelid down to the small; then extract the thread, and place a small tent of cotton and cloth under the paper, then sprinkle on the paper a figure of enchye, as the leaf of laurel, and always it must be that the figure is according to the quantity you wish to lift from the paper which is divided for all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is one who needs much of the paper according to how it has been softened; then make on the entire spatumile above the two lines that you have marked, and start from the large lacrimal gland until small; let it be one of the slits near the natural hairs in the size of a root, then pour the ounce into one of the two corners of the keur, then scorch all of it; then assemble the two lips with a seam using an awl and all the thread of thin wool, and wipe away the blood, and do away with the superfluity of threads above the two sorcilz to any sticky things, if you wish to do this; but if not, do not worry about it, then leave the seam and threads until three or four days; afterwards cure the wound without a seam using drying and constraining things, because the paper revives suddenly from the wound and their assembly, but the seam is decayed (as the ancients say), and these are works without fear; and in another way: and it is that you mark the paper with a figure which is as like to the leaf of laurel as we have recounted, three ounces separated according to the form which is here.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then apply those that surmount small forces equally according to the form which is described here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the forceps, and the things are not equal, take a needle or thread, insert it into the figure; and put the other thread through the large artery, and the second thread through the small one, and join the threads equally between your two hands; then withdraw your hand equally, and withdraw all the skin above what you have signed, as we have recounted, then join the two lips of the wound by suturing, and treat it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes from your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar alleviating ointment; and any time the hair of the paper turns: then you must use what we said about the incision; but the suturing in one and in the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of boils is according to this form: and it is that you turn the paper inward as I have said, and then make two canes by art, and two thin strings as long as the paper and as wide as the spann; and tie at the heads of both parts where you hold the threads; then join one to the other delicately above what rises from the paper of the eye, and extract the two canes from the parts formed; and let it be thus for some days, and the skin which was constrained will die and nerve and rot, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it lingers, and you need to apply more force, then treat until it is healed; and when the wound is closed, and the paper has been removed, and the hairs will no longer grow; and this is the form of the two canes that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The operations are such that you insert a thin needle, and thread it with fine silk thread; then join the heads and tie both finely, and let the lengths of the threads be one palm long; then set another short fine silk thread in the chase, and tie its head to the thread; then put the patient's head on your healthy side; and keep away from the sun so that the operations are clear, for this is a delicate and minute operation, then insert the needle completely into the root of the added hair, and make it pierce through the paper quickly as you pull it over the natural hair; then extract the hair up to the chase, and put in the chase that hair if there is one or two or three or more; then withdraw your hand so that all the hairs emerge from the chase with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not come forth with it, you will draw the chase out through all the thread that you have ordered, until the chase has been drawn from above the pertus and you see it by the vision of the eye; then you will draw the chase and the thread, and close the eye and let it remain closed for two or three days, until the hairs grow in their place and flesh appears above; and if the hairs are small, you shall accompany one long hair from the natural hairs, and raise it with that or where you leave it, until it is stretched and then release it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the corruption of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, which is called "aleacrati" or corruption, comes to the oil, it occurs in two manners: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly from a wound, or an incision, or a fire cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of the work in it is that you cut open the stitch, and separate the lips of it, and put within tents of linen, and tie it until it is sound; and it does not suit you to use in the treatment of it things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease returns worse than the first; but the work of things that soften, such as fenugreek; and the wash with water or urine and linseed cooked, and ointments melted in any of the oils, and wrap it in a tent, and treat it with these.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care lest it closes not according to the form it was before; and these works that we have said are only remedies for this disease so that it does not return according to the form it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds, cuts, fire cautery, and similar things; and the way of this work is that you insert a needle, in which there is double thread, and fix it in the flesh, and make the thread pierce from left lachrymal gland to right, so that the threads emerge at both heads of the flesh; then the flesh above is pulled by all the needle, and the cloth by the wide spatule.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns as it should, that is good; but if not, take a razor and place it in the crack, turn the paper, and make two cracks inside the paper; and let the heads of the two cracks be at the angles of your incision, and make angles such that when they are assembled, the figure is also as the figure of a letter which has no "I griesche"; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its sides are cut from underneath, from what follows the paper, then join the two separated parts with stitches of linen thread; then apply the cure that we have said of mollifying medicines and tents until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a crack or suture or cautery, you must make a full crack underneath the hairs of the paper, according to what is said before; then separate between the two flaps of a tent as I have said; and one must perform the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and master surgeons devise means with all their skill how they may make the figure return to its natural form; and the patients themselves, according to what is needed from the work and instruments in many dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	suddenly from the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this缝合发生在人手上以某种方式，纸张上方变得僵硬并用眼睛的白色部分固定，不能移动也无法完成其自然工作，那么你必须在纸上刺入剃刀的尖端，将其拉起；然后用钳子保持，直到你取出那些位于细微脂肪中的东西，既不要太锋利也不要太锐利，以免患者无法忍受太过刺激或使眼球变白；你的切割要轻柔地灼伤它们的集合体，使得纸张恢复其自然形态；整个集合体都痊愈了，并且在眼中含盐水和泪水中不会有任何一次不适；之后在纸上放一层亚麻布，并在眼睛上放置浸过鸡蛋清的羊毛；然后使用紧绷物品直到痊愈。
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	The nail of the eye is according to two manners: one is nervous and resembling hard skin, and another which is not nervous but resembles white congealed moisture, such that when it is touched with iron and carefully cut with tweezers, it cannot be held; and both resemble starting near the large lacrimal gland, and grow little by little until they cover all sight and light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is as follows: the patient places their head on your lap, then opens their eyes; lift the paper with your hand, then grasp the nail with small tweezers and hold it above. Then take a needle, and place the horsehair, or deer hair, or cow hair, and a strong thread. Fold the needle point slightly and insert it into the nail, piercing it completely through. Secure the nail with a thread and hold it above, then cauterize along the side of the nail where the quill and silk meet to the tip of the hair until just below the lacrimal duct. Cut off the remaining part at the root of the lacrimal gland with very fine forces, leaving the natural skin or lacrimal gland so that no tears are produced through the incision as they are accustomed; sometimes only the nail and thread are cauterized, as we have said; then cauterize along all the fine pores from which this is formed.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And beware that the spatillum does not touch the fleshy membrane and tear it, and that the probe is not pierced; after incision, pour a little powdered salt into the eye, and from cologne made of litharge, and leave it until the next day; then cure with what is necessary until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerveous, and you cannot pierce it with the needle, and the forceps cannot enter it, often this resemblance of a nail is treated with medicines; and they grow as I have recounted in the division, and if you see it copulate, work on the eye of the patient, and take the spatillum lightly somewhat sharp according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And gently remove the nail from above, and if you see that it thins at all and the root presses in, distill into the eye from your mouth cologne made of litharge and red cologne and powdered salt, and plug the eye until the next day; then restart the other work according to this same method, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary in the eye, as with a hot abscess, then let it be, and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh around the eyelid harms the eye by great harm, then suspend it by a wire, and cut off part of it but not all, so that no tears come; then instill in the eye red powder made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows around the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Some people's eyes grow red flesh once around the pupil, and cover the iris and are held on paper and turned over, seeming like a water lily; and the work is that the patient places their head on your side, then you turn their eyes, and cut all that flesh with suitable wires and hold it in place by force; then cut off the first layer of flesh, and continue cutting to the edge of the hairline until the end, and beware that you do not injure the eye during the work. And make the incision for the cataract as we said in the incision of the nail and with small forces from which one removes the film, as those who follow this chapter form after show; and when the incision is completed and all the flesh is removed, fill the eye with brine oil or you distill red powder and similar corrosive medicines, and place over the eye a cloth soaked in egg white, so that it is prepared for a hot abscess; and if there remains nothing, and the wound heals above, and you doubt a hot abscess, then leave the eye and treat the abscess with things that soothe a hot abscess; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do all flesh layers added in the eye by this resemblance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nonetheless, it is necessary that you cleanse the cure of each weak eye from the natural way; and from the accidental way, in the work of iron; and not put your hand in any of these works as long as you see that this limb be suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	If the veins around the eyes are red and cover the eye, and affect the vision with their work and weaken the eye for all days.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Therefore, for the first thing that you observe if the eye, in which the redness is, is outside, and there is no other disease besides the redness; then treat it in this manner: instruct the patient to place their head on your healthy hand, then suspend those veins to all ounces according to your wisdom, and let the ounces be subtly doubled according to this form.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two ounces by degrees in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then coil the forces of these veins subtly, and wipe the blood hour after hour until you see the veins removed from the eye; and guard that you do not damage the eye with the points of the spatulas, and perform this work at noon before the sun, and be very warm in your work so that you do not harm those veins; and when you have done this, distill colriere green and red into the eye to corrupt what remains of the swelling.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you do not have the power to coil all of this in that hour, apply a plaster to the eye with things that soothe the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pains are soothed and assured of the warm abscess, then restart according to this manner which is before until it is healed; and this is the form of the forces.
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	They are called "arissati" fistula: when you cure it by cautery and with hot aqueous medicine as I have said before, and if it is not healed, then you indeed cut above the abscess, where it should come to a head, and drain all the moisture that is in it, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and the blackness, then clean it with all the instrument of which this is the form; and it is called "aspre chief," and it should be made from a file, and be pointed like a rasp as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place on the bone that is corrupted, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a bit until you know that the corruption has dried up; do this once, then restore the layer of drying medicinal substances.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the bones are united, and flesh arises, and the core of the boil is united, and remains thus for 40 days, and it does not recur or become an abscess, and no ill accident happens, know that it is healed; if this is not so, there is no other means than to bring the fistula back to the opening of the vein according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time by iron and with medicines and water, and when it is uncovered take one forester according to this form, and let the head of the iron be at three angles, and the stake be thinned just to the tip as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it on the bone beneath the eyelid, and withdraw your hand from the eye a little, then turn the whole forester until it pierces the bone, and let the patient feel the pain where the fluid comes in; if he keeps his hand over his nose; and then restore the cover of medicinal powders as I have instructed you, and when the flesh grows and hardens the bones, the matter goes to the nose; this is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the issue from the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are completely opened and there is no obstruction, nor any amelioration, it is necessary to bind the patient. Then heal them, and apply cups or cautery without piercing to suction. Next, place on the eye a dressing made of myrrh, aloes, incense, and sarcocolla. Then press the eye, and plaster it with bandages and cloths. The method for the cloths is that you take soft enough cloths, double each one four times, and then place them one over another according to the amount needed by the eyes. Then press from above with a hard form bandage, and repeat the cups without piercing to suction. Remove the cups and let the eye be pressed day and night. If the dressing loosens, it is necessary to tighten it much. After removing the dressing in the morning and evening, if you see the eye healed, it is good; if not, continue with the plastering, cloths, bandages, and cups until it heals.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of the rupture of woollen cloth vein
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions come in the woollen cloth vein, then opened and comes forth like a grain of resin, and is terrifying to see; then if you see it copered, the operations are such that you prick with a needle at the root of the part below until above, then prick another needle where there be double thread from the eyelid; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to its placement; then cut through the double thread and tie a part of the vein around, and tightly hold it in place, then remove the needle and put on the eye moistened wool from an egg yolk; and let it be until the threads heal with the vein, then cure the eye with things that comfort until the wound is healed; and any time the wound is restrained by the vein in a circle of cloth around each part, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes have a great appearance, pierce them with a sharp needle that comes from the center of the eye, and draw out the moisture milky and lower the eyes, and let them enter soon; then extract them until they are healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the bow of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" does not come from the bow of the eye that assembles in the eye, seeming like water descending, and it is not water; and the manner of its appearance in the work is such that you make the patient sit on the prepared seat straight, then take the head between your hands from one side, and move the eyeball until you see the bow come above your eyes; then prick it and do not let it descend, and remove the light, and see the patient the things as he should; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descensions of the bow are not prepared as we have said, saith that it is water.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	place the patient between your hands, then take the sharp spatula and make incisions along the corneal membrane with the conjunctiva and the cornea, until the fluid comes out; when it has come out, distill into the eye hot aqueous honey or boiled fenugreek water mixed with honey, then cure with other remedies until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	from the fluids of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have the signs of eye diseases in the division, and the proper places to puncture; work according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you place the patient between your crossed hands, away from sunlight, and tie the healthy eye very tightly. Then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eyes are left-eye dominant, or in your right hand if they are right-eye dominant. Next, take with your right hand (if the eyes are left-eye dominant), or with your left hand (if the eyes are right-eye dominant), the instrument called "almagda." Then place the tip of the instrument beneath the cornea by the thickness of a grain in that black part of the eye near the lower eyelid. Push the almagda instrument forcefully, and turn your hand until it pierces through the black part of the eye, feeling when the almagda reaches the empty space. The measure of the almagda passage should be precisely at the same measure as from the needle to the end of the sclera; this is the cornea of the eye. You will see the bone in that paper due to the clarity of the corneal membrane, and then place the instrument until it reaches where the fluid is, and express it through one passage after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	if the water comes out now, the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a little while, and if the water rises again by the second way, put force with the instrument, and when it is firmly in place and it does not rise, extract slightly around it by turning your hand little by little; and then put a bit of silk thread around it, and remove this from the eye.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put behind the eye a plug of moistened wool in rose oil and plenty of egg, and tie with healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Now, and those of our time, put on with abundant egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if it hardens so much that it cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are people who have too hard eyes, then you must use the instrument called "alberit", of which the form is as follows:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but make it subtle, then put in the hardened substance as we have said; and when the work is completed, prepare for the patient to fall asleep on his back in a dark place; and let him be free from all movements, and give light meals, and do not move his head to the right or left, and bind him according to his condition for three days; then release him in that same dark house, and test his vision, and have him show some things, and then rebind him until the seventh day; and it is not fitting that you do this during the time of treatment or after incision now, but you must loosen it, because the moisture rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If abscesses appear, you release the eye before the seventh day, following the treatment for those who alleviate abscesses; and when it is pacified, you release the vision and place on its face an ointment or balm to cover any day, and let it be healed in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then leave the house little by little, and be cured in his case; and know that no disciple should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And some came to us who were from the Yrach, who told us that in their country they performed almagda punctet, for which one applies water, but truly I have never seen such a thing in our land, nor do I find it mentioned in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the signs of the forms of almagda, for those who do not know them will see; and they are of mercury properly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of aus be of this same subtlety, and the last in three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	from the cheek beside the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes cheeks beside the nose become malformed in various ways, of which some seem like scorpions with claw marks; and there are those where the cheek has a deeply embedded scar of a different color, and where the cheek has a healed scar of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	For those scars that are healed but not deeply embedded, you must place the patient's cheek against the sun; work on their nostrils, and sprinkle the ounce on those scars, and draw them out. Then, cover what you can withstand with a fine sharp point of spatumile (a type of instrument) on one side, until you know that the scar is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any thing that one cannot cope with, open it completely with all the subtle instruments lightly, so that nothing remains; and if without surmounts or an abscess occurs, give him the help as it should be; and if it is malignant abscesses, hasten and cauterize until the pus is exhausted and all the flesh be removed, then apply a cold poultice of bread or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the poultice works and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healed; and if the moisture does not drain as it should, know that there is new flesh grown on the bone above, which the instruments cannot reach to cut: then you must put a somewhat thick piece of flax thread, well knotted by hand, with each knot about an inch or less apart; and place the patient's head where the thread exits into his nose as far as possible, and pull in smelling until it comes out through the nose into the mouth; and many times do so with children at school, and this is a light thing for him who knows how to do it; then hold the head which comes through the nose with one hand, and the other head which comes through the mouth with the other hand, and pull alternately while attending to us who are by the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this as much as you know that the nerves have corrupted that flesh, then draw the thread, wipe the blood, soften the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrupts all that remains of the flesh; and then put a reed of flax in the nose for some days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the brain, to which one distills the eyes and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be made of silver or lead, resembling an open lamp, like a reed, and guide it thus; and if you see, make a closed reed, and let the instrument be full for purging the brain; and have one hand on the brain to hold it when one heats the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh off the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	many times a disease arises at the top of the nose which is called "telul" and grows and becomes large over days; and when it is visible to the eye; therefore, you should lance in the beginning, and extract all of it, then place a fire cautery or hot medicine on it; and if one delays lancing until it becomes large, one must observe if it is hard, pale in color, lacking sensation: do not touch it with iron at all because it is an embedded abscess, for when one lances it once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscesses are due to dampness touching, not pale in color, and you can see that they can be completely lanced, then empty the patient of it without fear, and treat the wound with drying and constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut off and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	When solutions of continuation come to one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, for in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, when this occurs to any, you must examine if the wound is fresh with all its blood; then approximate the two lips with a stitch, and treat until it heals.
