And if the lips are already dry on one side and the other, you must cauterize all parts of their edges until they heal, then approximate the two lips with a stitch, and bind them, and sprinkle with powder of dragon's blood powder, and powdered incense; and place over the powders a piece of plaster of strong or another binding plaster, and leave it until it dries on its own, then treat with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of stitching is such that you assemble the solution: or with needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly; or with thread, as I have made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	By hand, abscesses in the lips appear, resembling grains of wheat, small and larger; then it must be that you turn the lips, incise each side, take out the pus with forceps, and place in each part; then apply wine after the vitriol is ground, until the blood is stanched; and then apply almond oil, and cure the wine from dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a chapped flesh arises on the gums, which the ancients call "albulus"; you must hold it with tongs and cut at its root, and let the blood or blood run; then place on it vitriolated flux, or other constricting and drying powders; and if this flesh returns after incision, which often happens, you should cop it a second time, and cauterize: it does not return after the cauterization; and these are the forms of instruments for cop.
des sordens	of the sores
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes aches assemble at the root of the teeth, within the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and harsh; and sometimes the teeth become black and yellowish-green as corruption comes to the gums, making them stink; you must place the patient's head in your hands, and their chin on your knees, and remove any teeth or scabs visible, until nothing remains; and do this for the blackness and greenish color, and the yellowness and other stains, until they are all removed; and if what is to be done according to the first reason is good, it is well; if not, begin again on the second day and the third, until you have removed everything; and know that teeth require various forms of instruments to remove them, depending on what work your instrument shows, because those used to scrape out between the teeth have different shapes from those used to scrape out the teeth themselves; and these forms and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you treat the tooth of its pain, you should delay the extraction as much as you can, for it must not be done at all; for it is a very delicate matter until one has no excuse to remove it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained to extract, it must be certain that the tooth aching.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain urges the patient, and he thinks it is a good tooth, and has it extracted. Yet the pain does not depart from him until the bad tooth is removed, for we have already done this to these gentlemen. When you are well certain that the tooth aching, it must be scraped around the tooth thoroughly to prevent gum irritation from all sides; then move it gently or with fine forceps at first and first, until it is well loosened, then firmly set the forceps; and place the head of the patient on your thigh between your knees, and hold him well so that he does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, if it does not come out, take any of these instruments and push it gently into each part, and move the forceps as you have done before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and broken, you must fill it with wads of cotton, lint, or cloth; and use fine forceps to extract it without breaking it; you must work carefully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take great care that you do not break it and leave a part of it remaining, as this can cause the patient greater pain than the initial pain due to the malice of the root.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take care that you do not act as the ignorant surgeon does, who, through their haste and boldness, break the root once, and do not provide what we have detailed; instead, they bring about great illness one time through cutting, due to the roots remaining or the bone they break, as we often see. When the tooth is extracted, wash the wound with wine or oil of olive and salt; and if there is bleeding, which often occurs, fill the wound with vitriol powder; and if this does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, to which one must fit the teeth first, be long points and thick handles, so that they do not bend when you draw the tooth; and these are their forms.
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them have thick handles so that they do not bend when drawing, and let them be of well-made iron, and let them be toothed to hold tightly.
de la racine des dens	from the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains during drawing, it is necessary to place moistened cotton wool in the socket for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the socket is healed, then put in the tongs called "algefri," which the head resembles a doctor's bill; and let them be made inside like a file, and these are their forms:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not wish to come out with all these forceps, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh entirely around the root, and place the instrument called "althali," that is, pailance, of which the form is:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be firm and large so that it does not break at all, and if the root jumps out from there, that is good; if not, you must assist with all the instruments, of which the forms are given hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you need to use an instrument that has two prongs, of which the form is given hereafter:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are before mentioned for the reason of teeth, and of this instrument that seems a pair of large forceps, of which the form is given hereafter:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this implement not be broken, and know that few are implements of the teeth; and also other implements, which are not counted; and the master surgeons find their own instrument by themselves, according to those of their work and the disease that show them, for there are such diseases where the old ones did not teach an implement because of the diversity of jaws and if one breaks a part of the body or of the other bones, or rots, then it seeks the instruments that it suits, which I have told you, and helps with gestures, as is their form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-holding to hold the bone so that it does not escape but can be held and removed; then restore the head with medicines suitable for this, and if there is decay in the bone and it is small, it can be treated with all of this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not in accordance with their natural order, and the shape is ugly, especially in maiden women, you must know whether the teeth were born after the others and are not in the right place, and cannot be straightened nor filed: then you should extract them; and if they are beside the other teeth, take this instrument whose form is as described, and it resembles a small beak, and let it be of sharp iron.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the cop is rubbed little by little in the hand during the day due to the hardness of the tooth, and because you cannot move the others, and if it appears that it can be filed, then file it with a single-file as its form is described.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file with which we make needles; and you file the tooth little by little in your hand during the day lightly, so that it does not move while it hardens. Then in the end, level it entirely with any rasp, and if the tooth is too sharp and discolors the tongue, then you must file away its sharpness until it is equal, so that it does not discolor the tongue nor corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth chatter
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	when the front teeth chatter due to percussion or falling, and the patient cannot bite down on what they eat without dropping it, you should treat them with restrictive medicines, but this is ineffective; so you must restrain them with a gold thread, for silver threads turn green and rot, but gold never changes; and let the threads be of moderate size, neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to straighten the teeth, take the thread and pass it double between two healthy teeth, then place the heads of the thread between the teeth that need adjustment, whether one or more, until you see clearly to the healthy tooth on the other side; then re-cover starting from where you began, and withdraw your hand subtly and steadily, so that it does not move at all; and let your grip be at the root of the tooth such that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the head of the tooth with a needle and assemble them, and place them so they do not hurt the tongue; and then leave them so tight as they can stay, and if they come loose or the threads break, tighten them with another thread; if they stay tight and serve like this for all their time, and this is the form of the teeth and the alignment figure of the two healthy teeth and the two mesial surfaces, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, one replaces it in its place, frequently as we have said; and one must not do so except by someone who is skilled and suffers, and only once the form of a bone tooth from a deer is made, and it is put in the place where it is missing, and it is tightened as we have said, and stays and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the wound of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	no wound from the tongue by nature or accident arises thus; or by an accidental injury to a缝合的伤口；且你操作病人的嘴巴，使其头部偏向健康一侧，提起舌头；然后覆盖大血管附近的神经伤口，直到舌头脱离其正常位置；如果存在硬化或肿胀，并且是由于伤口突然造成的，那么用钩针缝合并广泛缝合该部位；注意不要将切口完全缝合得太紧，以免压迫下方的动脉；做完后，用玫瑰水或芦荟水以及冷水冲洗提起的部位，然后在舌头上放一块亚麻布绷带；让病人每晚更换，以确保伤口不会感染。
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding occurs, place a piece of ground glass over the wound; and if the blood fails to stop, cauterize with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then treat with other remedies until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it is of a red or black or hard color, and the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a cancer; and if it is turning white and there is moisture, then sprinkle the powder, and cut a small hole with a sharp spatule, and relieve it on both sides; and if the blood does not stop in your work, place a piece of ground glass over it until it cools down, then return to your work as you treat all further matters; then lift the wound from grease and salt, and treat with other remedies until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there are pouches in the throat called "godath," and these are properly known as the two almonds. When you cure them, as we have said in the division, and if they are abscesses hard with small size and of flesh color, take care: do not let them touch iron at all.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if they are red and the root is large, do not let them touch iron at all, also for the discharge of blood; but leave them until they are ripe, and then you may cut them out, or they would break open by themselves. And if they are white in color and the root is fine, prepare the instrument to extract them, but first see if the abscess has cooled down and calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore, place the patient facing the sun, and his head straight, and let him open his mouth, and have the sergeants hold the jaw between their hands, pressing the tongue under the entire instrument, which is its form; and it should be made of fine silver or brass as thin as a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	You press the tongue with all this instrument, and you see the abscess, take an ounce and the pin in almond shape, and draw force above more than you can; and draw nothing from the threads with, then cover the instrument, which is its form, that seems like strong forces; and always the head are curved, one next to the other, and are very sharp, and made of iron indigotina or antinnea.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, use tongs, of which here is its form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let it be sharp on one side, and on the other named; and when you have cut one of the almonds, cut the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot, sharp water, or with hot and easy water, and if bleeding occurs, gargle the patient with water, or cooked pomegranate peel, or bay leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stanched; then cure it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses arise in the throat besides the two almonds, so cut them accordingly as the two almonds evenly.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman who had an abscess that had arisen within her throat, specifically the small sens abscess; and I had almost completely closed off the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe due to the conduit being obstructed, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained in such a condition for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so swollen that he had to insert two arrows through both openings of the neck.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then quickly, and inserted the lancet into one, then drew out a great portion of flesh; then I pierced another in the other opening of the neck, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; after that I inserted the lancet into these abscesses, and drained a part of them, and only a little blood came out; and thus was the passage of the throat of the woman cleared, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not cease to lance this abscess for a long time; and the abscess reformed again, and filled the space that I had drained until it became quite large; then I packed it and cauterized inside the throat: thus it remained without growing further; and I left these parts, and only God decided what would happen to her after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When swelling occurs in the eye, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and when it is very large and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the abscesses are calmed and are subtle, then it is necessary to lance it; and that which is round gathered and is not long; and which is bloody or of linen color or black, then it is necessary to avoid incising it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it in the manner I have said, regarding its blenchor and length, you should seat the patient facing the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument we mentioned earlier; then place the oncine in the eye, and draw it out, and lance it using the two instruments I described in the incision of the almond.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cope more than the superfluity that is beyond the natural limit; for if you do so more, it grieves to the voice and speech; and after the incision, use of what we have said in the incision of two almonds, and cure until it is sane.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of coping, you must use an instrument for the cautery to alleviate the fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is very hot.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should put their head on your side, and then press their tongue with the instrument we mentioned in the chapter on cautery, using live boiling water that is neither too thick nor too clear; and fill the opening of this instrument as follows:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the patient have a head or cheek where one places the medicine, as with the hairs of a spoon, and put the instrument on all the medicine over the eye; and the patient be lying on his side, so that saliva and mucus flow from his mouth into the medicine, so that it does not descend to the throat, and the bile; then hold your hand on all the medicine and press it over the eye, the quantity of half an hour, until you see it congealed and the bites of the medicine are pacified; and if you see, take cotton and envelop it around any instrument, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument into the core above, so that the cotton wicks over the eye; and do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and after four or five days. And if you need to restart the cautery with the medicine, so do it, and after the cautery wash around the eye with cotton stuffed in butter, and cleanse what is around the medicine; and be washed with cold water, and be treated with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is treated by fumigation in this manner, take reed and yarrow and origanum and rue and chamomile and avron and similar herbs, and gather all of them or some of them in one pot, and place easily, and cause to boil; and the pot be well sealed with strong clay, and amid the pot have the instrument fitted according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And may be of silver or lead, and let one of the heads be inserted in the patient's mouth until the vapor rises to the eye through the cane, until the eye is numbed; after which renew often, until the eye dries, and guard that you do not do this at the beginning of the appearance of the hot abscess, for many things happen; and do not do so during the decline of the hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put an eggshell inside the head so that the patient’s mouth is not too hot; for the eggshell does not allow the vapor to weigh down on the mouth, and it is a good cure overall for health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times, it is applied to the throat with a bone or spiny fish bone, or any other thing; so it is necessary that you treat what you can see, and press the tongue towards the sun with all the instrument, so that you see the thing move; and for what does not become apparent and is lodged in the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit as if the meat were cooked in the stomach; by chance, this may be expelled by vomiting; or the patient might swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of naval, or a root of lettuce, or a morsel of dry bread; and tie the string to the sponge, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the place, it will be applied, and then you will pull out the force. And if it does not come out as we have said, take the plunger instrument according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the probe enter more easily into the throat, with the head lifted upwards; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest it be injured or forced inward; and the patient should move when they expel the instrument, because this indicates movement or that the area is clear; if they expel it downward, or force it thoroughly throughout the entire instrument evenly until it is fully out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat discharge
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	No medicine cures the throat discharge, as I have said in the division, through the treatment of medicines; and when this does not help, then look at the patient's throat in the sunlight, after you press their tongue with the instrument I have described.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the blood, draw it off with a very small needle, or with fine forceps that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, take a live cane, insert it into the throat of the patient, then blow or shake the cane with hot air, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is sick with water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, pour it into the mouth, and administer it so that it is swallowed, and move it often with your hand; and as soon as the blood tastes the water, let it go.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not go as we have said, submerge the patient in arsenic sulfide, using the instrument I described for fumigating the uve. Do this many times, for it will fall without difficulty.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot which has coals visible, and let it be covered with a coverseil pierced in the middle, and into that perforation are placed the head of the instrument; then you throw in your fumigation, and the patient puts the end of the cane in his mouth, and closes the mouth, so that the smoke does not go out but goes until the blood; and the blood will drop now, and if it does not drop, you must repeat the fumigation many times; and allow the patient to be thirsty, and eat salty and dry things, and do not drink water; and then it is necessary for it to come forth by this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats the blood, is such that when one can see it, it resembles curved tongs to enter into the throat; and it has the appearance of a doctor's beak, and it has roughness like a file, so that what it takes, it cannot let go. And behold its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters of the abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	many of the apparent abscesses are, according to what memory brings after from one and another in this book, and they differ in perforation and incision; and there are two ways of which one is in its appearance itself, and of that which it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for the boils or where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for the abscesses of the head are different from those of the deep part, and the abscesses of the soft flesh are different from those that come in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And for abscesses, we should not pierce them until the boil is dead according to its completion; and there are some that require piercing when they are ripe, but do not die according to their completion, such as abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come from joints, and one lets them remain until they are rotten within, by chance the ligament and nerve of the joint may be corrupted, which is a cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Or when the abscess is from the principal member, and if you delay the perforation until it is dead, it will harm the principal member; or when it is from the foundation, one should pierce it even if it is dead; and it does not matter that you perforate an abscess that has not completed digestion, provided that it does not rot completely and becomes elongated within, and then form a fistula; and it cannot heal in a great length of time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time for perforating an abscess that is dead according to completion, and this is when the pain is alleviated, and the departure of fever, and the reduction of pain and redness, and of swelling and the sharpness of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you should place the perforation where more dependent on the abscess, and where it opens most. And let the perforation be as long as the body, whether the abscesses are in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places equal where there is no pulsation.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that bend, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the firm flesh, it is better that you leave the perforation until its digestion is completed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before that, you will spread the poison throughout the body, and it will be full of much filth; and by chance the edges and depths may harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if for any abscess that is pierced according to the size of the body, as the member requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it must be that you make small punctures for small abscesses, and large punctures for large abscesses, and many slits according to the size of the abscess; and for such abscesses where it is necessary to cut the core and cover, when it has turned yellow and is softened, it must be done as with boils: and for those that are split into three angles, and for those from which one covers like a myrtle leaf, as with angry abscesses; and for those where you make a round incision, and other cuts and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who lack a head, as in a superficial abscess, it must be fully pierced; and when the abscess is large, and has gathered great pus, if you pierce it, do not drain all the pus at once in that hour, but only part of it; then cauterize the abscess until the next day, and again draw out some more; do this many times gradually, until the pus exits completely; similarly, if the patient is of weak constitution, or a woman with child, or small children, or elderly people who are decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For if the patient jerks even once with the release of pus, by chance killing the patient, and you are not at fault.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, handle this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, wipe the wound, and examine if the wound from the abscess is small; and if it is a complete incision, apply strips of linen or old cotton; and if it is large abscesses, and there are many punctures, it must be that you insert one strip into each so they come together; and if you have cut into the skin of the abscess and sewed over it, it must be filled with old cotton or a piece of linen rasure without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then remove it, and treat with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs in your work, apply cold water and balsam, and place a soft cloth over the area where the blood is flowing repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, apply a government and care, and the powders that I have said to use in their hands in this book, and whether it is or tends toward winter, and the limbs or abscesses are very nervous, then it must be that you place tents and moist cloths on them, soaked in wine and hot oil; and if it is in summer, and the limbs are fleshly, then it must be that you place moist cloths on them in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, for three days, as we have said; and then drain the abscess and dry it and treat it as it should be until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this must be known universally in the treatment of abscesses: or you have already been told how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or come from the head small abscesses, and their forms are like webs, as with the threads of a spider's web, and there are many that resemble them.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fat and like this with moisture, similar to pulps; and there are those that are hard and stony to the touch, and there is no doubt if the artery does not cause contrary effects.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the operations of the abdomen are such that you test with any instrument called "entromissoire," from which their form comes after, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, he lets it out from above the long bone.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, he cauterizes without leaving any of the skin that contains that moisture, for it repeatedly comes out if left untreated; then he plunges cotton in Egyptian ointment if present; if not, in water and salt, and covers the wound, leaving it until the next day; and this allows what remains from the night to drain.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then he resumes using the cotton, as before, the second day, and the third, until you know well that nothing remains from the night; then treat the wound with ointment suitable for it, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds out fat, shape it according to this form, long; and give your oncines, and scorch it from all sides, and put all your effort into drawing out its pus where it lies; and if the artery makes contrary work, do what I have said after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do the same for the abscess if it is stony, and cut and treat it as I have said.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cutting into the stony abscess and its moisture is more gentle, for they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if any of these abscesses or heads have no moisture, and these were the stony abscesses that I treated or from an old woman; and found the abscess as hard as a smooth, rough, and white stone, and could not be broken. And if one had made any from it, one would have also well made a wound from it as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming from the head or cheeks, these coming from the roots of the ears, the opening should be kept open day and night, depending on the most dependent part, to let the pus out; and the treatment as it should.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times this abscess occurs in the neck, under the armpits, and in groins, and sometimes come from other parts or boils, and are swollen, and are joined together with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its own part, like the lump and abscess of the head, as we have said; and the similarities of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are those that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In those that you see in good condition upon touch, and resemble the color of the body, and move in every part and are not burned near the neck nor near the artery nor the vein, and are not deep; it is fitting that you cut from above, and brand each part, and place the two lips of the wound with forceps if needed, as we said for abscesses on the head; and draw a little bit at a time, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve nor the vein, and do not let the pus or sharp instruments out, that your hand does not slip, and does not go too far, so you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you open the vein or artery, and it does not allow further work, put vitriol powder or any other coagulants in the wound, and compress the wound; and leave it until the abscesses are pacified, and the wound becomes softened and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is coagulated, return to your work until you complete it; then rest according to your proper indication if there remain any small scrofulous swellings, and drain and cleanse them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofulous swelling, it is not proper to open that swelling at its root. Instead, tie it with a double strong thread, and let it fall by itself without doing harm; then pack the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you remove the entire scrofula, it is necessary that you bring together the two edges of the wound, and now suture them, since there has been no excess due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	if it is necessary that you cut the root of it, and draw out the force, and suture it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas that have excess, puncture them where they apert urethra or vein; and puncture them as the one previously said, depending on it, then apply wicks with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what is remaining of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, the treatment with ointment and promoting healing continues until it is healed.
de squinance	of scrofula
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and wrote of the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen anyone do it in our land, and this is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have scrofula, it is necessary to cut the opening in the throat called "epiglote"; and no help should be given by this method because all the veins and the glands of the diseased are hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in the tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the gland, it is necessary to cut the epiglote to avoid the loss that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It must therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, be cut over three or four small cuts across, between the two circles or by the size of the cut through the sypha, not in the cartilage; and those who are thus are suitable for the cutting of the epiglottis so that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long enough.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, it must be stretched from the entire inch of the throat, then cut the skin until it comes to the chain; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cover the sypha as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the fluid of the chain that flows forth through the broken part, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed since one doubts strangulation, bring together the two edges of the wound in the heart, and suture it well beneath the cartilage; then administer medicines that produce flesh until he is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim states that one should not do this until the throat is completely suffocated, and the patient is judged to be dying, then proceed.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then lift the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and in this way, one is kept from dying; and for this, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease passes, and it passes in three or four days. Then they ordered to suture the wound and treat it until it heals; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I see that a maiden took the knife and pierced her throat, cutting part of the vein; and I was called to perform the cure, and found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found the blood issuing from it. I knew she had not pierced a vein nor cut any artery, but the wind was entering through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened, stitched the wound, and cured it until it was healed; and no harm came to the maiden so that she lost her voice, and recovered her strength afterward; for this reason, I say that in the surgery of the epiglottis there is no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large windpipe
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess in color like that of a hazel nut, and is very common in women; and according to two manners: natural, and accident; or naturally there is no device.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident is according to two manners, of which one is similar to fatty tumors, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from inside the artery; and there is fear, and it should not be operated on by making openings except in those that are small, and he proves and searches at every interloping: if you find it as soft as fat, and cannot be pushed into any vein, then cut it out like one cuts tumors, and draw it to all its roots; if there is any point, seek well immediately, and treat it as it should be treated until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many methods we have, of which I will speak of all the similarities; and now it is fitting that I say all the difference there is between us and dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that dislocation is heat and fever lasting until the boiling has passed, and putrefaction is accomplished; then the fever and heat cease.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	When the shoulder has neither heat nor fever nor pain, and contains the synovial fluid, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a swelling, and becomes large; and are according to two similarities, or fat, or moist, and much in color as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It must be, when you come to the treatment of the new wound, that you first examine and inquire about all the instrument called "entromissoire", according to what its form will come or chapter which is after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquisition of abscesses of the flesh is that you probe or more moist tissue that you find in the abscess, and turn your two probes little by little, until you know that the instruments have reached the core; then do this according to the size of the abscess; then extract the entromissoire, and be careful that it not burst.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the moisture comes out clear or of any other color, cut it as I have said for other abscesses; and if after extracting the entromissoire there is no more moisture, know that it is fatty, so cut it in a cross shape, and remove it with forceps, and slightly brand it from each part. Guard the cloth where it lies and treat it healthily with the wound; and if you cannot treat it healthily, remove it piece by piece so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if it remains nothing, it returns to us many times; and if there is a little, and the poison grieves the wound, fill the wound with some corrosive powders, restrain the wound, and put on hot abscess-soothing things, and cure it with other cures until it is healed; and if the wound is large, suture the two edges of the wound, and cure those who bear flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein beating is contrary to you or other so hasten and fill the head with pounded vitriol, and let it lie for 2 or 3 days, until the wound rots, and rest the boiling of the blood; then return to the copper that which has remained from the new.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of the intromissory instruments, and they are in three ways: great, medium, and small; and among them there are three squares called "albaret," and one that is called "breb"; and there are also three kinds to encircle abscesses from fistulae: great, medium, and small, like the needles with which one sews sinews. They are made of yellow brass or iron or silver, and the ones that are yellow are more tried for encircling black plaques from fistulae; and they are in three ways: great, medium, and small, according to the size of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the claws are similar in appearance, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and among these, some have two notches in three ways; and some have three notches, and are also in three ways; and some have two notches, and claws with only one notch, and are in three ways; and all of this are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The chief of those for which this is done is sharp, and among these are those that cut only half the way, with which one cauterizes the nostrils, because one does not cut the vein nor the nerve; and from these intrusive ones are the alembics placed in hands, so that the patient does not perceive them at the opening of abscesses; and they are in three ways: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses none with force in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, mammary glands, and at the armpits, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another instrument small, resembling shells of pistachios, according to this form, for which one stops bleeding.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed once in its place which heals by degrees from the veins, and in the arteries, and once again according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Once the breasts of some men swell when they begin to腐坏，直至看起来像女人的乳房；并且remain ugly and swollen; and if one wishes to cure them, it must be done according to this form of line .b. from .a. to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then cauterize the fat, and apply the wound with a medicated cloth. Then stitch the two edges of the wound together, and treat it until it is healed. And if the breast swells downward and becomes softened due to its size as in women, cut into the two ribs above, following similar incisions; ensuring that one edge holds the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the minor according to this form from line .b. to the line .g.; then cauterize the skin between the two edges, remove the fat, and apply what we have said regarding stitching and powders, as well as necessary treatments until it is healed; if it is not healed or the incision is not fully completed, due to the patient's inability to rest or the continued discharge of blood, you must fill the wound with moistened cotton soaked in a corrosive ointment. Leave it until it consumes the flesh and fat, then treat it until it is fully healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses and of arrows
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses coming from beneath the arrows are like hard scrofulous swellings with lumps, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be lanced according to this form, from the line 2 to the line 7:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the bowe that is in the abscess is evacuated, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with ointment appropriate for this until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are like scrofulous swellings, lance them as we have said for incisions in scrofulous swellings, and if the wound contains pus, apply a fire cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is ruptured and the skin above is sewn, there often develop abscesses. This likewise happens with a swollen vein and an abscess; and when one recognizes it as being due to the artery, the abscesses are long forming. And when you feel it with your hand, you sense the constriction; and when it is due to the vein, it is visible swelling appearing; and it is foolish to treat this abscess, especially when it is under the armpits, in angles, or near the neck and many other places, and is very large.
