Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, it is advisable to avoid the iron cure. For those who have a chief injury, this too should be avoided. In one who is swollen due to an artery, make a cut above the skin along its length; then operate the dissection with needles, and cleanly separate the artery from the tissues until it is fully exposed; then insert a needle, and pierce it through to the other side, and clamp the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries in the temples. Then pass an intermediate thread between the two ties so that what remains inside comes out, and thus release the abscess; then apply the cure as befits this situation until the threads are secure; finally, treat it with ointment appropriate for such cases until it is healed. If the abscess is due to the opening of a vein, you must stain your hand with as much of the abscess as possible on the skin, then insert the needle under the thread you hold in your hand and pierce it, leaving the double thread so that it passes through to the other side; then tie the abscess as I have said, or the thread from one part to both heads of the thread. If you doubt that the threads will pass, reinsert another needle under the entire abscess along the incision of the first needle, and clamp the threads in three places; then drain the abscess until all excess comes out, then drain the skin and leave what is tied; finally, place a moist cloth of wine and oil on top, and continue with bandages and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses coming to the artery and vein, coming from abscesses of nerves when they are injured, or through too great labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more frequently in joints and elbows, and in all places where there are joints, and it is the grief of abscesses, and its color seems like the color of the body, and is in many dispositions with pain; and when one extracts it forcefully, the patient feels great pain, and it is not just a pain throughout the body, but beneath the heart; and moves well from all sides, and neither forwards nor backwards, neither below nor above, and that which is in joints should not be treated with iron: by chance there might be contraction; and that which is on the head or on the forehead, cut the skin at the spatumile.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers and squeeze at its root; and if it is large, suspend it by the thread, burn it, then remove it and join the wound with sutures, and continue the treatment until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	of large boils hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it occurs in bellies and nowhere else thelul, and it is a disease called "fungus" by resemblance to fungi, and it has fine roots and large heads; and within them are both small and quite large; and I saw a man who had two or more bellies that were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had slender roots, and were split in some places, and within them corroded with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I copied and found in one XVIII ounces weighing, and in the other VI drachms, and the work in incision is such that you should observe if the patient is moist, and the color of the articulare is white and moist and of subtle root; so cop it on the spatumile large, and let the cautery be at your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For in the tailor, there are often too great outflowings of blood, and if the vein breaks, then you must hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient fearing and fearful of the iron incision, then take a well-made thread of flax, and place it on the articulare as we have said, and let it remain for two days; and then restrain, and do not cease to strain the thread of flax until it copes the articulare, and work each by itself; and if the roots are large, then fear to cope immediately for the belly, but you can well cope half of it, then cauterize that it does not return; then treat the wound, and guard that you do not cope the thule which is of fugue color and poor sense and looks like milk.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an embedded abscess, and I will come to the treatment of the chancre after this.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil is hard
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from a fire cautery on a wound or a cut in the skin, and is on the belly and near any of the bowels, as happens in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what was mentioned before, or from wind; and if it is by the rupture of the stomach and through the discharge of the bowel, then the color of the abscess appears similar to the color of the body, and is a slight thing without pain, and evident from various discharges.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the discharge of the intestine, then it is more varied. When pressed at its roots, it sometimes rises and then subsides, and by chance it may become swollen, and greatly increases upon entering the bath and through much work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light matter, and clearly seen when you press it with your hand; it does not constraint much. And if it is due to blood, it clearly shows by these signs: the abscesses are large and hard, and are pierced according to a quantity; and if it is due to phlegm, it sneezes at touch, and the operations are such that you observe whether the appearance is of arterial blood, or vein blood, or phlegm.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	Then you must let the treatment continue.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have said in the chapter on abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the bladder, you must instruct the patient to urinate, and be extended fully straight, then urinate completely throughout the bladder; then command him to lie quietly between your hands, then go under the head that you have marked for all spatumile, then place half of the abscess above at the top of the large uncine; then tie it firmly with a strong thread or a rope of strong silk, and keep it tightly bound; then work on the other half of the abscess extended over the thread, and use your index finger to press; if you find it caught by the thread, release it, and let the bladder lie freely in the abdomen; and if you find the bladder, take it with the uncine, and drain its excess; and if the artery opposes or the vein, go gently under it, then return to your operation and take two needles, and put two strong threads through what you made cross where you pierced; then pull the abscess in four parts over the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the head until it rots, and cut out the dead flesh by itself; or you cut it when it is softened and rotten, then treat the area that needs treatment, and cover the abscess as we have said; and extract the blood or moisture you find, then treat the head with what is needed, and close it.
dou chancre	of the sore
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division of the signs of the sore, and how one should treat it with medicines, and how one must avoid iron cure; and we say that sores arise in the flesh, and great caution is needed in their treatment. The ancients said that when sores are on the skin where they can be scraped as sores are on the sameles, and on the thigh, and similar places, and one should completely remove them when they are at the beginning; and when they are large and old, you must not approach them, for I have never seen any heal from them; nor has anyone healed before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operations, when it is on the skin where one can remove it, as we have said, are that you purge the patient once of black bile; then make him sanguine if he has manifest overfilling, then clean the skin well to prepare for the operation; then throw out the tumor or sore, and the hair from all parts, removing everything completely without leaving anything behind; let the blood flow freely, hold the skin firmly in your hand or with something, and if the bleeding is contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize until the blood is staunched; then treat with other remedies until he is healed.
de ydropisie	from dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already discussed the similitudes of dropsy, and how the assembly of the water is made, and the signs of each similitude, and the cure by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: they are only clarified; and one should not use iron in these two similitudes: namely, tympanites and yposarche, because they are deadly things; therefore when you medicate this similitude of dropsy called "eclites" by medicines, and the cure does not profit, see if the patient is weak or has another disease besides dropsy, such as immediate relief from the belly and similar things; then do not use iron, because there is doubt; and if you see the patient in good health, and he has only dropsy and is neither too thin nor too old, you should proceed thus: lift the patient upright on your hands, and the ministers press the abdomen pushing the water to the lowest part of the foot, then take the thorn spoon according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be cut from two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And let it be pointed, and in any case do not let it enter too deep that it might come to the intestines when inserted, and cannot be withdrawn; then look if the hydropsy is seated towards the intestines: so you must cut beneath the belly three cuts directly over the knife. And if the hydropsy is due to the disease of the liver, your incision should be on the left side of the belly three cuts; and if it is due to the spleen, on the right, and it is not fitting that the patient lie on the cut so that the excess fluids do not flow into that weak place. Then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and let out the fluid, and raise your hand away from all the spatumile between the skin and the syphac as in flaying to the quantity of a finger or nearly so; then pierce the syphac until the spatumile comes to the proper place, and these are the passages of the water, then drain it out, and this is the form of the instrument.
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a thin silver needle, made of light brass or iron, and placed under the part below the small hole; and on one side, three holes; two on the other side, and one on another; and the head is cut like a quill, and this is the shape of the incision that writers cut the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	Above the head is the alemele, so that when the instrument comes to the edge, it should be placed just above the instrument; then fill half or a third of it, for if you fill it more than necessary in that hour, by chance the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit by the weapon, or he falls senseless, or he approaches death; but fill according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient indicate, and his pulse; then remove the instrument and hold the edge, and it is held now for the cair which stops the hole which is below the sypha, of which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then reapply the instrument on another day, if you see the patient suffering as much, and draw a small quantity of fluid; do this any day, and take care not to follow it too long but only a little while.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and there is much fluid, cure it with hot burial earth or sand, and by much sweating or bathing and in the sun, and make him drink; cure with medicines that are drying until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the fluid, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping up of the urethra
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is born who does not have pores in the urethra, or where the pores are small, or are not in their proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary to do so quickly before the very fine sperm has completely discharged according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	then place or perforate the inner side of the scrotum, and sew it up and keep it so for 3 days or 4, and when it is time to urinate, remove the stitches and allow urination, then put it back; and by chance it may not be necessary at all, as the urine that comes forth does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the hole in the scrotum is small, it should be treated with a piece of flax, as we have said, and it will enlarge.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the hole in its place are bleared, for none are born with the hole at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate until they lift their penis up; and they cannot copulate because the matter cannot reach the urethra, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is such that the patient lies often on his back, then the head of the verge and the cope are placed as wide as a pen's tail, so that the perforations close in the middle, as it should; and beware of the flow of blood which comes many times, and if it happens, stop the bleeding with what stops blood, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pustules of the verge
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these pustules come in the verge, and they are an appearance of ugly flesh; and among them there are malignant and non-malignant; so you must treat them with a sharp knife, and cut and cleanse all, then place soft cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment; then treat with diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the ulcer is malignant, of putrid color and exuding, you must apply a cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	And when you have cut it out, and if the ulcer is in the groin, and has part inside the skin and part outside, you must first remove the ulcer that is inside; and when it is drawn together, treat the outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it all together, the head of the groin is not assured so as to prevent perforation, and black corruption comes into the groin and wound; you must remove everything that is black and corrupted, then bind with a plaster made from the bark of pomegranate peels and lint, and continue to treat until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if there is a bleeding episode, apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery aids in two dispositions together: namely, in bleeding and in corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary to insert a probe of plonc into the penis and let the patient urinate through it; and when the hair is reversed at the head of the penis which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or where there is a wound or abscess, then it must be scalded with a cauterizing instrument until the ligaments are released, and the head of the penis is freed from all sides; and if this is a serious matter to discuss, then it must be scalded with a spatule slightly at the head of the penis and skin; then separate them well apart, and place a thin linen cloth moistened in cold water over them, so that they do not become revesed again.
de la circoncision	of the circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the dislocation of continuity like other wounds; nevertheless, when we perform this work of our own will, and properly on infants, it is necessary that we do the best work and the most gentle for their health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcising their children, for they do not use it in their law, and we have no reason except what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the majority of masters and practitioners who performed circumcision using a knife, forceps, and an entire pair of scissors; they found it difficult because there are two blades, and by chance one could cut the upper part and remain with the lower.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the recovery is coped with, and the pain is doubled, and in the dressing which is from the palm, the points of the limb are not assured; and in the dressing of the nail by accident the iron escapes, and the work runs, and many times they arise thus without needing a dressing and I have wanted it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the dressing which is done for the strength to all the thread of hair I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the strength cuts just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, cut equally all along the whole thread; but that the hairs be well thin within the skin; and let the manner of the first work be such that you make the child think, if it hears, that you only tie the hair around the shaft merely, and let him hope in every way that you can; then place it straight between your hands, and put the forces under or over your feet that the child does not see, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand to the shaft and blow where you choose, and pull it up until the heads of the shaft are dry; then well dress from the ordure which is collected, then tie the part signet with a double thread, then tie under one by one the threads; and hold at two doigts by the second hour in pouchet and on the right index, and cope between the two threads, then lift the keur hastily and pull the head of the shaft; then let the blood run little by little, for it is the most important; and put powder above and above the powder a glued drapeil from half an egg cooked untimely in rose water, confited with rose-scented oil good and fresh, and leave it on until another day, and cure with other cure until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forceps for delivery is this: the two heads should be held and sharp, and the heads of the forceps should be as large as the fingers are equal.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in delivery is when the child within comes to an incision; therefore, you must stretch it with your finger, just as the fingers make an abscess; and keep it equal, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, hold it with forceps, and then stretch it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it persists for three days, and that which is beneath the scrotum is swollen, let it be so until the abscesses have calmed, and gently cauterize it; handle it as you can move, and avoid the part of the scrotum, as it will not harm it.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat therefore the shoulder of sudden wounds from powder, as we have said in treating powders, and if it swells beyond measure, it will not harm; treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	For the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	For the retention of urine, it is due to stone impaction, or congealed blood, or bowel, or new flesh, or similar things as we have said in the division. And if the urine is not relieved and you see the retention is due to a stone at the neck or opening of the bladder, then the patient should be positioned with their knees bent; place their feet on the back, and extend their abdomen above the back, and restrain the patient so they cannot move as much as possible. This will force the neck of the bladder to express the stone upwards, thereby relieving the urine retention; if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you should administer extraction using an instrument called a "syringe," which has this form: it is made of light, thin silver, like the feathers of an eye; its handle is one and a half palms long and very fine at the end.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of the issue of urine is that you take a double thread, and tie at the end a little wool or cotton, and insert the thread into the syringe; and clip the excess of the wool and fill it just to the tip of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and place the patient on a seat, and he arouses the bladder and the penis with moistened oil and olive oil and water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis, until it comes to the root of the penis, then cover the penis above towards the mouth; then fill the syringe before just to the bladder, and let the patient feel urine coming up to the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order because what leads it there is crooked; then pull the thread all little by little, and urine follows the wool, then extract it out, and make flow the urine; and refill the syringe as long as the bladder is emptied, and bind the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When burns or blood come into the bladder, or putrefaction is gathered there, and you see it discharge acidic fluids and medications, make use of the instrument called "clepsydra," and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and has three holes: two on one side, and one on the other, as you can see; and the leashes are attached so that the medicines may be well retained by the verge upon application, allowing for the removal of moisture when necessary. And when you wish to administer your medicines into the bladder, place the head of the catheter in the moisture, and draw it gently through. By doing this, you will draw the moisture out with the catheter, and then firmly reinsert the catheter. The moisture will enter again and reach the bladder, allowing the patient to feel its effects; and this is the form of the subtle clyster used to treat the bladder: as shown here.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or of silver alloy, and the head is higher; and below at the chest where the cords hang; then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture you see to be able to soften the bladder, then tie between the two breasts forming a single double thread, and heat that part of the moisture over the fire; then insert the tip of the clyster into the vagina, then squeeze your hand on the bladder until all the moisture is applied appropriately, so that the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it roundly around; then insert the strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a nail, and put inside what you want of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; do so as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	from the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already discussed in the division the methods of stone, and their extraction together with medicines; and we have said the difference between a strangled stone and all the signs, and in which stone one should operate by size; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you plainly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is strangled in the bladder happens more often to children, and this is a sign that the urine has jumped from the bladder seeming like urine in its subtlety; and it clearly harms the child's penis, and pierces many times, and then hardens; and most of these jumps are dangerous; and the cure is light for children until they are four years old, and is much more serious in older people, and is medium for those between childhood and old age; and the treatment is lighter for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to treatment, it is necessary first to purify the patient with enemas, to remove all the filth from the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it obstructs at times in seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and draw them out and move them into place so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and passes out through the urethra; then have the patient sit between your prepared hands, and their hands be beneath their thighs, so that the bladder hangs entirely downward; then wait and touch it from within; if you feel the stone in the space, hasten now to incise over the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall at the touch from top to bottom, soften your index finger of your left hand, if the patient is feeble, or your middle finger, if the patient is a young adult; place your hand on its base, wait and feel for the stone with your finger; when you sense it on your finger, moil around the neck of the bladder; then press above your finger and incise at the point where you see fit to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand upwards, and remove the skin that is beneath the nails in the part where the incision is made; then pour in the mixture cutting, of which this is its form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And cut between what is between the nails and the fundament, not exactly in the middle but on the side of the left thumb; and be straight above the stone, and your two hands should be close to or on the fundament, and make the incision so that it is wide at the back and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; perhaps the pressure will cause the hand near the fundament to burst without effort. Know that there are stones with angles and edges: they are easier to remove; and there are others that are underneath, resembling a glans and round, from which the release is gentle.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	For those who have angles and margin, make the size greater; and if it does not pass, you must grip with tongs that are like a file at the head, to move and extract the stone so that it does not escape; or you put under the instrument a subtle curved blade at the head; and if you cannot manipulate thus, you enlarge the hole slightly, and if the skin is undamaged, you extract it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stone, you put the larger one first in the neck of the bladder, then cover up, then pull hard, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is much larger, you must sew it up, and make a greater wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or urine comes out through it so that the legs cannot be sewn up; but nevertheless strive to treat it, or to cut with tongs, as long as you remove it piece by piece. When you have completed your work, fill the wound with incense and aloes and dragon's blood, bind it, and place a wet cloth over it in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to cool the abscess; then restitch the patient on his side, and do not untie the bandage for three days.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you dislocate it, raise much well the head of the oil and water, then treat with the ointment defninicon and ointment basilicon until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses and corrosions in the wound, and clots of blood in the bladder, and so are retained by urine, which is known to pass without jumping with the urine: then pour thy thumb into the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will rot the bladder; then wash the wound with oil, alum, and salt, and aid it in all ways you see until it is healed; and it is necessary that all ointments you treat it with, thou bind the two thighs, and apply the medicines to the head.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is lodged in the passage of the penis, and urine cannot pass; then you should cut as I said before, but an excuse can be made for this cutting due to the cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have proved this thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take I iron fork according to this form and fix it in the coal:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	then take the thread and tie it around the penis over the stone, so that it cannot move back into the bladder; then insert the fork gently into the penis until it reaches the stone; and turn the fork in the stone little by little, as much as you can pierce the stone from another side; then urine will come soon, then press your hand on what remains of the stone inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is soon broken, and then jumps with urine, the patient recovers. And if you cannot do this for any reason, tie a thread under the stone and another above, then place the rod at the stone between the two threads, extract the stone, untie one thread, and cleanse the congealed blood in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	from the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	Often it happens that a stone forms in women, and if this happens even once, the wound must be cured gently, and is forbidden for three reasons: the first is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a well-informed woman who can safely disclose herself to examination, especially when she is pregnant.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman skilled in this art; and the fourth manner is that the woman's opening is more tightly shut than a man's, for which reason it requires a deeper incision, and great fear arises. And if necessity demands this of those, you must seek a midwife well knowing, and at points thereof find one; and if you cannot find her, you should consult a skilled surgeon; and present to the woman a guide in the lives of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command concerning the inquiry of the stone; and carefully observe whether the woman is a virgin: then she must place her finger or foundation under her and seek the stone; and if she finds it, you should force her to hold fast with her finger or under the sick one, and press and squeeze her left hand on the bladder firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, she must move it greatly from the entrance of the bladder until below, until she comes to the root of the thigh; then cut on the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the groin, and let what is ready appear in that part; and do not move your hand over or under the stone, and make the cut first small; then put the rag into the incision, if you feel the stone increase the wound as much as the stone can issue forth, and know that there are many kinds of stones: namely, small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and those with grooves.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the signs to know the issue.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the stone passes, put vitriol on it, and hold it for an hour until the stone is discharged; then return to your work until the stone is passed, and have the instruments I told you about in the extraction of stones for help in your work; and if the stone passes, and it is the artery that has been cut, put powder on it with hemlock and bindworts, and do not repeat this, and leave the stone undisturbed, lest by chance the patient die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is pacified, and the swelling permits, then return to your work, until the stone is cured.
de hernie carnouse	of fatty hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Aqueous humor is nothing but a collection of moisture or white fluid, which is beneath the heart of the eyeball that contains the egg [eye]; and it is called "syphac," and sometimes properly in the membrane of the eye, if one thinks it is another egg. And it is the skin of the eyeball between the white syphac fluid as we have said; and this does not happen often.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this humor arises from weakness that comes to the eyeballs, and this substance is diffused.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the joints, and this moisture has many colors: or it is a color declining to jaundice, or it is without red, or black, or watery white, and this happens more; and these are the signs to know this assembly, for if it is or whitish as we have said, it is an abscess ripe, not long as the figure of an egg, and does not open the joints, for it has moisture throughout.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if it has moisture in the proper lining, it is an abscess ripe with part of the egg, and because of this, one thinks it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the joints and the whitish, you sense it well; therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, you prove it through the entire intervening square, of which the form was described earlier.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the introductory part, judge of what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we cauterize with iron, the patient must be anesthetized according to our power and the fullness of his body; then place the sponge on his back, on a spot slightly high, and put a lot of lint over it; sit on his left side, and instruct the minister to sit on the right, extending the staff to one of the two ribs of the heart; then take the cauterizing iron, burn the skin between them long until near the knife, and make sure the cut is straight by dividing the heart's skin up to a white seam, and gently sear it according to your power; then pierce the white seam fully with water through large openings, and drain all the water out, then put in your needles, and raise the white seam upward; do not touch the heart of the ribs, but only the white seam; cut completely or in pieces the rib's edge precisely thin, for if you do not cut it well deeply, the water will return; and if the egg was spoiled during your work, reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the white seam; then join the two flaps of the heart of the ribs with a stitch, and cure it as other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, it must be that you bind the vessels that are suspensive, doubting the bleeding; then scrape the yolk throughout the suspensive part, and extract the egg, and cleanse it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the fluid is collected in two parts assembled, know that these are two branches; then scrape the other part as you have done the first equally, and wipe away the blood, and put in the wound moistened wool in rose oil; and place another moistened wool in wine and oil, and put between the two yolks, and place above folded cloth, and bind it over everything according to this form.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and bind them with strips of torn wool according to this likeness, stitching them in the waistband of the breeches. One shoulder is placed down to the fundament just to the back, and the other to the part of the thigh; and the other two corners over the two angles, and be entirely stitched together at the loop of the breeches; and once this branch is medicated with a fire cautery instead of an iron knife, it should be that you bind the cautery with a sharp small blade, and scrape the skin of the yolks, and heat them as we have said, so that the white syrup containing the fluid is revealed; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that yolk at the pricking points, and scorch it with this sharp hot cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the cloth in all manners that you can, until you dry it all; and keep that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more holy; and move guards against flow of blood, and make sure incisions are clean; and if nothing else causes contrary effect, or abscess forms or blood flow or other thing, so cure what causes contrary effect, according to what was said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not wish to wait for this work because of its horror, then perform perforation as I have told you. This is when you are certain by the signs we have said that a watery abscess is present, so make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess from beneath at the part underneath all the way to the large spatumile, and place the perforation along the length of the body. Make the openings wide enough for all the fluid to flow out. Then place cotton over the opening and bind it, allowing the remaining fluid to drain, and continue to treat the wound until it heals. If the white cloth does not allow the fluid to escape through the hole in the wound, then you must insert a pen or the instrument used to drain fluid from dropsy patients, as described before. Widen the opening of the wound, and know that the fluid will return and gather after about six months or so, and when it has gathered as described before, then the patient's days will pass in this manner.
de l’aposteme des coions	from the abscess at the joints
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	In this section of the branch there is fear in many dispositions, which is why it seems to me that we should leave it as it is; and I will tell you the work and similar things of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses come from flesh, and especially at joints; and it is by much chance.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to say that they come from bitter and acrid superfluity spread at the joints, or by percussion; and the color of the abscess depends on the color of the flesh; and it does not find any pain, and it is a grievous abscess; and by chance it may be a painful and stony abscess with a flowing color, and sometimes comes from a vein or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from an artery, it is known by the arrangement of the hot abscess, when you press it with your thumb and fingers; and you should not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	Who is made of venous swelling is known by its arrangement at the expression from pressing with the thumb and fingers, and can well be cut from this appearance and from other marks; and you peel the core of the lump, then the yolk is on top, and the force of the white is soft, and deliver the suspender from all sides of the yolk.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the yolk is already firm with these marks, then you must incise the yolk and peel it; and if it is airy at the soft part or within the vessels, then you must remove all that is tender, and peel the core roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birthplace of the flesh is rotten behind, it must be cut out entirely, and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is accomplished, dress the wound with moistened wool in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other salves until it heals.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the groin
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess wrapped in a wrapping resembling a gourd, with the groin area softened. The patient will experience pain as it changes; and the treatment for this illness should be well applied like the one mentioned earlier. We will describe the work of these treatments according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It must be that you place the patient on an elevated seat, then apply the suspensory ligament below the hips to your thighs, covering all the vessels near the groin, and you must master the technique, stretching them fully; then cut along a sharp spatulum through the vessels, until they are exposed, and then scrape from each side as we have said in the extraction of arteries in temples; then insert an awl with double thread, attaching it to the first spot where the vein has come out, and again attach it to another end; then cover centrally straight according to the length of the body, removing corrupted moisture; then treat the wound as for other cases where there is a large opening, ensuring no vessels that nourish one of the hips are severed; because from this no harm comes, but if it happens at all the veins have the same condition, then you must remove the hip at all vessels; so that the eye does not lose its nourishment due to incision of the vessels, drying out and unable to be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the seam
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The events of this ramification are by section that comes from the rupture of the seam, or the extension on the belly in the part of the inguinal region, for which reason the intestines descend through that rupture to one of the iliacs; and this rupture is either of the seam or due to its extension, and come in these two manners of causes: by percussion, or jumping, or shouting, or lifting a heavy burden, and similar things; and the signs when it is due to the extension of the seam are that it happens little by little, over a long period of time, and does not come suddenly; and the abscesses are equal until near the perineum, for the seam presses on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	The signs are when it is due to the section of the seam, which causes a sudden onset of pain, and the abscesses appear varied and beneath the skin, for the release of the intestines and the core outside the seam.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes with the circle [of the wound] around the intestine, it is retained in question, and causes great pain to the patient, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these treatments with iron, for which it is advisable to avoid.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of this treatment is that you command the patient to remove the intestine with his hand inside the wound if it can enter; then anoint around his neck and lift his legs; then place the keur above, and cut all the skin from the long length; then insert the leaves of the taille uncines according to what you need to open the wound, making sure they are such that the oes can issue forth; then scrape the surface beneath the skin of the keur until the white surface is uncovered on all sides;
