then place your index finger where the keion should be, between the white surface which is under the skin of the egg, and between the second surface, and depart what is behind the egg, and between the second surface; and then move the hand with the keur of coions with your right hand, and bring the white surface up to your left hand, and lift the egg towards the entire surface of the syfac towards the taille; and command the minister to extend the egg upwards, and release what is behind the ligament; and keep your fingers quiet if there is any part of the intestine enveloped or hard white surface, and if you find anything, place it in the belly under the skin; then take a needle with a thick thread made of ten strands, and insert it into the rear part of the syfac, which is after the skin of the keur; after the taille, then cut the heads that appear from the threads until there are four strands; then assemble them one over the other in the shape of a cross, and fix the syfac where we said it was under the skin of the keur with a strong thread of two fingers' length; then cover the heads of the threads, and fix them firmly with two fingers, so that no vessel that nourishes them can enter into them, and the abscess may not come back; and put the thread again according to the first long thread for two fingers, and after these two threads leave from the syfac under the keur of coions the size of a finger; and then cut the rest according to the roundness that the egg carries; then cover in the part that is under the skin of the coions until it does not corrode or rot as we said before; then apply moistened wool, and put it on the wounds, and apply the thread as we said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the whites of the eyes are cauterized after the incision, out of doubt about bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens many times, and leave the thread until it falls on its own; and if it delays in falling, then soak it in hot water, and put on what we have said, until it falls; then treat the wound with another dressing until it is healed perfectly.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia carnosa
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch I have never seen anyone dare to perform the treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is made like the branch which is twisted together at the vice, in such a manner that you tie the vessels, after lightly incising the dislocation; then cut it in half, and treat the abscess of those who work, until the vessels close; and treat it as we have said until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes there is a rupture in the groin, as we have said, and it opens the veins; and no parts of the intestines come out through the wound, and if they do come out, it is little and returns every hour; and yet, if it remains too long in this spot, it causes the wound or syphilis, as much as the intestine comes out; and this happens due to the extension of syphilis which is in the groin, as we have said, for it extends, then softens and swells the veins and opens them; and the cure is by cautery, as we have previously said; and sometimes the wound is cured with a piece of iron in this manner: and that the patient lies often on his back between your hands, then cut the vein from the large swelling edge according to the size of three fingers; then remove the syphilis that is under the skin that follows, then take the rod and place it over the apparent vein; and press firmly against the belly, then sew the two apparent veins on top of the head of the rod, and sew one and the other; then remove the head of the rod, and neither copulate nor extend the wound in any other way, as I have told you in the cure of the intestine ramification; then cure it by the method of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, it relaxes and treats the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The soothing is constrained, and shows no sign in the rupture, and the cauterizations are healed in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin around the shoulders
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin around the shoulders becomes soft in some people, because the flesh within is softened, and it is to be seen; and when one wishes to treat such a wound, one should have the patient lie on their back, and cut away the soft skin above the natural skin; then join the two edges with a缝合线，如果软化皮肤的多余部分需要更牢固地缝合，则用三针或四针；然后在这些缝线之间切开，并像其他伤口一样处理，直到痊愈，剪去线。
dou chastrement	by punishment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Punishment is prescribed in our law, and for this reason, I would like to avoid speaking of it in this book; and it is necessary only for two reasons: one, that you may know how to respond when asked about it and how to treat it; and the other, because we often need to punish certain animals to aid us, as with goats, sheep, dogs, and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say then that punishment is done in two ways: either by attraction or by splitting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the method where we do punishment by attraction, seat the animal in hot water until the joints become soft and relaxed. Then grasp them with your hand while they are thus softened and you no longer feel any resistance.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of castration: You must castrate the beast, and press the scrotum with your left hand, then tie the suspender, and cut above each testicle one by one when you have well seared them; and leave a little piece of fat and the subtle fat which is under the vessels; and this way of castration is better than that done by suction, because in suction some part of the scrotum may remain, causing the beast to desire lust; then treat the wound until it heals.
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphrodites.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphrodites are according to two manners in men: one is that between the two testicles, it appears as the figure of a woman's nature, or it has hair, and sometimes for urinary purposes.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other method is for women, and is done with a knife as with a rod and two clamps.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the care of the man and woman is that you clean all the set bones thoroughly, and treat them as other wounds; in the second manner, for those whose urine jumps through the skin of the scrotum, they do not need treatment.
de la tentigene	of the excrescence
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Excrescence is a set bone on the natural part, to such an extent that it is too ugly to see; and some women have them as large as a hand, and this is how they are treated.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You must dye the excrescence with your hand or claws and clean it gently; and do not apply too strongly, lest blood flow. Continue treating it until it heals. For another bone that grows at the mouth of the vein, fill it and sometimes it will protrude, resembling a cow's hoof, hence they called it the "cow disease" in ancient times.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary to cut it, as we have said regarding the texture and treatment until it is healed.
de erratique	of erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic if it is when the nature of the woman is not known, or the perforation is small; and it is natural by birth, or an accident caused by illness that came about; or it is due to a mistaken cautery, or a thin or thick syphon, and is made perfect in the loins, or in the sides, or beneath, or elsewhere; and it prevents conception, and childbirth, and sometimes the flowers to have; and the knowledge of these is by the sight of the midwife.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the stoppages are close and apparent, feel with your fingers or the rod.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a thin sweat, and it is near the two flanks, hasten, and roll thus: place your two index fingers together, and let the woman be on her back, spreading her legs; then form the two flaps, so that the thin sweat is rolled, and over the stoppers; then take wool, and the fat in oil, and put it on the wound, and let the woman lie on her side each day, so that it does not scab.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the sweat is hard and thick, it is necessary that you fold it with the spatula resembling a leaf of juniper.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the stoppers are of new leather, suspend them with a needle and thread; and have the medicines that staunch blood, such as myrrh, dragon's blood, incense, together with many eggs; then apply a large piece of lint, so that the wound does not scab; and thus leave it long, and give him another linen bandage; and continue to treat with other dressings until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the sore comes flesh grown, you must treat it according to this manner, if it is not embedded abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the embedded abscess in the sore, one must not touch it to cut.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that, without treatment, commonly recur. And when hemorrhoids become old, they turn into warts; and I have already described their appearances, signs, and symptoms in the division of similar cases, and I will now describe those that can be cured.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and warts, when fully inflamed in the sore, do not appear by touch; they are cured only with iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the abscess, which one can feel, are those one can treat.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, you should place the woman in a cold room, then heat the altar root with tongs, and pour it into its roots, then sprinkle medicines that restrain blood, such as aloe, dragon's blood, and incense, and similar things; then let her sit against the wall for an hour, then immerse her in cold water; and if bleeding continues, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and the bark of pomegranate peels and galingale and similar things, and then take flour of barley, mix it with honey and garlic, and apply it as a plaster on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops bleeding, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, if they make you apply suction cups to the back and breasts without injuring; then take wool, and grease in juice of plantain or juice of agrimony with old wine, and apply to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess rests, cure the place with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough head, so you should cover it as I said for the thigh; and then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses of the armendaris
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses occur in the armendaris, such as chancre, stone abscess, herpes, cysts, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and hot abscess, as well as many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore, I must say in this treatise on the hot abscess that comes from the armpit, which is not among those abscesses that boil; and if you wish to know the iron work, observe whether the abscess is active at the beginning of its appearance, and full of heat and fever, and becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore, do not hasten to pierce; but let it die until the pain is appeased; and then seat the patient on a chair, and provide two stools for him to recline, supporting his back and bringing his feet together below the knee; and let his thighs be spread, and place his arms beneath his knees, binding them well with a good bandage; then apply the bale towards the right side, and lead it to the instrument used for opening the armpit, of which we shall speak later in form; and it is necessary that when you see this instrument being applied, you insert the rod first to know the depth of the armpit, so that what enters from the instrument does not go more deep than it should, and does not harm the patient; and if the instruments are larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the armpit with cloths, so that the instrument does not cause pain; and it is necessary that he place the horn of the instrument above, and touch the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is opened and they make it soft by hand, it must be dressed at the head, with linen soaked in rose oil or green fat oil; and place the dressing well inside the wound, and on top of the wound and on the handle of the knife a clean piece of linen moistened in water or honey that has been cooked; then cure after two days of suitable ointment until it is healed; and at any time lift the wound and the area around it with a clyster of water and honey, and then of water or roots of lily and aromatic long-cooked.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is placed on the abdomen, you must guard against using iron to cook it, but dress it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Master it first in the dance that she know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman press down below, and desire to smell the air: then hasten for the child to be soon born; know then that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and comes out with its head, and the second follows with it; and when you see these signs, you must gently press her belly, so that the child comes forth quickly; for when it descends above its head, the second follows with it, and is cleansed of its superfluities by good purification; and who comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it comes sometimes above its feet, and is born into the body or shoulder, and the hands, or if it comes above the belly or spine, and is turned by chance over the neck, and in other harmful shapes; it is necessary for her that she be wise and subtle in these matters, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the shapes how one must aid them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes down on his head by natural means, and the woman gives birth easily, and the virtue of her is weak, then let it sit on a saddle, or where women keep it; and from its nature, take oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then pour the balm between her two little spatumiles as they are formed.
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and cut the secondine, and cut away its membrane until the moisture that is within comes out; and compress the woman's abdomen until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then you must administer a suppository to the woman with fenugreek muscilage and olive oil; then let her take snuff of condisi, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: then extract the child now.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands appear swollen, you must gently reduce them little by little; and if they cannot enter, place the woman on a seat, and lift her feet high; then move the seat to the ground, and shield the woman so she does not cry at the reduction; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, cut off the child with the knife placed before, and extract the child, reducing them equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the issue of the child at his feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes at his feet, you must lift it up; then turn it little by little, until it is equal; then dress the feet and extend them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps to the thighs, instruct him to press, and make him sneeze by means of sniffing; if it is worse, let God will it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not worse as we have said, turn it little by little, until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is lightly.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come worse as we have said, take muscillaige of althea, and oil of sesamum, and melted gum, and grind them all in a mortar; and put the nature of the woman inside and above this ointment; then make her sit in hot water until under the ribs; and when she is softened underneath, give her a collar of myrrh, and put it under, and let her keep it for an hour; then make her sit on a chair, then make her sneeze and press her mouth and nose, and gently rub her abdomen, for the child now jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the issue of the child above his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, one should gently place their hands little by little; then it should be bathed on its neck, and its feet should be hanging down, and it should lie on the bed; bend its arms little by little, and then put its hands on the abdomen, and remove the cushions below until it is prepared to hang down; and if the child does not cry, take its feet and move them into shape, then lift the abdomen upward, and then place your hands; and gently guide the child; and command the woman to press until the child passes.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child who comes with one hand wide open
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I must devise to bring back the hand: if one cannot bring it back, make the woman stand and walk; if she cannot walk, lay her on the bed, prop up her legs, then administer the ligature as I have recounted; and if she does not miscarry, make her sit on a chair, then study to bring back the hand; and withdraw the child according to its natural position, and command her to sneeze, and tell her to bear down until the fetus has passed.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From the issue of the child at its neck, and have spread its hands, and its face turned toward its mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I must have the midwife grasp the child's hand, then turn it little by little and gently; and when it is aligned, place the natural ligature of thread and oil on it, as we have said, then command her to move it little by little; and when you have done this, make her sit on a chair, and command her to bear down; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in this same manner for all the second part
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to the second part in this manner, cut the umbilical cord with your nail until all the moisture is drained; and if the child can be placed on its face and neck, cut the cord from the mouth, without holding it back, and strangle the child; then put the child inside, placing it as you see fit, and instruct the woman to do this once: then gently extract.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the extraction of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins often are born, and sometimes three or four are born; this is not an uncommon thing, and it happens frequently.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are extracted things, and do not live much, if at all; I know them, that they be multiplied, and are deprived by the syphilis which devises them, which is linked to the brain; and sometimes issued also naturally like unto those under it, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they issue properly, the treatment as we have said, and let the subtle bile operate quickly and easily; and proceed thus as it best serves for salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the womb I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to fifteen, and are all formed in the shape of a child by the measure of the glorious sage, and it must be that the bile know all this, for similar things may happen; do so according to what is appropriate.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman who has lost a dead child or is pregnant, as I have said in the division, and there is no expulsion, and you are constrained to perform manual labor; it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound health and has no accidents or fears of death; she should be fanned from behind, and her head inclined forward, with her legs raised; and the minister should be on two sides, tied to the bed so she does not move during the descent of the child. Then rub her mouth with moist oils mixed with muscilage of alethe and fenugreek and linseed, then apply these mixtures to her hands. Gently place the fingers in her mouth or throat or palate or under the beard or on her temples or near her sides, and if the descent is through the feet, insert the needle or dagger between the middle ribs; it must be that she holds the finger on her right hand, placing the cord between her left thumb and first finger, and gently rubs this to her right hand. Insert the finger where we have said, until it reaches the empty place; and this is the form of the finger:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	then pierce against the other arrow, or the third if you need it, so that the extractions be equal; and then stretch equally by moving from one side to another, to let them out, and let the arrows have teeth to hold them, as is shown here:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part of it remains, open with any of his eye teeth, and push it into that part, and cut the other part; and if there remains no part, set this arrow or higher up, and do this until it all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be brought back due to constriction, you must wrap it with a cloth, until it all comes out; then cut the cloth at the sole joint or with scissors, and do this likewise for the other hand, and for both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the child is large and the birth canal is narrow, or it has a sharp head that assembles, then you must insert the spatumile spine between your two fingers, cut the head, and extract the sharpness; or you can rotate it with an instrument called "almidach," from which form comes with instruments or chapter after this one; and thus similarly make so that the child has a large natural head; and then pull out the bones with tongs, and if the head breaks free and is restrained by force, split it until the moisture that is or more issues; and if she cannot issue, cut her apart into pieces as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then you must pierce her until the moisture runs.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the injury is on his feet, the traction is light, and the direction to the mouth of the vein is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is narrow in the belly or the breast, it is fitting that you extract it with a flying cloth wrapped around the hand; and cut the belly or the breast until the moist parts are removed; and if the other limb has been removed, and the head remains, then bind the hand fully with the vein; and draw it until the mouth of the vein. Then give an ounce or two, and draw forcefully; and if the mouth of the vein is narrowed by a hot abscess that has come, it is not fitting to work on it, but you must administer moist and greasy things; and apply poultices, and a wetting sitz bath with mollifying and moistening substances.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the patient is on his side, and you can place him level, then administer what we have said for the living child; and if it is not possible, then stretch with pieces, and leave nothing of the secondine.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, administer what we have said for abscesses that come in the thigh, and if bleeding occurs, it should be placed in cold water restraining, and administer other dressings.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly an infant had died, then sutured the other [infant] over it, and expelled the dead one.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, abscesses formed in the mouth, and swelled so much that they opened, and caused great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called for the treatment, and I thought long, and could not staunch the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a plaster of strong吸引力，and it brought out some bones, and after several days, others followed.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marvelled much, for the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that these were the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I examined the wound and found bones there, so that the woman was much improved; and the woman lay there long thus, and still had a bit of swelling from it; and I did not recall this chapter because whenever a master finds an unusual thing, he should know how to provide aid.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring back the joint to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	After comes the form of the presser, to which the books refer; and to two turns of the two heads of the ligaments.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Firstly, the horns should be finer than those of a restrictor, and made of ebony or boxwood. The hole in the wood should be two fingers wide, and the edge of the holes one finger long, and each should be as long as half a palm or slightly more. These two adjustments are inserted into the hole in the joint to open it when the two horns are turned.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, finer and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, resembling tweezers. It should have two adjustments at the heads, as you see, each one finger long and two fingers wide. When you wish to open the joint completely with this entire instrument, place the woman on a bed, with her feet hanging and legs spread apart, then insert the two adjustments together into the joint, holding the head of the instrument under her thighs. Then work your hand on the entire instrument as you did with the tweezers equally, according to the amount you wish to open the mouth of the joint until the hinge does what it wills.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This tool is entirely mounted, and its images are multiplied; and when the mirrors have been arranged, the work is more speedy, and higher for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not arrange the instrument, you must have it ready, for its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine is retained during childbirth, you must instruct the patient to grip her tail, and then make her inhale condisi, and hold her hands over her mouth and nose; and if she passes through this way, well it is.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If this does not work, take a pot and make a hole or coverlet in it, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the mare inside, such as calamus, rue, fennel, chamomile, cinnamon, and centaury; all these herbs, or any of them, be cooked or placed in water on the fire. Then place a reed or hole in the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the mare, and hold it until the vapors come inside the mare. Then make her inhale as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second joint moves quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment, and is not already healed, command the maid to moisten her left hand in sesame oil or in almond oil, then put the bottle back into nature, and seek the second joint; and when she has found it, take it and extend it little by little straight, so that the tendons do not tear during extraction; but it must be moved slightly from side to side, then cut; it will come and resolve itself.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the tendon is narrowly strangled, we have already said the treatment for sneezing and fumigation with herbs; and if it is not cured by all that we have said, guard that you do not follow the extraction; but it must be that what is at the mouth of the tendon you tie to the thigh of the woman, then catheterize with tetrapharmcon ointment; she will take it and restore it, and it will become healed; but still, if it comes ill-smelling to the stomach and head, and blisters the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If therefore suitable fumigations are needed for it: some of the ancients have proven the fumigation of cress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman for the retention of flowers and secondine is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is made of glass resembling a cane, and one places the fine end in the nature, and the broad heads above the fire; and let the fumigations be over the coals, and the scab until it is eaten away, and begin another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the foundation pierced, but have a soft syfac: then it is necessary for the baile to pierce that syfac in the right place, and not pierce the spatumile too deeply, and take care that she does not touch it; then put on wet wool soaked in wine and oil, and cure with ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not return to place, put or insert a pledget of wool, and let it remain in place, and be removed when the child wants to go into rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this plug comes suddenly from a wound or abscess; then it must be handled suddenly: it should be treated as we have said for the pledget of wool.
de la fistule dou fondement	from the fistula of the fundament
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from the fundament are nodes, and grow larger as they proceed from the fundament down, or in the space between two parts, either one or several; and when this node is old, it works, and exudes moist white or subtle liquid, and sometimes these fistulas are Persian; they are known by those who have them through evacuation or windy discharge when the patient evacuates, and by accident through a passing urine.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if the fistulas extend to the bladder, and to half the length of the penis; and reach to the knee joint, and to the ankle.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows whether the fistula ends at the anus, and not at all: it is that you insert your index finger into the anus, and insert a fine needle of brass or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is tortuosity, insert a fine probe of linen or horsehair, as far as you can feel the probe or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and no excretion or wind or vermin come out, as we have said: know that it does not reach; hasten to treat.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is infected up to the bladder or up to the urinary duct, it will drain urine, and cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is cut up to the joint of the thigh, the infection comes up to the place; if there are no twists and turns and the location of the pain is within, if it is deep seated and not reachable, then neither medicine nor immediate treatment with ointment helps; in these infected fistulas, there is no cure other than hard work and the vanity of foolish people who intervene.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	For those that are not infected and not old, with hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced, and where the patient lies on their back; lift the legs up to the thighs, and incline the thighs toward the abdomen; then place a tent of wax or pitch if there are twists and turns, as long as you know where the infection is coming from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain deep within the fundament, you must place your index finger there; if you then feel that the tendons have been pierced, know that it is purulent; if you do not work on it, it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One can properly heal some cases, but this happens rarely. The aid we apply, one must heat the fine cautery according to the width of the fistula, as was previously said; and place it hot in the fistula until it comes from the fundament; and do this two or three times, until you know that the charred flesh has been thoroughly burned, which resembles a bird's feather; and then cure with ointment-soaked cloths until the charred flesh is gone, then treat with an inflamed ointment to close the wound.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healed, that is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it is thus healed, and the tent comes out, and does not pierce just to the depth which is the foundation, and between your thumb and the tent there is a thick covering of flesh or fat, and you see the fistula at that which follows the covering from the heart; scrape from the beginning of the fistula, and apply something before the tent, and cauterize after it until it reaches the top of the tent; then the tent will be delivered and fall; then defray those flesh wounds that seem like a bird's feather, and there remain none.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the wound becomes infected and cuts between you and the work, cauterize with fire or with a watery medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery, it comprises two good things: namely, the burning of these edges adjutant, and the stopping of blood and drying of moisture; then the treatment of wounds soaked in butter or ground cheese, until the eyes emit pus, and remove the burnt edges in the pus; then treat the wound with ointments thickening hard flesh, and are dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes just to the point of the foundation and is distant from the body, then probe the point or foundation, and inquire there.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	And if the fistula comes just to the point of the foundation and is distant from the body, then probe the point or foundation, and inquire there. If you feel the tent, and between them is cloth or skin or edges, or it is about to perforate, then there should be no ways other than a path of faith and hope, by administering one of the three methods: either you cauterize as we have said, or you cut down to the root, or if you can, put tents and treat as first; do not go too far from the point, lest you cut the tissue that holds the foundation, and allow the passages by their own will; then treat, as we have said; perhaps it will be healed. Or you remove that cover and cleanse since it is cut close to the foundation with a tent or another pointed instrument; then depurate the affected flesh in the wound as much as you can; then study to restore the wound and keep the fistula above the foundation: this would be a lighter matter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are treated in this manner: and it is when you puncture the fistula, and it is located near the base beneath the skin, so take a needle pierced at the top according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And you wind the thread twice around it, and insert the needle with the thread into the fistula until it reaches the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is near the margin beneath the base, then extract the thread from that punctured area, as you would puncture the base; and pull the top of the thread, and join the two heads together, holding them against each other, and leave them for one or two days; and hold them together once until the threads close the gaps between them completely. Then treat the wound until it is healed and sound.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not perforate, make it perforate in all ways that you can, provided it is not too close to the surface.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not fitting to cauterize for the ligature too close to the surface, and then treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spinal bone from which a fistula is made is very hard on one side and sharp; and on the other side not so much, because what should not be cauterized should not be cauterized, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: either they are within the fundament, like grains of resin, and there may be small or large ones, and some have much moisture, while others have little, sometimes only a bit of yellowish water or a bit of blood, and have the color of the flesh. The treatment for those within the fundament is to instruct the patient to lie down to relieve himself in chambers until the fundament passes them, and you can see the threads; if you are in a hurry, use tongs or your finger to remove them, then cauterize at their roots. If the moisture prevents them from being held by the fingers, remove them with flax, or cotton, or a piece of camphor. Then extract them with your fingers, cauterize, and dust over them with some warm powders that are in place of cauterization; or you can cauterize as is said in the chapter on cauterization, and treat them with other remedies until they are healed; if the fundament cannot pass them, apply astringent and bitter ointments to the patient for washing what is within the fundament, so that it may pass openly. When the patient presents, and the threads are passed from the fundament, the treatment is light; this is done by extracting them with your fingers or tongs, then cauterize as we have said until they are healed, and there is no fear of incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you must administer the suturing in this manner: take a twisted thread and put it into a needle, then draw the thread over and make the needle pierce from the other side, turn both ends of the thread under the needle, and leave them loose; tightly form the thread, tie the thread, remove the needle, and do so for all others, leaving one loose to control the excess of blood; then place a wet cloth in oil or cerate on the foundation, put it over the foundation, and command the patient to rest; and let him lie until he mends, and when they are healed, apply ointment and other treatment until he is well.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	dry the foundation or wound steadily
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is a dry cough in the intestine, and by constraint of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you reset at the point of a spatule or under your nail the bark above, which does not leave moist; then cure it until it dries as it should; and if it cannot dry, then renew the scraping more forcefully than before, until it heals much, and be scorched; then cure it until it is healed.
dou fremit	of trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	A formice is a small false appearance on the body, and goes much beyond it. Sometimes one finds coldness, and feels like death by trembling, and comes over the whole body, more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a needle from an ostrich feather, or a very hard vulture feather, and place that needle on the tremor, so that the purple circles completely surround it; then turn your hand with all the needle until you cover the tremor entirely, and put it perfectly, and root out the tremor from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, do this with a needle of silk or iron according to this form, and make it thin beneath and drawing over:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Not piercing it, for you to hold with the two fingers, and press. And if you see, cauterize the tremor, as is described in the preceding chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the shoulder
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Any time the shoulder is dislocated using a silver or copper mold, or one made from melted iron or metal; and at any time these instruments are made, whether small or large, according to those for which they are intended.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those instruments that are used in the treatment of children and who are weak and painful are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the shoulder, whether small or large, is broad, or the stomach is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And let it have an opening or the stomach be tied as you see, and the shoulder be pierced through; and let it have two perforations on one side and one on the other. Let the stomach contain the medicines in a bladder of beast or parchment, and be pierced all around with small openings, with one digit's breadth between each opening. Then insert a strong thread of sinew twisted ten times or several times into these openings, and join it together like a sheep. When the medicine is inside, tie it in front with a strong thread, then reset it; and this is the shape of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine neither be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the cistern with oil or yolk of egg, or something similar, then insert it gently; then the ministers withdraw their hands together until it is all visible, then remove the cistern, and lift the patient's legs to the wall, and if the medicine sees fit to come out, so let it come forth as much as it will; and if he sleeps a whole night, it is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cisternize for a disease of diarrhea and the medicine hastens to come out, then repeat it until he is cured.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are internal or in the foundation, or abscess, then use the cistern as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle cistern on which the skin is constrained.
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken about the treatment of wounds in the division of wound care; now we will discuss hand treatments and medicines according to their effectiveness.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the joints or parts where they are made, and by what means they are caused.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the impact of a stone, and cuts from a sword or knife, or a lance or pole or arrow, or similar things; or they are made according to the joints of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or the head, or the shoulder, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, starting with simple wounds of the head, because their chapter will come later.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or a head injury, and the bone is not broken, then take care if it is from a stone impact or similar things, and the skin is fully torn and the wound is large, and you slightly doubt an abscess hot: so do this immediately with the cephalic sinner itself if little blood comes from the wound, and let the sinew be on the contrary from the damaged part; and avoid the patient's wine overfilling and large meat.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it should not be sinned, let the flesh be diminished, and do not drink wine nor eat meat; and place on the wound, if hot abscesses come, only wet cotton in rose oil, or in styptic wine; and if there is no hot abscess, place on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and has not dried by air or powder, the powder I will say a little later; and if the fire has dried it, place some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like a sword cut and similar, and the edges cannot be brought together by stretching, stitch them together, as I will say for wounds of the belly, regarding stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to bone, penetrable, and holds together only by a little, sew it; then treat the wound with medicine, restoring hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat solid meats, such as heads and cooked wheat, like pulses, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find rotted skin, and it does not reach the bone, sew it completely, apply salve, then treat it. And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, cut without cutting deep, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, then tie the artery with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is light: and it is that you put this powder which binds as though the arsenic had burned them.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live resin three parts, and powder them subtilly, and apply it to the wound, holding it firmly until it burns well and joins with all its blood; then bind it well, and leave it undisturbed unless it swells; for the medicine is not removed until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with resin alone when one lacks incense or the dragon's blood, but allows the arsenic to burn the wound.
