Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the art has changed the wound, even while it was, one does not put this powder there; but apply some digested ointments, or pulses of flour of barley made with water and honey until they exude dew; then cure with other cures until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound and it is small, extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you about the fractures of the head later.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between this and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerves, there is no other way but to leave the treatment alone and put nothing restrictive on them, for it harms the nerves and causes them to wither; and do not apply anything cold to the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation lies with the brain, which is the highest member; but use medicines above, such as boiled wax in sweet water, mixed with rose oil, and boiled cucumbers in sweet water, and other mine stones in this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, stitch and bind it with bandages, then leave it to heal.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and filled with pus, pierce or cut lower in the limb; and if an artery is severed, and bleeding occurs, stop the bleeding, ligate it, and cauterize if necessary; and if the spinal cord of the throat is severed, or the vessels, and the passage through which the flesh flows is guarded, so that the flesh can flow, stitch the vessel above the throat canal, but do not touch the throat itself, placing it according to its natural form; then bind it properly, and let it for a few days, then treat it with drying ointments until it heals; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, set it; and if there are pieces of bone, remove all that you can, and leave what you cannot have to rot, allowing the pus to drain out; and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle it with the powder I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a sinus, the treatment should be as I have said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a spear or knife, and the wound is deep, examine whether from the wound there are any signs that the patient will die: then know that the wound is fatal; and if it is not deep but fresh with all its blood, do not apply powder at the first hour nor leave it uncovered for the blood to stop properly and return to the heart, which would kill the patient; but apply an attractor ointment and change the dressing twice a day; and if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to drain out the moisture, and let the patient rest on the wound for three days, or four, or more; so there will be no spasm, nor male heart tremor from deep pain; and when you see proper healing signs, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat the sores and other treatments until they are healed; and if they cannot be healed, operate, then you know there is a fistula; treat the wound as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple or worse or on the back, treat the one in front; if it is large, stitch it; and if it is small, powder it; and if it is near the bone and has cut pieces, clean the wound, and remove any loose threads; and if they are not loose, let the wound drain to lighten the extraction; and for other wounds on other limbs, make judgments as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	for the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The ruptures of the abdomen are great and medium and small; from a large wound, sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines come out; and the stitching is more difficult, and sometimes a smaller wound proves worse than a larger one, because we cannot easily put the intestines back in place without warmth; for when they feel cold, they swell quickly and are harder to position, and thus a medium-sized wound is better managed, as we must reset the intestines to their proper place. And know that the rupture of the abdomen occurs according to four ways: the two common stitches happen at the abdominal wall seam, and the stitches for other body wounds and the other two specific seams are commonly used with other wounds; yet all the same they are more suitable with the abdominal stitch, and I will say each one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and no intestinal matter is present, and there is nothing to remove, this can be done by one of two methods: either due to the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in a proper manner: moisten a sponge or a cloth with only hot water, or you can boil it in water with cinnamon and cypress and spike, and wash the intestine until the swelling is removed; and after doing this several times with constricting wines, let it be reduced to relieve the swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water or with cooked ale and mead, for by these it is alleviated when a small amount can enter; and if nothing can enter, make a small incision in the wound with the instrument used to treat hemorrhoids; and let the first cure be reduced that it not be cut unless there is great necessity; and this is the tool to make the incision: so cut inside along the curve and do not exceed, and see here the form.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine has slipped out, put it back in place according to its natural form in its proper location, if you have the ability, for this requires movement.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is large, and it is in the area below the abdomen, you should make the patient lie on their back, and raise their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the area above the abdomen, you should raise the head and buttocks higher than the other parts. And if the abdominal rupture is in one of the two areas, you should place the part that is intact higher than the other part; and thus you should administer as I say for both large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, use what is at hand, then have at your disposal the minister of pittous who can reach the entire rupture with his hand, and close the lips; this is the common method of suturing, where you take one needle or more, according to the size of the wound. Leave a space of two finger breadths from the head of the wound, and insert a needle with a good strong thread; pierce both sides of the skin with the needles inside, so that it is pierced from this part, and assemble the three heads of the needles together. Then pass a double thread through the needle from both sides, then bring the two sides of the wound together properly, and leave the space of two finger breadths, and insert another needle; then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and continue doing this according to your need for needles until all the wound is secured. The needles should be medium in size, neither too fine nor too thick, because very fine needles cut through the flesh entirely, and those that are too thick cannot enter well: therefore they should be medium; do not insert the needles too deep into the flesh and skin so that they cut the wound before suturing; then remove the heads of the needles so they do not irritate the patient during sleep, and place small cloths or napkins at the needle heads to keep them in place, leaving them until the wound is healed. This method with needles is more suitable for small wounds, as one needle suffices for a second stitch; this is where you assemble the two sides of the skin and the two sides of the siphac on one needle with a medium strong thread. When you have pierced these heads all four together, retract the needle to the part where you began, in the manner we sew cloth; and place the size of one finger between each stitch. This method is recognized by people, and I sewed a wound from which a man had been cut on his belly, which was more than a palm's length large, and contained intestines twice the length of a palm, and it was located in the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after twenty-four hours, and the wound healed in fifteen days, and I treated it, and he was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the priest had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicines; and placed old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was cured.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two proper methods of suturing: take the needle, and thread it from outside in; when it has pierced through directly opposite, leave the end of the needle or the suture thread on the syphax or where you have threaded the needle, and pierce again from inside out. The understanding of this suture is that you sew as a tanner would sew hides, leaving the syphax on one side and returning to it from another until the suture is completely completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of suturing, as Galen precisely describes, is such that no one does it differently. They join the two parts naturally and apply one end of the needle to the other's edge in this manner: pierce a thread with an end of the needle closely, then pierce only that side, leaving both edges of the tissue; then turn the needle, and pierce from the opposite part inward to those edges of the tissue; then pierce one and the other from the opposite part inward, in two other holes of the needle on the other side. This is the finest method of suturing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this word, and no one testifies against it, that we must stitch the belly with two needles, where there is thread in each; and we must put one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew wounds. And know that when the rupture is within the belly, the stitching is more grievous than on other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, as the surgeon has drawn it, you remove the intestines and the skin; then put on powder for growing flesh, and if the surgeon has drawn it, you put on any ointment that is present until the wound heals; bind the threads, and let the sponges and the lint be sewn; then cure the wound as with others until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, you put on old cotton soon as it begins to exude fluid, and change it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you have no need of other medicine in many situations where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not communicate with the principal members, it is right that you moisten fine linen in tempered warm oil or in rose oil, and put it between the layers, and under the stitches; and if there is pain or putrefaction in boils, which often happens, then use enemas of black tawny wine, especially if the putrefaction comes to the intestines; and puncture within, and know that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called "jeun" cannot heal when it is severed, and this is due to the closeness of the veins there, and the subtlety of the whole body, and its proximity to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the shoulder jumps from the wound, reset it back as with the intestine while it is fresh; and if it is old and turned to brown or black, you must tie the part that is black, to prevent blood flow, for there are veins and arteries there; then cut what is between the ties, and place the two heads down below the part of the wound until above to ease the extraction when the shoulder falls, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the bone
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are intact, and the wound is small, one can restore it in some people, for I saw that a man was wounded or cut by a lance; the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and became fistulous, and there issued from it excretions and flatulence; I treated it as best I could, and did not cease to cauterize until it healed, and the tissues were sutured.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it heal, I doubted that the patient would have pain in his abdomen; and there was no pain at all, but he remained in better condition, eating and drinking. And some surgeons said that when a small wound is on the intestine, it should be tied in such a manner: take thread of large needles, then gather the edges of the wound together, and when the thread has opened the mouth, put it on the two edges so that it clamps its mouth shut; then cover the head, and this remains so that it cannot be untied. Then put another thread after in that manner as before, until the wound is completely filled; and suture the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the chief is seared in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can sew the intestine with a thin thread cut from the intestine of an animal in this manner: take the head of this intestinal thread that be most unshrunk, and then tie at the head of this intestinal thread a fine linen thread twisted, then put the thread into the needle, and suture the intestine, and tighten at the wound; and this method of suturing for a tremor is not removed except according to the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the larger intestines, there is nothing that can be done but with subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	Of the fistula or if it be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it has formed, is universally called "fistula", and especially when it is closed and round.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the true nodation hard and white, where one does not feel pain, and it is also closed like the feathers of an eye; sometimes clear round, and at other times thick; sometimes small, and at other times large; and I have spoken of this in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed and has no flesh, can only come forth through one of the nine causes: namely, by the smallness of the blood or flesh; or by its malice; or because there is hard flesh within, and above the edges, which does not allow flesh to grow; or there is too much pus; or the bones are rotted, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the treatment; or because the corruption is like a pestilence; or due to the property in the region where digestion is delayed, and health is slow, and naturally swollen; or there are veins or bone: and I have already shown all these causes, and their signs, and treatments with medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or it must be that I teach you the treatment of an abscess caused by manual intervention.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that an abscess can occur in all parts of the body; for there are abscesses that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or in the throat, or intestines, or bladder, or some of the ribs, or the spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet; and so they affect the principal part of the limb, and similar ones.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all abscesses of this nature are serious for health, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance; and if there is any abscess that does not come from the source I have said, and you have confidence in its treatment, and you can recognize it, take a tent of iron or brass, if the abscess is straight, then probe it; and if the abscess is curved, use a fine linen tent for probing, because the linen bends around the curve. And if the abscess has openings and you cannot thoroughly probe it with tents, inject medicine through one of the openings, for moisture persists between the openings and cleanses them; then probe carefully as much as you can, so that you may know if there is bone or nerve, and whether it is completely closed, and ask the patient to feel the pain when pressed by your hand, and locate where he feels it; and when you truly know its location, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or any of the places I have said, then treat it according to what I have said, and remove the false tissue and decayed flesh inside; and then continue the treatment until it is healed. If the abscess is deeply seated in its proper place, you must thoroughly copulate it as much as possible, then insert moistened tents into medicated water, and let them extend to the head of the abscess, so that the medicine may corrode the remaining excess at the bottom; and then apply healing ointments until it is fully healed; and if it is not fully healed by this means, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the abscess, treat it accordingly.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerve is not injured or a principal limb, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then let the king remain until all the corruption is removed, then cure the flesh around it until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and you return to bowing, know that you have not gone far enough: so uncover and rest until you are at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If this is not the case, know that the corruption is too deep to be remedied; then there is no other means but to let nature take its course; and if there is a small corrupted bone that you can extract with tongs, do so with an appropriate instrument; and if there are many bones, extract them all, leaving none behind; and if moisture prevents this and there is no error or fear, cut the flesh, moisture, and muscle, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, apply something fomenting to the wound and let it remain until the flesh is rotten around the bones, then the bones will be less painful; and if it is a large bone, such as in the leg or thigh, reset only the corruption until all the blackness is removed, then close the wound; and if there is much of the corrupted part, coming to the marrow of the bone; you must excise and cauterize all up to the corruption, and then cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you about a fistula that occurred in a man's leg, so that you may take example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man around XXX years of age, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came within the body, until the matter reached the leg and it swelled with a large abscess. There was no apparent reason to open it; but they pierced it out of their folly, causing much discharge, and it became a fistula. A great deal of pus continually flowed from the body; and for two years many healers tried to cure it, but there was no wise man in the art of hands until I was called. I saw his leg and the medicines used to treat him, and what flowed through the openings caused much corruption. The body of the young man became red, with a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these openings, and then searched all the openings, and found that one went against the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hastened then, and cut into one of the openings enough to discover a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and perforated, with corruption extending to the inner bone; I saw what appeared from the corrupted bone, and thought there was no other corruption beyond what I removed; but I continued to treat the wound with medicines for a long time, and it could not heal; then I began again, and exposed the bone as before, and found the corruption continuous in the bone, and treated it, and removed it, and labored to mend the place; but I could not do so until I cut into about a palm's breadth of the bone, which was entirely hollowed out, then I treated it; and it healed quickly and was securely mended, and there was no need to resume the work except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and for my fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the bleeding often occurred, but it was completely healed, and in the place of the bone grew a hard tissue, and it was well formed and had no harm or adverse effect at all, neither externally nor internally.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated in this manner: take a thread, and draw it taut at the end of the bone that is exposed, and command someone to stretch it upwards; then put another larger linen thread over the hard tissue next to the bone, and tie it securely so that you pull the corrupt flesh away from the bone, and expose the area where you wish to operate without harming the flesh; place a hot coal or a board under the bone to help heal the corrupt flesh; and continue to treat until you can see and feel the corruption, and do so again if necessary.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or part thereof, uncover the flesh completely; then place a coal beneath, and thereafter let the soot run from one side to the other of the corruption, and let the soot be as long as the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, cut the corrupted joint, and sew the bone on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no old custom but to copper them; and if the corruption is by a knife of the hand or by a knife of the foot, this thing is very strong, but nevertheless it must be that you inquire about that corruption, how it appears; and cleanse it in all ways that you can, but let neither vein nor nerve hinder you; and know that the incisor and sinews for coppering these bones are many, according to the arrangement of the bones and the appearance of the bone, and their size and subtlety, and their grandeur and smallness, and their hardness; and for this it must be prepared an instrument suitable to each workpiece; and know that the work will show you the instrument you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases; so think about the instrument you need according to what is fitting.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The shoulder dislocates either from within or from without; and when you have medicated the corrosion by treating the wound with medicines, and it does not heal, then you must operate on that member until you reach the place where the corrosion comes from, so that the patient escapes death, or greater harm from the lack of the limb; and the signs are that the member becomes black, seeming to be burned by fire, and after the blackness, the corruption spreads from one member to another, taking hold throughout the body; so hasten the operation, and if it is due to the sting of certain venomous beasts, such as sea scorpion and snake and similar, and the corrosion is at the head of the arm, then treat, and do not give it time to spread to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes as far as the hand, clamp at the joint, so that the corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it comes to the arm, clamp with the knife; and if it passes the knife, it is death, and there is no remedy except for the quantity of its virtue; and thus do when the corrosion comes or pierces: if it comes to the first joint, clamp after the other joint; and if it pierces or wounds, clamp all the wound; and if it ascends into the leg, clamp at the joint near the knee; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other means than to let the patient die; and the way of clamping or sewing the limb is that you tie over and under, extend some ministers below, and some others above, and you separate the flesh which is between the two ties as wide as one spatumile, until the bone is uncovered; then clamp or sew, and place a linen cloth on each side, so that the sinew does not touch the healthy part, and cause another lesion and abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs when you work, cauterize the limb quickly, or apply some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed, and bind the injured limb with an appropriate bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in our village: he had a black spot that seemed like a burn from fire, and this corrosion first appeared on his big toe of his foot, spreading to cover the entire toe; when the man saw the corrosion, he hurried to cut off his foot, and he was healed. Shortly after, the corrosion or lesion appeared again on his hand, and he came to me, and I placed reflective things after cleansing his body, but the corrosion did not cease; he requested that I amputate his hand, and I did not do so because I had hope of reflecting the matter; I also doubted whether if I cut off his hand, he would die, since the man's virtue was weak. He became desperate and returned to his land, hurriedly cutting off his hand himself, and was healed; I only relate this story for others to use if needed.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess forms in the flesh, and stays so long that it creates a large accumulation of pus; then it ruptures and drains, and the pus jumps out, leaving the fat like vessels; the skin above is as delicate as untangled thread, and does not run all the way to the bone or to the nerve, and such illness is called "sain," and is not called "fistula"; but if it extends so long that it reaches the bone by perforation, it is called "fistula"; and the skin is such that you peel away the entire layer of skin, especially when it is delicate, like thread; and does not burst due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you suspect that the skin will ulcerate and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, cure it by enema as follows: observe whether the swelling is large, and the pus within has a foul odor; then prepare an Egyptian medicinal enema in this manner: take aloe, oil, and litharge, equally, and cook them in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey; then use as much of it as needed, mix with water and honey, and apply the enema to the swelling, pressing on the puncture. Let the medicine remain for two hours, then drain it off carefully; do this repeatedly until the swelling is resolved and the pus removed; if such medicine is not available, you can use ash water instead: take vine wood ashes, pour water over them, settle, and apply as an enema. Do this until you are certain that the swelling has been well cleansed; then use an enema to create flesh in it, for which you should prepare a diaphoretic paste with rose oil and wine; or use various medicines and ointments, of whose properties I have already spoken when treating ointments; if the opening in the breast is small and cannot be reached by the enema tube, enlarge it slightly with iron, then place a tent of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment over it until it is enlarged enough; if the wound is too large, cover only the area where the enema can enter, and if the opening through which pus drains is above, you should peel back more skin below.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bow is perfect, do not let it drain flesh; and if you cannot stop the bleeding under it as you see fit, arrange it in such a way that the bow runs to the lowest place where it is. For when the bow is perfect, do not let it drain flesh and if you cannot stop the bleeding under it as you see fit, arrange it in such a manner: that the bow runs gently downward, leaving nothing of the bow; and take consolidative medicines to put over the sound, and keep them on an linen drape that covers all the sound; then apply strength toward the hole in the breast slightly larger than the first, for let ointment souef be applied under the other drape according to the size of the hole, and place it over the hole in the flesh to lessen the bow, and do not remove the large drape outside until after many days once; and that which is underneath the hole in the breast, often remove to drain the bow, and know what comes from the bow, whether it be venom or little or enough, or digested, or undigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or numbness, and whether there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in such a manner and you see the nature that sautes on the hole in the flesh, know that the breasts are already averted, and approach health; and then release it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you release the wound, change the other drape, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast expels undigested food after many days, know that the breast is not healed.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons cut after long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	And if there are people whose wounds heal slowly despite proper care, and those who do the opposite; and if undigested food starts to come from the breast after many days, know that the breast is not healed; and if the breast heals slowly and is far away, apply drying medicines with both substance and virtue, such as a diaphoretic ointment, for there is a great part of vitriol in it, and this is the last medicine; use diaphoretic ointment, prepared with rose oil, and mix it with equal parts old wine by volume; then apply it after allowing it to infuse; if diaphoretic ointments are not present, you may take myrrh, aloes, and frankincense, grind them together in honey when they are on fire, and wrap them in cloth and place them over the breast, administering them frequently by a physician as needed, along with celestial lily roots, which are like wheat flour and centory; use simple or compound remedies: grind them, make into powder, and mix with the honey I mentioned, then apply; if the cure is prolonged and not cured by this method, know that the corruption has fully affected the bone, or hard members, or ligaments; thus, treat the fistula as we have said earlier.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Pannicula is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the finger, or of the foot, or by chance in other toes; and when it grows old and no attention is paid to it, it comes to a head, swells, and discharges pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and sometimes carries it away entirely; and brings about corrosion down to the bone, causing such intense pain that the joint of the finger becomes wide and the color fades.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, then you must cut away all the remaining nail, and then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauteries are much great help if the bone is sound and the nail is sound; and if the nail presses on the flesh and begins to prick it, and the blisters, then you must put a piece of lead under the nail so that it does not touch the flesh, and lifts up, and cuts this subtle flesh gently and lightly, and places over the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove all; then the wound heals with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut and pull firmly, for as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal; and if you see the bone decayed, cut it out as described before, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is pierced and swollen, and it feels great pain, then you must first heal it; then cut the nail with a sharp spatule by cutting across, and watch that the cuts do not come to the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, place something on it that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain comes from the deafness of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	the dislocation that arises in some men by accident is either all flesh or has bones, and sometimes an angle, and none of them arise at the root of the joint, or the birth is in any of our bones.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	That which arises in any bone of the shoulder does not move, and that which arises at the shoulder joint may move by accident; the size of that which is fleshly is light, almost like this: cut it at its root with a broad blade.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	That which arises at the root of the joint is grievous to treat: if you hold it with copper.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In that which is born or must be done last, it is necessary that you scrape the flesh roundly until reaching the bone, then cut the bone with an appropriate tool, and then clean it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The symptoms that come together in these injuries arise either by birth, or suddenly from a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is necessary that you scrape this scab, so that it heals according to its natural form; then place between two moist cloths or woolen drapes in rose oil, preventing them from sticking together; or you can place between two thin pieces of cloth, until the wounds are properly sewn.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If the scab comes with either of these two with the palm, scrape this scab as is fitting.
des vils	of the wicked
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	When his veins are swollen enveloped with excessive melancholic humours, coming from many parts of the body; and more occurs in legs of those who walk and work and carry burdens than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must administer to him once purgation of bile, and then cure him with the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The iron cure is according to two methods: one is where they cauterize and cut or burn the black blood; and the other method is that you incise the vein and let all the blood flow out completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The incision is performed in this manner: first, heat the leg with hot water greatly until the large veins become thin. Then, stretch the patient's leg from below the knee to just above the knee; next, make a cut in the vein at one place or two or three, using a wide incision. Hold and let all the black blood flow out by hand from one end to the other, as much as the virtues of the patient can bear. Then close it up, and instruct the patient to dye their skin with meat juice containing black bile; and repeat the evacuation and cure when the veins are full, and benefit the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The extractments are done in this manner: hold the limb of the patient, if there is much hair, then put it into a bath, and lift the limb with warm water until it turns red and the veins swell; and if you have no bath, heat it over fire, and apply it along the vein from the bottom of the knee to the part below the ankle; then cut the skin inch by inch, and cauterize each side of the vein until it appears when one feels it; and it will appear red and black, and when it enters or touches the skin it seems like a white cord; then insert a rag under it until it rises from the skin, and then pull it with one finger, then apply another in a higher place over three fingers; then cauterize the skin above the vein until it appears, then lift it off the rag as you did before, and pull it to a second finger, so as you did first; then cut another size or several if you need them, then lift it, and cut at the sole of the foot, then draw and lift until the second size; then extract from size to size until it is all free, then cauterize; and if you cannot pull and lift it, insert a needle with a strong double thread under it, and tie and draw it, and put one rag over it, and turn your hand on both sides until it comes out; and beware that it does not stick, for if it sticks, you cannot pull or lift it, and it is harmful to the patient; and when you have done all this, put moistened wool soaked in wine and rose oil under the place of the wound, and cure until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight as we have said, then you must cut it crookedly, but do not cut it completely; and draw it out as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of iron with which one cuts the vein is curved, and does not cut completely, so as not to cut the vein; and it is of substantial curvature, for if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but it should be thick as we have said, and this is its form:
de la voinne civile	of the common vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is embedded in the legs, in warm parts where no herbs nor trees grow, and in earth where there is no moisture; and by chance it may arise elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens from rot that comes from beneath the skin, as serpents and worms arise within the body, entwined between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that a very great inflammation comes in the leg, then the toes change color, and the veins begin to protrude, as if they were the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the shoulder is opened, it must be wrapped with a piece of flannel about one and a half to two inches wide, and the bandage, and let the flannel remain on the leg. Every time there is no pressure from above, wrap around the flannel and the bandage; if it is too long, cut off a part and wrap the remainder, but do not cut it at its root until it is fully out; for if you cut it, it will enter the flesh, causing an abscess, putrefaction, or other illness. For this reason, it should be treated little by little until it is completely out, leaving nothing or a core behind. Sometimes this vein, when treated from five inches to ten and even more than twenty inches long, comes to me, from which it protrudes ten inches long. When you cut it, push one or two fingers through it and pierce it thoroughly so that all of it comes out; then drain the matter inside, and apply topical medicines to prevent putrefaction for a few days, and then treat it as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes there are small wounds, and especially when they appear in the joint of the foot or hand, and there is much damage, and from which small pieces fly out; treat them as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	vers that arise between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "cattle disease," because it often befalls cattle, and it is a small worm that arises between skin and flesh, and goes up and down throughout the body, feeling well as it travels from limb to limb, until it eats through the skin where it goes and comes out; and it is nourished by putrefaction of certain humors, such as come from serpents and worms and ascarids or intestines; and doubt arises about its malignity, for when it goes throughout the body, and it climbs to the head, and it comes to the eye, by chance enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being treated and drained, one cannot force it when it goes: therefore, you must tie the area above and below with a tight bandage, then cut it out and drain it. If the blood is thoroughly expelled from the flesh, and you do not find any, cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greater harm it does is that it can damage the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming or close to the eye, tightly bind beneath it, then cut it out. The patient must be cleansed of bodily humors using soluble medicines for putrid bad humors, and beware of meats causing putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from wind
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes into some members, and then moves from member to member; and I have seen those whom I say this of.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was summoned to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and just after that, I saw it rise as if a worm on the shoulder, faster than anything, like live silver when it is cut from one piece to another; the pain left that place and lodged in the shoulder, and then shortly after spread throughout the body until it came to the other arm; she told me that it returned repeatedly within her body, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed how it moved from member to member in such a manner, for I had never seen this disease spread in this way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Firstly, I willed well that they would wish to move pain from one place to another, but I did not will it as much as I saw in the woman; and I thought that this was because the woman had a hard core, and veins uncovered, and because these winds constrained were apparent; and they do not appear according to this reason to those who have delicate cores and closed-up veins.
