Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see this disease treated, and the patient feels this pain, if it reveals itself as we have said, clean the surface and underneath rapidly, and then stop once these constrained winds have left their place; and cauterize the area; and if you do not see it with your eyes, treat it with what expels winds, such as bitter pills, spider pills, and other similar ones.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows come in various types, according to their shapes and the parts of the body where they lodge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of their forms is that some have large points, and small ones, and barbed, and soldered; and some have two angles, and those with tongues, and some with pieces. And the one that falls into any limb does so in various ways: or it pierces a principal limb, such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls into any part of these limbs, and the signs of death, which I will tell you later, appear: then you must beware of extracting this arrow, for death comes after in many conditions; and when none of these bad signs appear, and the arrow is not completely removed, extract it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow strikes and pierces the bone, and the sinus fluid which is above the brain bursts, is when there is scotomia and sodness and vertigo and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps it comes from the nostrils or the ears; and perhaps it affects speech and voice; and the wound oozes moist white fluid resembling a pulse, and it oozes also as if boiled flesh; and if this sign appears, keep to the treatment, and extract the arrow if it is present.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the arrow when it strikes or the heart is that it is near the left nipple, and feels as if it were embedded in something hard, not empty; and perhaps the arrow moves like a pulse, and draws black blood, and brings coldness and cold sweat, and fainting: then know without doubt that death ensues.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that Nerve Lomour did not remove is that without any bubbling of foam it jumps from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs loudly and retains the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls into the covering of the foot, it affects the small ribs; it causes great pain and sighing; and all the limbs from the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls onto the stomach, by chance it jumps from the wound with some undigested meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls onto the abdomen, and in its jump, no hay from the intestine route, so there is no hope in the treatment, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine spurts out and flows, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, such as the arm and the neck and the throat and the shoulder and the scapula and the spine of the back and the femur and the legs, and limbs similar to these, are safe according to many disposals.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or the artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because you would do otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow fell or pierced at the root of the nose: I tried it, and extracted it from the other side beneath the ear fat, and he was cured without any difficulty.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And draw out an arrow that fell into the grease of the eye under the paper, and the arrow was lodged, and could not be reached with the tip toward the wood, and the arrow was as large as a Turkish bow, light as iron without ears; the patient recovered, and no bad accidents came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And drew out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears: I pierced the barbs, and drew it out carefully, and the Christian recovered.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And drew out an arrow from the man, which had pierced his side or stomach, and I thought he was dying; and after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change at all. I cut into the arrow, treated it, and drew it out, and he had no bad accidents.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you wish for a man who has an arrow that fell or hit him, and the wound was sewn up; and the arrow remained inside, and did not change its natural positions, nor caused harm in any of its natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And if you wish for another man, who had an arrow in his face, and the wound was sewn up; and remained thus suffering great pain; and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And treat an arrow that fell upon a man of the king's princes, which it struck among the nails, and was slightly inclined to the right side; and the arrow was entirely pierced. I was called for the treatment after it fell three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I took all the subtlety of it, and did not feel it at all; and he felt pricking and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the point of the arrow. I placed on his eye the poultice of atrative and digestive herbs, because the eyes were swollen; and it appeared that the arrow's head was still in his eye.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the poultice for several days, and redressed the wound again. The patient remained in this state for a long time, until he felt the arrow's head one day in his nose; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied corrosive medicine to the wound with my hands for several days until it was open. I tested it and felt the head of the arrow corroding at the site; then I placed the corrosive medicine in the opening of the wound, until the head of the arrow became visible; and it passed well through the tissues for more than four months, after which I cleared the wound so that I could use pliers to extract it from both sides, but it would not come out. Then I continued to refine and devise methods with tools until I successfully extracted it on one day using properly made pliers, as its form will be shown in the end of this chapter; and I restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the surgeon judges that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I will restore it, and the wound was sewn, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or have I told you about the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you place your cure on what I do not say, for books cannot take in everything; but master surgeons compare on very little things, and on what is present and lacking, find nine operations, and nine instruments, for the removal of foreign objects that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows are in members where they are fixed in two ways: either by the place where they enter, or by another part; and that which enters through the place where it enters is an arrow entering into the flesh, and is never found again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not burst now, let it be left until the flesh rots through, and the issue becomes clear; and also if it is embedded in the bone and cannot come out, let it be left for several days, and change it each day; then it will burst, and if it does not burst, pierce through entirely with a sharp instrument, so that the flesh inside is widened, and then draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is embedded in the bone of the head and goes as far as one of the brain's ventricles, or any of the other accidents I have said to the patient: do not treat it at all, but let it be until it becomes equal after a few days, for if the arrow reaches the septum pellucidum, it is fatal.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not pierced deeply only into the bone, and does not come close to the sinew, and the patient remains without any bad accidents for several days, then the means of drawing it out should be used.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is not pierced deeply enough and cannot be pulled out forcefully, then I administer thorns between, as I have told you; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is embedded in the flesh of the body and cannot be seen, then seek it thoroughly with your hand; and if you feel it, draw it out with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is neither bone nor nerve nor vein, then enlarge the wound until it is large enough; and draw the arrow if you can, and if it has ears that it holds to, remove the flesh that is embedded from both sides toward the part you can reach, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow as much as you can so you can draw it out; and with great care, do not break the arrow, as you would draw it more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, let it remain until the flesh between the bones is rotten, then remove it, for the extraction would be painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the drainage of blood makes it contrary, administer what we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and beware of incising the nerve or the vein, and find a way to extract the arrow as you can, whether soon or late, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow fell upon him, for this is the greatest aid that it be, and if you cannot, then place him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, or where it pierces anything, or where the skin is swollen so one can see or feel it: cut there, as much as the forceps can grasp, and then extract it: if it be now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand roundly until it enters the bone, and enlarge the bone, then pull it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it for now, and then restart the extraction until it comes out; and if the shaft of the arrow is still in, push the entire shaft; and if the shaft falls out, when you need to administer a thrust, use the tool with a point, so that the point of the arrow enters the hole of the tool; and then push forcefully, and if the arrow is stuck, push the tool with the point entering it, to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is touched, it is necessary that you cut out all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as required.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls or pierces in the abdomen or bladder or side, and it is nearby, you may attempt to remove it; but be careful not to open the vein or nerve, then extract it, and afterwards suture the wound if needed; and treat the wound until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tweezers used for removing arrows is similar to the beak of a bird, and here is the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in many sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the needle used for piercing is also similar to the feather of a bird, to push at the tip of the arrow, as shown in the form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of the tongs for pressing and for knowing this is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of veins of the body common
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	Of the veins from which one is cleansed there are thirty-one, of which sixteen are principal, namely: two jugulars which are behind the ears and called the "herbech" veins; and the two arteries which are in the temples and apparent; and the veins that are in the corners of the eyes, called "aspirate" veins; and the vein that is in the forehead; and the vein that is on the nose; and the two subclavian veins which are under the collarbone; and the two veins that are in the upper lips above the mouth, and these are the veins called "augeherich" veins; and the veins that are beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins from which we commonly draw blood are V in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it lies on the left side, and they call it "vein of the head"; and the median is called "faste", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and they call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic lies on the right side, and they call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the fossele, and it is this one from which we draw blood, which clearly appears above the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvatelle is the vein that lies between the auricular and annular, and it has two roots; in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is below the arch of the left pocket, and the second sophene which is on the right side at the ankle; and the vein called "nese" which is on the other side of the ankle; and in the other leg there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The healing of veins that are behind the ears helps with old catarrhs and headaches; and the qualities of the healer, as I tell you, and it is that you reset the patient's head, and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then bind the patient's neck to a screw so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two loops dependent on the head: hold them with your thumb, and where you feel the pulse under your thumb, prick; then take the lancet, and let it pass beneath the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand all along the vein upward, cut and remove the skin and the vein thoroughly twice through, and let the blood flow until you see; then drain it and bind it so that it heals; and I have already said the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The health of the two arteries that are in the two temples, is equivalent to ancient migraine, stiff, and customary blindness, and in the body of watery tears on their eyes; and the qualities of this health are as I say: and it is that the patient draws his neck, so that the two veins clearly appear; and feels the pulse beneath your thumb, and then sighs deeply; then lift the heart over the vein upwards to your index finger, and place the lancet underneath, and lift the vein upwards, and the cloth, as you have done with the other veins, and draw off the blood according to your necessity; then release the patient, and put your thumb on the vein for an hour, then put on cotton; and then form it well, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken about their tying and extraction, or the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The sinew of the vein on the forehead is worth as much as the cephalic sinew for diseases of the face, and for headache, and for redness; and its quality is that the patient's neck twists until the vein becomes visible; then take the instrument called "fosseur," whose form is described here:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and pierce through with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity you see; then release the patient's neck, and bind the vein until it is sound and never work with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	In all ways, it is not fitting that the flames be too hot; and let the sinew lie across, for the bone is close, and by chance the flames might break when they are fine.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The health of the two veins that are in the eyelids helps with the eyes, and for hiccups, and for redness, and for the white part in the eye, and for diseases of the face; and the quality of their health is such that the patient draws his color by twisting from any joint, as before; then the savior, and let the saving be through the traverse, a bit long like a flame a bit wide, because there is no point of flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, by chance they break; then make the blood run as much as you need, and then tie with cotton, and tie well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The health of the vein near the nose is good for water and hard scrofulous disease, and for diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, especially when it is old; and the quality of its health is such that the patient draws his color by twisting from any joint, then twists his nose with your left hand, and take a subtle long flame, and stick it between the lip in the space which is between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well herein, and the wound will start to run now; do not go too much beyond perfection, and make the blood run as you need, then tie it for a night, because it is most easily restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The sinew of the two girdles helps in the narrowing of the alainne, and in the beginning of mingling, and much to diseases, and to petechiae, and to corrosion, and to herpes, and estiomenes; and the quality of the sinew is that the patient draws his col out from under both, as we have said; and let the master be on the head of the patient, and the patient lie down on the seat, then cleanse the vein from long a little bit widely, then draw temperately the blood or as much as needed; then do another thing in the other vein, then untie the ligature, and tightly press all the veins moderately, that the patient does not strangle; and leave until morning, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the health of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the veins of the lips helps in swelling in the mouth, and to corruption of gums, and cracks in the lips, and at birth and afterwards.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of the health cause the patient to sit before you, and hold his neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left. One can be known by their black color, and by the small black veins around them: cut both of these, and if you do not know them and are in doubt, cut the largest from each side, and do the same for the two veins above and below, for they are of the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the health beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The health of the veins that are beneath the tongue aids after the health of the cephalic vein, and this is in the constriction of the throat, and for diseases of the uvea, and for mouth diseases; and the quality of the sinner is such that the patient's condition improves before your eyes in the sun, and it lightens the tongue, and you look beneath on each side a black vein: therefore both are healthy, and do not go too much into perfection, for beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the costumarily treated vein are healed in two ways: either by pricking with a large mirtin flame or with a subtle olive oil as you hear sharp, which is called "anesil"; and they are large and subtle according to the size and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the martyr's flame is very renowned, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it has need to open veins filled with thick blood visible on the surface, and which contain much thick blood; and this is the form of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more pointed subtle, and is for opening subtle veins, where there is thin yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The basilica's treatment, which is one of these veins, helps diseases that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the side, and in the belly; and it is suitable for the sinner to bleed and to avoid the artery beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if the artery is cut and bleeding occurs, it must be staunched as I have said; and the fire should not be pricked but cut like flax.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilique vein does not open clearly, it must be extracted and replaced with another; or you take any rib of it, or you incise in lieu of it the vein inserted in the arm: it opens clearly; and the cut is made with flax, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to know the place of the incision, it must be thus that you extract the arm, and touch the place until you feel the pulse; then mark the place with a needle, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein with flax. Be sure that you do not wound the artery when you see the place swollen, for this is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it bulge up high as urine in a child, and the skin is red and fine, know that it is blood from an artery: hasten then, and place your finger longwise, then withdraw your finger when the bleeding stops, for this often happens; bind up the arm, and leave it thus, and do not move the patient until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the skin is not yet stopped and it pains you, and medical help is not present, cut the artery if it appears, for the head of the retractor will stop it.止血。
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a bark from the fisticle tree, split it open, and use one half well bound until the other day; if the skin stops bleeding, that is good. If not, treat the wound as we have said, using powders to stop blood. The dressings are not greatly affected by many preparations for the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein in the middle helps treat blood from the head above, and from the body beneath, for it is composed of the basilica and cephalique, as we have said; and it is necessary for the healthy one to guard against the nerve underneath, and if it points too much towards perfection, and he finds the nerve, and it swells, and the health be spoiled, and by chance cannot heal; and this nerve often appears, and if it does not appear in any man through its subtlety, it is necessary that you anesthetize the vein with the instrument; and avoid the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, cut along its length.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The cephalique vein helps, as it treats blood from the head and aids the eyes; and it is necessary to anesthetize it by pricking with olive oil flame or myrtle oil, for this is the safest of all veins, because it does not have any nerve or artery beneath.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	In every way, it is necessary to seek the lightest touch, and not grievously wound if it must be done for the first time, and one restarts; and by chance, the limbs swell in some people when it must be done for the first time, but it does not grievously wound.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the skin is according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about surgery is that surgery should only be performed to maintain health and to avoid future illnesses; and surgery should be conducted in one of the three veins: namely, cephalic, facial, and basilic; and surgery should be done at the beginning of prayers on knees, and in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear; and it should be performed on the first or third day after two or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The medicine given for diseases has no fixed hour determined, but when need is of day or night, at all hours and in every time; and it is not fitting to medicate children up to fourteen years, nor women bearing strength only from the fourth month up to seven.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Old people who have passed sixty years should not be medicated.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when any wish to be medicated, in whatever manner it may be, it is fitting that they purge the intestines with a light enema, if there is not much fecal matter retained, so that the veins do not attract from the intestines the putrefied superfluities harmful to the principal limbs; nor should one medicate those who are too salted by meat, nor those who are drunk, whether they be strong or weak, nor those who are dropsical; and if one wishes to medicate after a colic attack, vomiting, and evacuation of the stomach, and multiplication of abode in women, and travail, and watching, and fasting, and those whose entire virtue is diminished by force of weapon or body; then for subtlety of humors, if the sans is gross, from meat and drink and medicine, if you have such power; then between or after bath, if anything does not prohibit, to subtilize the blood, and medicate through the vein in the foot between the third and fourth, as we have said; and on that day avoid work, and labor, and lust, and similar things; and be tied and joyous, and let the one who medicates be higher than the one being medicated, and rub the arm two or three times, then extract the leech moderately, for when it is too tight or loose, it cannot adhere properly; and then rub the limb with your hands until the veins swell, and you can feel them; then anoint the fingers of the left hand with a little old oil, then place his thumb under the vein just above the limb where he wishes to medicate, so that the vein does not break from the pressure.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flow as strings to the surgeon, and some that are full of windiness, such that when one puts fire on them, they retreat from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus one is of those; and if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, for which reason the surgeons must be cautious in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, that is good; but if not, one must attempt it again a little below that place or quickly above, if the limb is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the limb is swollen, and the patient feels pain, let it rest for one or two days and do not bind the arm: perhaps abscesses will form; do not enter a bath, but continue with the surgery if it pleases you. And if the opening is small, or the vein is thin and subtle, and you doubt that there is not as much blood as you see, then apply the flame directly to that opening; work quickly, as the limb becomes swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the limb swollen, do not resume the healing, and place a bit of lard on it, for it lightens the body from blood, and makes the lard that is there in the swelling thin; thus administer lard in each healing where you heal the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and the same is done with honey and wax when placed on the limb; so subtlely does the blood separate when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes an abscess large, which happens often, even when it is not healed more than that time or the opening of the vein is small, hasten, and place on the limb a wet sponge in water and salt a bit warm, and hold for an hour; and you must do this after the bleeding from the vein has stopped. And if after some days there remains any black or green on the limb, it does not hurt it; and if you see, place on it any substance of aloes or myrrh set in calamus juice, must, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often an abscess and appearance arise in the skin of the basilica: therefore place your hand there, and if you find the area soft under the pressure of the hand, that is the bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not apply anything of what we have said, for by chance it could cut into an artery; but make it a dry poultice to harden the area, and then treat with other remedies until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw from each of the humors according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is fitting for him who is full and strong, and has need of blood extraction, to make a larger wound, and let the flammes be wide; and for him who is weak, do the opposite, and he should be healed little but often, and one should heal in cutting across, not by pricking; and this manner of healing saves from running of blood and nerve compression, and is better than long or wide wounds.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for him whose body needs nourishment after the healing, it is fitting to give soft bread with pomegranate juice; if he is heated, draw blood three or four times. And if he has a cold complexion, eat soft bread before healing in mûre syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it swells at the joint, after the discharge of much blood, it is fitting that he inhales broth of flesh and fragrant subtle syrup, and use the other things we have said in the division or chapter of syncope for the evacuation of vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if it swells in the arm and was swollen before, it is fitting, when he is weakened by great swelling, that he be swelled a little and a little, according to the quantity of its virtue continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever swells in the arm after the first swelling, and has strong cor, should be swollen seven hours after the first swelling, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever is swollen in another part, should be swelled the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	Because there is much blood within the body which is already heated, and this causes fever; therefore it is necessary to drain a great quantity, and enlarge the puncture until it becomes inflamed around the wound; after you have restored all conditions of health, and place your hand on your pulse when it heals, so that death does not come from under the heart, and this happens many times, when the surgeons are negligent; and it is not fitting when you see release the arm, and make blood flow a second time, and the puncture is closed, that you press firmly upon it; nor if it is crooked, that you stretch the arm hastily, for that would be ill; but let it be until it heals the second time; or you may prick at the tip of the flame, until the one who has been frozen to the point of the vein breaks free, and place a little salt in water, and press lightly upon it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not compress it until the abscess is pacified.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if the need arises to treat the blood a second time, let it be done in that same vein, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is treated in place of the vein in the hand because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the method of treatment is that the patient puts his hand in warm water until the fingers turn red; then tie it moderately so that the vein appears well. Now suture it from the side, not from the length or the width; and make the punctures wide, and suture them close to the joint of the hand. If no blood can come out, put the hand back in warm water and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough; if it is in winter, do not repeatedly put the hand in warm water, for it should be used more in summer than in winter. The suturing of this vein is safer than any other veins, whether artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The health of the right hand's salvation is good for all liver diseases, and this is the manner: stretch the hand, and pour in warm water until the veins are swollen; if it is crooked, and you cover it completely, do not harm anything; and do not go too long, for the nerves are beneath all skin, and then put the hand in warm water again, if the hand is frozen in the wound, and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have let out enough blood as needed, put a piece of oil-soaked cloth to seal it quickly, and do this for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The health of the hand in the left hand is good for the disease of the lungs, and do everything as I have told you for the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sickness of the spleen is useful for all diseases that are below the body, such as diseases of the liver, retention of flowers, and disease of the reins, and of the thighs and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of its virtue are that the diseases cause pain in hot water, and one should rub on the vein until it hurts, and tie above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot go much of the reins; therefore make it healthy where there is a larger vein or at the ankle, which moves well.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you make it healthy on the foot, beware of the nerves beneath, and make it healthy by cutting through them as when sawing; let the flambes be ash.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the stone cannot pass out, place the foot in the water, and let it well drain the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the stone is needed for the first time, start again the second time above a little, because the loins are salted; nor doubt the nerve, as we have said, and so do with the sponge of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The loins of the sciatic vein are at the ankle, and its stone is worth for the pain in the hip when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its stone is such that the patient enters the bath, and expels four doles above the ankle by twisting, for otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, you can stone it in all ways that you can, and by crossing; and it is best to twist it, because the loins are soft, and it responds well to manual manipulation.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, trace any vein from the shin or back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves; and let the bleeding continue as much as you see, then release the bandage, and place a cloth and bind it; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of the suction cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suction cups are made of horns, or leather, or glass; and suction is performed in two ways: either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this suction that is performed without pricking is done in two ways: either with fire or without fire; and the suction that is performed by pricking and drawing blood is done at fourteen places on the body, of which one is all around the head; another is inserted into the neck; two are on both sides of the neck; one is under the chin; one is on both shoulders; one is above the armpits; one is on each arm; one is on each leg; one is on each ankle; and fire suction does not treat blood, but only the small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason it does not weaken at all, as we do with a vein from a cut; and it should not be administered either with fire or without fire in any disease caused by excess, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if for necessity of sickness it is fitting to bleed, or for custom, we shall conduct it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and between times; for there are such as, when they have need to bleed, have heavy heads; and there are such as find fullness and redness in their face, and on their head, and neck, and darkness before their eyes; and such as find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongues, and draw blood.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially between hours of the day, we command to bleed after three hours.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The health of the brain and helps in the hardness of the head... that comes to them, and it is not fitting that this be after the evacuation of all the body; and this bleeding is instead of the health of the cephalic, and it is not fitting that those who are of a cold complexion use it, or who have chyluria, for it does much harm to them; because of this, it is not fitting that those who keep watch use it, nor those who have cold diseases in their head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who is often cured of this, becomes forgetful; therefore, a bit more suction should be applied due to the doubt of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation at the neck is in the place of the healed shoulder and basilicus muscle, and for this reason, it is good for narrowing the vein, and cutting the channel of the brachial artery, and everywhere, and for filling; and one should apply it only slightly, because if it holds too tightly, it can cause forgetfulness or stomach and heart issues.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventilation at the second ribs of the neck is good for headaches, eye diseases, and migraines, and for stricture, and pain in the roots of the teeth, and it is in the place of the healed basilicus muscle; therefore, you should instruct the patient to hold his hand when applying, so as not to compress the artery and avoid hemorrhages.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The ventilation above the chin is good for mouth diseases, and gum decay, and similar ailments in the mouth; and it is found in healthy tissues of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilation of the shoulders is good for diseases that come from heat and congestion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The ventilation of the armpits is as effective as three veins in the arm, for it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the healthy person not to pierce it too close to the center, for the area is naked of flesh and one can feel the nerves and arteries beneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping applied on the buttocks is good for hemorrhoids at their root, and ailments below. It should use large cups of iron, which must be well-sealed; otherwise, if they were too delicate, they might break, causing great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cups of the legs heal openly, for they draw blood from the whole body, and are effective for old pains in the sides, and in the hips, and generally weaken the body after long use, and bring on paralysis in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of placing the cup is to first empty it, and then press it gently, and put it quickly, and move evenly, and continue doing this until you see the area turn red and swell, and appear with a glow of blood; then remove it, and place the cups again, and take care in the disposition of the body, for some have thick flesh and clear pores: so it is necessary to prick only once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and slightly deep ones; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is large, it must be pricked twice: the first time to dilate the passage of the large blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very full, it must be pricked three times; and when we want to draw a little blood at a time, we prick only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want much blood, we begin often; and if the vein is full, prick it deeply, and the endings should be that the vessels are suddenly pierced, and for those with thick skin and hard veins, and who have narrow pores, you should anoint the eyes of the suction cups with a pungent and dissolving oil: if it is in heat, use olive oil or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is in winter, use mustard oil, or lavender oil, or chamomile oil, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take bitter almond oil, or balsam, or anise oil, and similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one who is being cured has flesh and large pores, it is not necessary to put any oil on it, but it should be washed after ventilation with rose water, or cold water, or pear water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or other similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture, let him rise from almond, or pear water, or sumac water, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large excesses rise from old wine, or pomegranate water, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things; and it is not advisable to be cured by suction before the bath or after bathing for one to two hours; and do not sleep after ventilation, and they should be wrapped when they are to be suctioned and when they are suctioned.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And watch over him who is healing if he is choleric, and if the blood is too acrid and inflamed; it is fitting that he take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces in vinegar, and similar things; and eat grubs, and meat from capons, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And he who has a cold complexion, should take syrup of honey and moderate fragrant wine between the old and new, and eat little, and eat grubs and small birds and pigeons; and on the day he will cupped, he should drink more than eat; and it is fitting to give some men triacle or musk before or after cupping to comfort the principal members; and let the blood be subtle, but it is not fitting that those who are hot drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are placed without piercing are those placed on the liver, and on the thigh, and podagra (arthritis of the foot), and on the belly and mouth and veins and hip, for these parts do not tolerate being pierced with needles, and one uses heat only to draw blood from member to member, as we place them on nipples when a child is born; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we place suction cups on the belly and on the mouth to diminish the swelling of the member; and removes pain, when there is abscess or stone, it sometimes removes the abscess, or displaces the stone from its place; and thus does it when placed on the liver and on the thigh when there is retained windiness, and these suction cups are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes they are applied with fire, and sometimes full of tepid water, as in diseases of pleursin (a form of inflammatory condition), and in such a manner one fills the suction cup with warm water or with water containing herbs suitable for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction cup applied with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And let it be two inches wide and half a palm's length from the furnace, with a small hole in the middle, as for inserting a needle, and made of tin, with a spout at the front so that it does not burn the patient when placed on the limb; and let there be a cross rod in the middle of tin or iron to place a wick, and their sizes should vary according to the diseases and the strength of those who use them; for the suction cups of children are different from those of adults, and of thin people from those of fat people.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one must place the suction cup on the limb in this manner: take the wax or linten wick and insert it through the hole in the middle of the suction cup, so that the flame is at the bottom of the cup to prevent burning the patient; then put it on the limb, with your two fingers on either side of the hole as we have said, so that when you look, the vapor goes out, and remove the suction cup; and replace the wick as before, and repeat often if you need to.
