En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the ventouse that is administered for a disease of pleuresy, it has no straw nor perforations, and is not applied forcefully unless it is filled with fluid, and is placed on the limb only; and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Without straws they are not applied forcefully on members where straws cannot be placed due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas; and on bare skin like that of the ear or nose, and other similar places; and the quality of the straw is that when you find withouts that are in clear, sweet water without corruption, take them; and place one nut in clear water until they are softened and have nothing inside; then draw blood by venesection and ventouse, afterwards rub the limb until it becomes red, and place the withouts on it; and when they are full and fall off, if it is a place where a ventouse can be placed, put one there, for this is very effective.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, lift the shoulder blade, and then wash it well with water, very thoroughly, and then dry. And if the wound heals too soon after the body's fluids, make a linen pad wet with cold water and place it on top; until the flesh is infected; and if there are many wounds, place broken glass or garlic, and similar things, until they are infected; or you may put on the shoulder half of peeled beans, and leave them until they burn on the shoulder, and will now stop bleeding. And if you have more need, take other fluids.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the wounds do not will to heal, rub the shoulder with fresh blood, or prick it with a needle until the wound bleeds, and then place something on it; as soon as they smell the blood, they will burn. When you see them weep, sprinkle a little aloes and ground salt or ashes on them, and they will now dry up.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These chapters are often necessary in the art of medicine, and are for the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear friend, that the knowledge in this chapter is not found in any of the ancient books or writings; and because of this, the science has been lost in our land. For I have never found anything good in them, and I know nothing of it except through the science of the ancient books, which I studied so much that I treated it, and by experiment, and from the habit of my life. And I have described here what is contained, abbreviated at the end, and shown clearly the forms of the instruments that are used, as I did in the two chapters before these.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It must therefore be said in our prologue to this book the summaries of the word and the chapters where the wise put their understanding, and remain on the truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twists or cuts happen to anyone, it must be that you hasten to sain the patient on both sides, if any condition prevents you from doing so, such as bodily weakness, illness, or age; or if his skin is too loose or too cold; and give him cold meats, that is, cold joints, and rabbit and chevron meat, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not become overly full of foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of a hot abscess or spreading of matter in the limb; so the patient recovers under the primary governance he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it must be nourished with meats that promote rapid healing or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, lentils, beef tripe, eggs, fresh fish, and good wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	And in proper nourishment, the healing process accelerates and the fractures mend faster.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the bones of old and decrepit people do not heal or set well according to their nature due to the dryness of the limbs, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but take no cure, reset the broken bone and wrap it tightly so that it unites the limb together, until it strengthens as it was before; yet do not bind it too tight in its work. For this, you must nourish with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the fractures are different in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot or the leg, and I will tell you all kinds of fractures in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go lengthwise, and others that fracture across, just like the cut of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And for each kind there is its own method and proper tool in restoration, according to what memory brings to its place; and fractures of the bone are known by the deformity of the limb, and are clearly perceived by palpation and tapping. And when there is no deformity, nor a sensation on touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there may be no fracture; but it can well have a deformity, or crack, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not fitting to move it by hand, but place medicines as mentioned hereafter, and then hold it delicately now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture which goes across, and are the two parts disjointed, you must now put them at equal points, as apertures close up to live; and if yellowish apertures come, let it remain a day or two until the apertures are pacified; then set them equally at the joints where you can gently and securely place them, and know that the restoration of this is less laborious than the restoration of that which has pieces; then hold them as it is fitting hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, set them in two parts, whether it is a hand or foot, or by your own hand if it is a small limb, or by two strings, or one string and your own hand; and place the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken member are separated, you must reset all additions within their places at the joints where you can, and see that through your work no injury or pain comes to the patient; and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well with your hand if you think it is not quite right: dress it beautifully, and do not hold it too tightly or press it as those who bring on a hot abscess and contraction to the limb through their work do many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is at point, chastise well the patient that he does not move it, neither while awake nor asleep, nor in turning, nor any other way; and see to it that the limb be so secured that he feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, it is not yet at point, and it needs to be put in proper disposition so that he feels no pain; and see to it that it be set straight, lest tortuosities arise when it is restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are varied in smallness and in largeness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For small limbs, such as arms and thighs: it is necessary to wrap them with soft and fine cloths; and those that are large, such as the thigh and leg: they should be wrapped with wide and firm bandages, because broad bandages encompass the entire limb and constrain it evenly, so there is no gap; then tie in light stops three or four times according to the limb, and slightly tighten your hand around the whole bandage, then go above the break and constrain less, so that the break can be moved a little away from the break; and gradually soften the bandage until you perceive a large part of the healthy tissue, then take the other bandage, and wrap again above the broken area; then return to the part below the break, and constrain moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first hour above; then place light stops of linen or cloth, so they are all equal, then tie everything over the main binding, and put your well-made pads on top if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, place something that soothes the abscess and reduces swelling on top, and leave it for several days; then apply hot compresses, which should be half as wide as a thick rope, or from wood used for spindles, or from palm fibers, and be according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it must be that the compress placed on the fracture is somewhat larger and wider than the others; and should be as long as necessary for the size or length of the limb. Then apply the compresses in the same manner as you did at the first application, then tie a suitable thread above them, just as you tied above the fracture at the first time. The threads are closer together below, thus less so above; and it must be that the thread is medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft flax. For if the threads are too thick, like those from leaves that make their rounds with twisted linen strings, this is a great error, because the thread cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it does not suit that there be less than two fingers' width between each compress.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the heads of arrows after being tied tightly in their sound limbs, place over them linen plugs or bandages of woollen cloth so that they do not swell.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	And when the wound is with the cauterizer, and the bones are broken, I will describe the treatment after this.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not advisable to tie up with arrows all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not advisable to tie them up tightly with arrows on the first day; rather, do so after five days or seven, or more according to your discretion based on the heat of the abscess that has come about. And here is the method of ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: take flour that clings to the walls of the mill, mix it with abundant egg, and apply this mixture not too thin nor too thick. This is a common method for using restorative plasters to treat fractures in various conditions, especially for women and small children, as it is neither too harsh nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method for a plaster to restore fractures and dislocations and twists: take 3 parts of myrrh and 1 part of ladanum and incense and gum arabic and mugat, mix 7 parts; 4 parts of myrrh and aloes, mix 5 parts; 9 parts of ambergris; grind these into a powder, then melt with the yolk of an egg; if the person's complexion is warm, use this plaster, for it is of good composition and quickly restores broken bones, worth many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method for a plaster that treats twists: take mugat and vismalve, mix 7 parts; myrrh and aloes, mix 9 parts; acacia, mix 6 parts; armenian balsam, mix 10 parts, and grind well, then prepare with water or the yolk of an egg, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another plaster for joints and the bones out of their sockets, and soothes the pain coming on, and the cutting of the bone, and the breaking: take new wool, and the fat from fleece and cooked oil, and put it on the wound.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not heal, but it is good for soothing hot abscesses, and properly removing pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another plaster to heal broken bones: take dried fig leaves, and ground ivy leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another plaster for the healing of bone fractures and to reduce the swelling of abscesses.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of visvalve, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of vetches; of each one part; and grind them, and make a paste with wine; and if the limbs are heated, mix the paste with moist coriander water or just water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of plaster more powerful than the first, when an abscess hardens during the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of visvalve, and seed of flax, balaster, melilot, and savin, and flowers of violets and chamomile; of each one part; and grind them, and make a paste with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	And Hippocrates in his book states that one should not apply anything to a broken limb for restoring strength that is made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, and he says it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen seems to say that one should apply to a broken limb things dry and slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another plaster for lesions and pain: take mithridate and horsehair cut into small pieces, or bird feathers, and vinegar, and salt, and grind them all together, and make a plaster from it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then remove it after some time, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor have the bone moved from its place; if no pain comes, do not remove it by hand. If pain comes to the area, or itching, with discomfort or swelling, hasten, and remove it, and take off the plaster now. Use a light cloth and a moist sea sponge, dip it in water, and wrap the limb until the itching ceases and the pain is relieved; then let the limb rest for an hour, after which put on dry wool soaked in water or rose oil, and bind it with a bandage until you are sure of the warm abscess; and subdue the inflammation of the limb, and remove the pain, then resume the subtle dressing and a little plaster, but do not bind it as tightly as before. Continue this subtlety until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess has become empty and redness and pain and swelling have all been removed, and you need to apply a plaster and bandage, then restart it as you did first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if none of what we have said comes to the member, and it is not dislocated after three days or four or five or seven; at some point leave it twenty days, as one sees, until the fracture dries up, and bring near the adjustment of the flesh; then restrain more than first, and let it grow its flesh, as I said before; and if you see that the place dry out more than is necessary, know that nourishment cannot come; apply hot water cloth each time you dislocate it, and let it rest a bit; by this work thus cut off the nourishment to the member, and mend quickly what the foolish menders do, which leave the member deformed: this is bad, and such are fear-filled works, and I see nothing else but to leave it and work straight.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many ways of fractures are, and various figures, and the causes are destined; for there are fractures that are made by the percussion of a sword, and the neck cuts all the bone just to the syface which is beneath the bone, as does a hatchet or club; and because of this, this manner of fracture is called "hatchet fracture.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts through the bone from above without piercing, and this manner of fracture is called "absolute"; it includes both large or small wounds.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a compression fracture, or a split, from stones, or falling on stones, or other similar cases.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture perilous, which approaches just to the tissue beneath the bone, or on the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that is seated in the bone as fine as hairs, and is a small裂伤，因此称为这种骨折为“毛细血管”骨折；而如果伤口是由石头撞击、跌落或类似事物造成的，并使骨片向下进入，使骨头的边缘像铁匠在锅上打击时那样；石块内部会有裂缝。
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have or chief moist bones, such as children's bones; and it happens in all these ways of fracture where small pieces are dislodged like splinters; and I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all manner of fractures by their symptoms, and by probing, and by the rotten flesh that is upon them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the hair is known by this: when the bone is discovered and rubbed over it, the black fractures become apparent.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, take care of the patient's condition, and if you see no bad symptoms, such as vomiting of bile, loss of consciousness, swelling, paralysis, feverish chills, and the eyes turning white and red, and other similar things in various dispositions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any alarming symptoms, and you hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the pain comes first to you, and it is in winter, then you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day after the moon.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, you must hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue beneath the bone becomes corrupted, and the accidents as we have said come about.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone comes just to the tissue that covers the brain, then you must split the fractured part in such a way: and you must take hold of the chief part of the injured bone, and uncover above the bone in all ways that you can, and more especially over the figure of the wound. And if bleeding from the bone occurs upon uncovering the bone, or an abscess forms, then assist with what is needed, and it is that you fill the space under the skin with moistened linen soaked in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the abscesses subside, and you are assured of no further bleeding; then begin beneath the bone to remove it, and this is done according to two methods of work: one method is that you cut precisely at the front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I make another incision larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have a number of different incisions, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and made of iron. And work lightly, so as not to burn the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and dense, you must pierce it through and through, as when making incisions with trepanning tools, not completely but so that the point does not pass beyond the bone of the skull. It should have a margin or circle above the point, preventing it from passing beyond the bone; and you must have several, so that each comes to its place according to the thickness of the skull, ensuring you have trepanning tools for all skulls. And this is the form of the three kinds of trepanning tools.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities to pierce through the bone break and are that you place the probe on the bone, turn it to your two hands until you know that the bone is pierced; then remove the probe a little bit further in another part, and do this throughout, then scrape with the lancets the space of the bone which is between the perforations, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, so that you bring the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments you have such as tongs, forceps; and guard that you do not touch the brain nor the face.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, it is necessary that you reset the displacement which has remained from the bone to all other similar instruments, but it must be more tense and more subtle than the other lancets; and if there remains any small bones or no scales, you should remove them gently with the instruments; then cure the wound with dressings and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of work is that which Galien said, which is safer; and it is strong, and it is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, at the spot where the break opens up, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place under the head of this incisor a lens-shaped piece, as described here.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and let the broken part be on two sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer above, so that you lightly fracture the bone all around, and take care to protect the membrane beneath; if it is close to the bone, gently remove it, for it can be removed too easily and with fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not pierce as far as the membrane, and the bone is cut only from above, and there are small pieces, then it must be treated after that roughness, and remove the scales with a fine razor of which you should have various quantities, to apply in each place what is most suitable, according to the work and the shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you use large razors first and then finer ones, and do not stop until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other fine incisions and subtle breaks, you must apply what is most suitable according to its nature; and this is a matter that is not fully covered by one who has devoted his study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the face is uncovered, you must take a linen cloth according to the size of the wound, and in oil from roses, and apply it to the wound. Then take another doubled cloth twice or three times over, with wine and oil from roses, and place it on top of the first cloth. Do this as lightly as possible so that you do not burden the face. Then apply a bandage above the other one without binding it too tightly so as only to touch the wound; leave it like this for a day or two until the abscesses are calmed, then remove it and administer medicines such as lily roots, wheat flour, incense powder, and aromatic herbs, and similar things. Make these into a powder and apply it to the wound, and administer additional non-irritating medicines without causing stinging. And see that the wound remains clean; do not leave the ointment off, nor allow it to gather moisture, for when moisture gathers on the cloth over the brain, it will flow and cause great harm to the patient; for when anything irritating is applied to the face, it does not heal properly from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take note, if no adverse accident occurs to the patient, as we have said, there is doubt without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if night comes and only because of the medicine we have put on, it has such virtue, then you should take a part of honey, three parts of rose oil, and in gum one rag, and apply it to the sore; then treat it as a wound should be treated until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts above the neck are broken, or only one of them, for these are two bones; and the one beneath is cartilaginous, and does not break nor cause pain or twist, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you insert your small finger or thumb from the root, and set the break equal within your index finger, and in the palm by pressing, so that the root regains its natural figure; and do this gently, and ensure that the patient does not feel pain through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is above the nose and your finger cannot reach the place, it is necessary that you set it equal to the base of a thumb slightly larger.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is on both sides, do the same on the other side, and hasten to restore the first day if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscesses are subsided, then insert tented linen threads into the base of the nose, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or if you strike the other side, where the injury is; let the swellings be so large that they fill the pores of the birth.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And any restorer shall moisten the swellings with butter and change each one every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem right to me, but the swellings should be moistened with a preparation of egg white and flour of wheat; then leave the swelling until the bones are firm and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one uses goose quills in place of swellings, and if there is an opening, cover it with a cloth; and keep the wound clean, and blow on it to dry it out; do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses form on the nose as you work on it, apply a poultice or a moist cloth in rose oil, or with a little diaphoretic.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses do not form on the nose, apply an ointment from above, made of silkworm silk powder and incense powder, cooked with egg yolk. Then place it over light stoppets, and do not tie the nose. And if the break in the nose is small, and it is broken into small pieces, extract it with tools suitable for this, then close the wound and treat matters concerning flesh, sewing, as ointments and applications suitable for this; and if there are no wounds inside the nose, treat with lint, and place cottons until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the rupture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is ruptured but there is no wound visible, and the fracture is open only, not broken into pieces but rather like corners inside, one can recognize it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It must be, if the fracture is in the right part of the jaw, that you place your index finger in the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is in the left mandible, you place your right hand's index finger near the fracture gently, and complete it with the other hand through a small opening and keep it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is separated into two parts, it must be that you administer an extension to both parts, making them equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movement of the teeth occurs, or rupture, strain them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place on the broken jaw a poultice, and place under it a double cloth; and place on this cloth a well-made pad, or a piece of leather equal in size to the jaw, and attach it to the cheek as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, release it on the third day, and then put back in place what has changed; and apply a poultice with flour from the mill mixed with abundant egg or sinew flour after you have removed the poultice; and place over the poultice a light cloth, and if the poultices dry out and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until he is healed; many times it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses continue to form, administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, note any piece of the bone that has been removed; so subtle to remove with instruments suitable for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with flammes according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there is none remaining, close the wound if it is wide, and apply suitable plasters over it to promote healing until it is healed.
de la forcele	from the strength (or force)
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The shoulder blade breaks multiple times in front, near the shoulder, and the break occurs in three ways: either it is broken and dislocated into two pieces, which is the lighter to reset; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the procedure is as follows when the break has no wound: you should have two assistants, one holding the shoulder blade that feels the broken bone; and the other extending the neck toward the affected area. Then align the break with your hands so that the shape is as it should be, and there should be neither appearance nor movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place a round pad of cloth or wool over the shoulder on the patient, making it as large as necessary; then stretch and lift the broken bone, and hold the pad with your hand, so that you can align the break properly.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder outwards, because it comes perfectly, then it is necessary that the patient lie often on his back, and place a medium pillow under the shoulder, and direct the attendants to support the shoulder downwards until the bone of the shoulder is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then treat the fracture with your hands, and if you find any fragments, you must split them; and draw the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join for any prominence, use one of your incisors; but place this instrument over the shoulder to prevent swelling.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it seems like a spoon, and is not in place, and should be as wide as it suits, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and has two heads, as you see, and one should be broad, and the other narrow, as is the tear of the wound that you made when you drew the bones; and when you are assured of a hot abscess, close the wound, and if the tear is small, or you doubt a hot abscess, fill the wound with cloths and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess is fully formed, I wrap it in rose oil and honey and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The setting of the bone, when it is sensed by wounds and cuts, is that you place on the bone a plaster of flour powder and egg yolk, and cover with light stoppers, and put a sphere underneath the stopper if needed; then take a very large bandage one palm wide, place the folded cloth over the stoppers and the plaster; next, take a thin stick three fingers wide and long, wrap it around the bandage, so that the ends of the bandage hang down; place the stick on the fracture, turn the bandage around the neck, under the stopper, and above the injured part; tighten each part, and when you see that the ligatures hold the fracture properly, and clearly see that the stick does not move over the broken bone, then dress it daily, and when the skin loosens, release the restraint; make the patient lie on their back, and place a small pillow under the stopper to raise the shoulder; this will alleviate the force of the fracture by supporting the shoulder, or tie the arm around the neck, and do not untie it unless bad accidents occur, up to twenty days; then reapply the plaster if needed, and keep it tight until it is restored; it is usually restored within twenty-eight days, but in some cases, it may take less time.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the shoulder is broken or cracked and not entirely shattered, and one cannot tell from the touch; adjust the joint according to the shape of the break, and reset it in its natural form in all ways possible; then apply a powder made with flour and egg, wrap lightly, and place over a double cloth; next, put on a broad, thin strip slightly wider than the shoulder, ensuring no movement in any part of the shoulder. If necessary, secure this strip with linen stoppers so it sets evenly; then tightly bandage around the entire area to keep the strip from moving, checking the stitches each day; whenever it swells, re-bandage and adjust the strip if it is out of place, and let the patient rest on their side; the shoulder will be healed in about 20 or 25 days. When these numbers are completed, release the bindings, for it is not bone that sets quickly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone tends forward and points out from the heart, make an incision, remove the bone, and do what we have said in the breaking of the forcele to cool an abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The foot is often broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; it breaks frequently at the ankle.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it bends outward, and the patient feels great pain, as well as loss of consciousness. Immediately, and by chance, they may vomit blood, and the movement in the broken bones becomes apparent, and everyone can see this well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on their back, and they place a cushion between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and align the ribs of the two sides with your hands, subtly adjusting them in all possible ways until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then apply plasters and ointments over the fine salt substrate or another light material, wrap them in a cloth, and tie them securely to the broken bone so they do not move; turn the bandage round the back, adjust it appropriately, and rewrap the ligature every hour, tightening if it loosens; and if it needs to be untied for corrosion or itching at the site, or pain or abscess, you should hurry and untie it, remove the plaster, and treat what has appeared as in wound care; then rewedge the plaster and secure it until healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	The breaking of the ribs comes from force only behind the shoulders and at the upper part within, and they do not bend from force because they are lubricated; and one feels this well during examination through the sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	The restoration is that you set the break equally, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and bind it with a bandage if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break of the ribs is leaning inward, the patient feels intense pain and puncture-like discomfort, similar to weeping, because the bone pierces the membrane; they wrinkle their face, and immediately vomit large amounts of blood, which is a serious health issue. The elderly have used great skill in treating this.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if some say that it is fitting to give foods that swell the belly to administer, to put off the ache.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make those that abscesses form if they have not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have come, let them heal.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And if any of you put cups on the shoulder to draw fluid, it seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cups will attract the superfluities to the shoulder due to the disposition of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And if any of you say that we should cover the shoulder with wetted wool in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to make the treatment uniform, then it should be treated with the pleurisy cure, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain he cannot endure through the bone where the vein is ruptured, and there is doubt for the patient, it is necessary to incise above the rib of the broken rib, and it is necessary to place something beneath the instrument to protect the lung; then one must cut the bone, and extract lightly, and then suture the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat with plasters until he is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses continue, place wet cloths in rose oil and apply them to the rib. Cure by treating the rib as needed for the abscess, and keep lying on the side where it should be, until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	from the break of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there is a break in the bones of the neck, and rarely does it bend; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be cured or not, look to see if their hands are softened, swollen, and dead, and they cannot move or extend them. And when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is fatal in many instances, and if they can move and feel well when you hold and prick them, know that the joints of the bone are saved, and that the patient will recover if proper treatment is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things come to the spine of the back, and you want to know if they will be cured or not, look to see if the patches are softened, and if the accidents are those in the hands, and on the back with windiness and involuntary evacuation; and when it is sovined over their belly, there is involuntary evacuation.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is inflamed on its back and he wishes to apply a salve, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	It is mortal: he should not work at all in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to him, it is a much lighter matter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you apply it if there is a hot abscess, placing an olive oil or egg yolk oil on it until it subsides. Then place one of the comforting and drying plasters over it, and bind it with a bandage. Instruct the patient to rest; he should not sleep in that part where he feels the pain until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone splits open, it is necessary to cover over the heart; remove the bone, then join the two edges of the wound, if large, with a stitch, and treat with ointment promoting flesh growth until healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the cow," you should hold your left hand's pouch and place it equally in your right hand at your power, then apply the plaster and bandage over it if needed; then bind it, and if there is a split bone, make an incision, remove it, and treat the wound until healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the breaking of the bone of the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	Often, the bone of the hip is broken, and if it happens, there will be only slight swelling at the head; make a long incision, and angle downwards to the front teeth, and bring about pain, point tenderness, and swelling where it breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above, as long as you are over the burner; and know which are the breaks and their figures; and if the break is only in the head, you set it evenly so that it is in natural figure.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or it declines inward, you make the patient lie on his stomach so that the restoration of that break may be aligned.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it even, apply a plaster, then place a stick or a cork on top, and bind the burner so that it does not move. And fill the space under the ribs, making the binding even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their sound side, or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if abscesses form and come up, do not touch them until the abscesses are pacified, and apply what we have said before; then return to the restoration, and hold them as is fitting, if there is no bad accident; and this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the breaking of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The adjutoires are those between the scapula and the head of the shoulder. If they are broken, you must restore them according to one of the two methods: one method is that you take a stick filled with moistened grain, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two heads of the ligaments, and press them upwards, and place the patient's broken arm on the stick until it reaches the armpit, with a notch in the stick. Then place some heavy thing or have the attendants extend it downwards; then place the broken part level with the patient's hands together, so that the broken part returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that one soothes the patient on his haterel, and ties his hand to his neck, then commands two ministers that one pricks him above at his hands, and the other pricks underneath at both wrists, extending each to their part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is stronger, hold the wrist both below and above the pricker, and extend each of the ministers to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the pricker is near the head of the shoulder, you should place the wrist in the middle below the axilla, and the other towards the side, below the pricker; and similarly, if the pricker is towards the side, you should place the wrist lightly, without labor, so that the pricker is level both above the joint and above the side; then place the incision as it should be, and hold it steady, unless abscesses come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if abscesses have formed, do not extract them until the seventh day, and place on a wetted cloth in oil of roses, until the abscesses are pacified; then extract them, and the manner of extracting them is that you apply the plaster to the wound, then assemble the arm over the assistant, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and put the bandage, and bind over the assistant, and over the arm, so that the arm be in a level position, unless something prevents it, or if the bone is displaced.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is displaced, use a splint, and place over the wound a splint wider and stronger than the others, with two fingers' breadth between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it passes the wound three fingers' breadth on each side; then bind over the splints as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the wound, more tightly but not by drawing away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the seat of the stars, and the constriction, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken limb, and you doubt the hot abscess, let it remain bound for seven days, as we have said; then look each three days at the wound, to see if itching or swelling arises at the site, or if the growths cannot come to the limb because it is too narrow.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the treatment, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents occur, and the dislocation does not happen after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, and place his hands on his stomach; and put underneath the shoulder a cushion full of evenly cut wool, and observe each hour of the day or night that the figure of the broken limb does not move, or that the ligaments do not become soft; if the treatment proceeds by the virtue of medicine, and let him have the meat as we have placed before, in such a manner that the meat be at the first subtle stage; and when it begins to take hold, let it be generous.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is custom that the shoulder and the leg should be taken back in forty days from all; then one must release them and administer baths and ointment medications to correct the resetting.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the contraction is ugly and constricted, it must remain to be released for one or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.
