The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "fascicle" bones; one is small and follows the pocket, and the other is large and is below, opposite the small finger; by chance, only the large fascicle bone may be broken, or the small one, and by chance both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, the restoration is light, and the healing; and when the large ones are broken, the healing is poor, and more grievous than when they are broken all together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small bones that are broken only, then it should be extended lightly, and placed evenly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bones, they should be held more firmly; and extend them on the cushion, and lift the pocket of the hand higher than the others, and the small bones lower than the others. Let the patient cross their limbs over themselves, with the cushion in front higher than the patient so that the patient does not suffer any labor; then extend the attendants' arms below their hands, or at the elbow, and another attendant above at the other side.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then set the bones equal, according to their best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture it is broken into pieces, set each piece in its place, and if there is any that cannot be grasped by the hand, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut open and remove it, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the bone saw, I have spoken of it in the singular chapter; then proceed with the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if during the beginning of the restoration abscesses appear, apply a dressing made of rose oil and white wax, that is neither too hard nor too soft; and tie the dressing tightly enough so that the abscesses are pacified.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the plaster, and put the ointment of the powder from the mill with abundant egg, pour in the cloths, let one of the cloths of the burner be stronger, and a bit wider than the others; and know that it must have six cloths or arms in several positions: whether the burner is in one of the bones, or two; and restrain more above the burner than elsewhere, and all day less by extending, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let those on top of the burner be soft and moist, and not hard nor rough; and let the thread from which it is drawn be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the joint after several days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accident comes to the limb, as itching that comes to the limb, it is necessary that you moisten the limb with hot water until those itchings are soothed; and let the limb rest not too tightly.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then reapply the binding, and if the ligaments are softened and the bones displaced, and something seems wrong, set them right.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if one watches that the swelling does not come to the limb, because it is too tight, it is necessary that you soften it a little, and let it so for some days, until the swelling goes down, and then bind it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of the things we have said come to the patient, do not unbind it for up to 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	or between the neckbones, then turn his hands to his neck, and let his neck be even, and beware of movement and displacement, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is restored in XXX days or in XXXV, and by chance in XX days, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that in the back of the hand and at the knuckles, fractures occur rarely, and there often comes much pain.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the sole of the hand is fractured or bent, the patient should place his foot with the sole straight in front of him even; then put his hand on the extended surface, and extend the broken bones, placing them evenly so they are well aligned; apply the plaster and stopes if no abscesses come, then place a bandage according to the size of the area; let it be wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is in the heel between the sole and the shin, make a sphere of bandages, and instruct the patient to bind it to his broken heel; then bind with a long strip of cloth, and let the padding be of cork about as large as the palm of the hand, and bind as appropriate.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the foot, it is necessary to place a pad above and one below on the sole, so that the hand remains open and straight, then bind tightly around the hand, and secure the bandage between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to any of our fingers, if they are broken, set them equal, as is appropriate; and bind with the palm, and if you see, place a small straight pad to lift the fracture, and it does not move; and if the fracture is on the other fingers, such as in the index or one of the others, set them equal, and bind with the healthy finger that follows; or you can bind all together, keeping them still, or you place a pad above, like a pouch; and take care in the restoration and arrangement of warm abscesses, and aid those who come, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and one can see this when it twists frontward and backward; and the restoration is to tie one ligament above the break and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on their side, then each minister extends their ligament to their part equally; and this is when the break is placed in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the thigh, then place one ligament on the side of the knife, and the other ligament below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is near the knee, then place the ligaments below the knee, and the extension downward; then set the bone equal with both hands, so that it is according to its natural figure, and then apply the plaster and the ligament, unless an abscess forms.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside first, then return to your work and treatment; the incision is made in such a manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap around the sprain with a linen bandage doubled two or three times, and let the surplus remain, then turn the leg until the heels reach the root of the ankle, and insert a long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the knee inside, and let the end of the thread appear above; then turn back to the leg and thigh with the bandage, and place a splint on the sprain, and put one splint on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and thigh with soft cloth to ensure even pressure, then begin to tie in three or four turns around the sprain; and as you go further from the sprain, tie less tightly; then attend to the two ends of the thread that you inserted between the leg and thigh, and put three splints above them, then return below to the end of the thread, until you see down to the foot; and tighten so that it does not move in its place, then leave it thus, until no abscess or swelling appears elsewhere.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, reset it, and align what comes to you as we have said many times; and if there are bone pieces that prick, it must be washed if possible; and if one cannot, it must cut the limb, and draw out pus; and cure it as we have said until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the thigh broken thus we set it, as in the shoulder and arm; nevertheless, in the restoration done, the patient does not suffer pain.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in three days, or somewhat fewer or somewhat more, according to the diversities of the constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the groove of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the joint of the knee there is little fracture, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it fractures, it is not just a crack or hole, but comes to all wounds and wound-like injuries, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that one should place equal wax on its two parts, as long as they are assembled and can move; then apply the plaster, and put a round strip, if you need it, and hold it properly. Then re-establish all the dispositions that we have said for other fractures, such as hot abscesses and similar cases; apply what is suitable for each accident until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	In the leg there are two bones, of which one is called "mustelz" and the other "foscile"; and fractures occur in all ways as they do in the arm, and for this reason the restoration is equally as that of the arm, and the operations are the same. And if both bones are broken together, the leg turns in every direction.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the finer bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the larger bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it is clearly visible; and it turns outward.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then apply extension, and set it equal, and tie the straps equally; but in any case, if the fracture is ugly and there are many pieces, the extension should be less and lighter; and lighten it according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed all your work, take two straps of woven wood that fit the leg on one side and the other, and be long from the leg below the knee to above; then wrap in two layers over and under with a bandage, and tie them in the middle thus, and at this place the leg will not decline to right nor to left, and so it is well; and none administer a long bier of wood for the leg, and set the leg to guard against movement, and properly do you make it in the fracture where there is wound; and move each day the leg, to see if there is a hot abscess or any other accident; and cure until it be healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	In the ankle there is no breaking, but in the bone of the foot there is sometimes a breaking and in the toes there is no strength besides weakness from multiple conditions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a breaking in the bone of the foot, and you see these bones sticking out one over the other, place the patient's foot on the ground as if it wanted to walk, and then put your foot on top of his, where the bones are raised, and press until they return to their places; then apply the plaster and ointment, and put a small board with two pieces of cloth under the sole of the foot, then bind it appropriately. After you have wrapped it with bandages around and other things you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four have passed, untie the bandage, for you will find the bones equal, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the two are broken, restore them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then put on each broken finger a splint according to the length of the finger, and let it be somewhat wider. Then place under the foot that block which I have said, and hold it properly in place; and if there are two or three, or more, broken ones, put on each finger one splint according to its quantity, wrapped in a linen cloth, and place the block under the foot. And let it be placed over the head of the block behind the sole of the foot, so that it touches well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said to the other breakers, as we have said; and assist each accident as it requires.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone at the blade
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's nature is fractured, make her sit propped up, then incline her towards the part of the back, and hold her by the rear. Then fill the cavity of the woman's nature with cotton, putting in as much as she can tolerate. Then remove the woman, gradually lifting her back, allowing the cotton to fall until it reaches the entrance of the body, and the bone returns with the flesh. When she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, replace it, doing this for seven days or so: thus will the fracture be restored. If you wish, take a bladder from a goat, attach a string to the opening, and fill the entire bladder inside. The nature will return the fracture; then fill it with cotton and leave it that way for some days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the hand is broken in man or woman, restore it as we have said for the bone of the hip; and these nearby breaks are not hidden from him who applies his study and his use, and hears my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the breaks signify in many ways the right way of restoration: understand them accordingly.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the thigh, when it is broken, take a goose quill and insert the thigh into it; then wrap it with bandages around, and let it lie for three days or more, and it will be quickly healed.
de brisure avec plaie	from break with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	For he who has a break with a wound, even if the wound is large, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, must be healed now, as our treatments indicate.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healthy, staunch it with vitriol, if you have nothing else, then resume the healing at that same hour or on that same day, if no abscesses arise.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if no abscesses arise, let the healing continue until the next day, until the abscesses are appeased, and do not touch it on the third day or the fourth, for you would cause harmful accidents.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is apparent on the exposed chest, it is necessary to place it gently with your hands, extending it slightly.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not available to make it equal with your hands, then reset it with an instrument made of iron, which has seven or eight lengths, and its width is according to the size of the wound; and for this, a splint must be prepared that soaks three or four times, according to what it needs for each healing of a fracture; and it should be round and slightly thick, so it does not bend much under compression on the limb during your work, and it should be hard in front, and thick in the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche," for which it must be that the curved heads of the shoulder be placed on the head of the apparent bone; and set once, until it returns, and let them be even one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instruments cannot take hold of the bone well, then you must file the head of the bone until the instruments can grasp it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back, as we have said, file the head of an appropriate instrument, such as a scaler or probe, to your ability; then remove what remains in the bone by hardness and small fragments.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is brought back, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you place it in its proper position, then moisten the bandage with black wine vinegar, and properly if it is soiled; do not put any ointment or anything else on the wound that might cause infection and decay; then administer leeches when you have set the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, covering around it according to the size of the wound, and take great care that the wound is not compressed by the breakage; many times foolish people have done this and caused the patient to die or become infected at least once; let the compressions be softer and less severe than other types of bandages.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a harmful accident may occur, as we have said, and you find pain at the site, then it should not be covered with leeches; but wrap around it instead, in place of leeches, with hard bandages, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days the wound weep from the wound, remove what you have placed above all the wine, and put healing ointment for wounds, such as tetrafarmacon and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must dislocate the limb two times a day, in the morning and at evening, until it is set and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limb must be adjusted in such a manner that the wound runs downward smoothly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass and the wound cannot heal any further, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which you must clean the wound with a tent, and remove all these detached pieces that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the head, or any other kind of corruption, it must be treated, according to what he says in his chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and open in the same limb, as the bones of the thigh or shoulder, or other similar large bones, do not treat it immediately, for many times death comes from it, but let it be until it rots; by chance it may fall out by itself after 20 days or 30, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	from bruises that come over the sutures
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Many times after the breakage, especially when it is near the joint, and it is a sad sight to see the figure of the limb; by chance it cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore take care that the joint is fresh: if it allows, administer styptic medicines such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, as well as sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others, so that you use any of these things or all together, and prepare them with styptic wine or plenty of egg or with honey; place them on the joint in vials, and bind it tightly, not letting it loose for several days by hand; then remove it, and start another one until the swellings are gone; or you can bind it over a well-made pad; for the properties of the padding so completely dissipate all swellings above the limbs; and if the swelling has already turned to hardness like stone and needs removal, cover it with a poultice and let the superfluous part be seen; or you can send it to any barber until it is removed, and cure it when it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of a limb that is weak after the siege
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored and remains after the limb is weak and delicate, it happens for many causes: one of which is because it was tied too tightly, and not as it should have been; or because there were too many bindings, preventing new growth in the limb; or due to excessive swelling; or from too great movements, not at their proper time; or because there is little blood in his body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you make the patient eat and strengthen the body until the flesh multiplies within him; give him baths, and provide him joy and ease; then apply ointment to the limb, so that the ointment draws toward the great growth, and frequently wet it with warm water until the growth reaches the limb; and return to its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the limb twisted after recovery
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after recovery, and the broken bones are exposed, and the form of the limb is ugly, all in all, it does not affect its natural function: one should not believe the fools who say that one must break the limb completely anew; many such foolish acts have been done in our land; these works are blamed, and they bring great harms, and even death by chance; therefore, if the swellings and tortures are fresh, it is necessary to treat them with warm water, or cook herbs that soften, such as the leaves of vismarl, roots, marjoram, and similar medicines; then apply a softening plaster, well made, and take the muscilage of vismarl, mix it with gelatin fat or silk oil, and apply it over; or take fatty figs, grind them with colon flour, and use such medicines that quickly alleviate.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the nodes are removed by rubbing continuously and for a long time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And may the limb be moved each hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is aged and hardened, like stone, and it is necessary to remove it with iron, then it should be cut down to the bone using a sharp incisor gently; and great care and skill are needed in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book on dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, it is fitting now to reset it without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the shoulder will swell, and by chance, if it is set with pins at the swelling; for this, it is not fitting to move it while it is swollen: many times it brings about spasm and other pains; nevertheless, when this happens, make the patient lie down, then let him rest until the abscesses are fully healed; then apply hot water and oil, and reset it gently, and cure each limb as it comes back into its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on shoulder dislocations from the head down to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Often the jaws are dislocated sideways, and the dislocations of both sides occur in two ways: either they are slightly displaced from their joints and somewhat softened; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the chin, and stop saliva from the mouth so he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, enveloping his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is slight, it often returns to place through natural means.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if the dislocation is complete and thorough, you must quickly reset it without delay; and in such a manner that the attendant holds the patient's head, and places a cloth or poultice from one of his hands at the root of the jaw dislocation inside the mouth, if the dislocation affects both sides; and the other hand should be free to ensure equality. Instruct the patient to soften and move his jaws in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And place the joint equally, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the reduction is difficult, especially if it involves the two lower jaws together, apply hot water and oil, gently resetting them; do not force the reduction, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are reduced equally, and the patient's mouth closes well, gently soften it by applying moistened cloth in a paste made of rose oil and wax. Then loosely tie it with soft threads; and let the patient sleep on his back, with his head between two cushions so that he cannot move left or right, nor force his jaw to close. Instead, give him light food until the pains are gone, and secure the lower jaws. Then allow him to eat and drink lightly as he wishes without opening his mouth for eating and drinking, until the mandibles are well set and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibules cannot be reset to place within an hour and are not completely returned to their sockets, then fevers and stiffened conditions become accustomed, and by chance there may be a collapse of the abdomen, and by chance pure vomiting occurs.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know it is fatal; many times those who suffer from it die within nine days.
de la forcelle	of the forceps
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot dislocate downward along the continuation of the bone and outward toward the foot, and is only dislocated once at the fracture, and one can feel this clearly.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on their back and extends their arms. Then press the bone firmly with your palm, and it will return. Place a plaster and a bandage over it, and tighten it. The head near the cut cannot dislocate; if at all, then reset it to its place as we have said. Place a plaster and a bandage over it, tighten it, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed. Thus, the head of the shoulder is brought back when it is displaced from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	The shoulder is dislocated in three ways: one, it dislocates at the part of the socket outwards; and the second, at the part of the humerus; and by chance it dislocates upwards, which happens seldom; and it does not dislocate backwards for the shoulder, nor internally for the nerves; and often it dislocates from below towards the socket, especially in those who have little flesh, because in them it springs suddenly; in those who have enough flesh, it springs with a wrench and returns with a wrench.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men from a blow or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated for this reason.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It must therefore be tested thoroughly until you are certain; then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that dislocations occur when the head slides toward the armpit, and you make a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a clear difference between them; and you will find a hollow in the head of the shoulder, and beneath the armpit at the edge of the shoulder blade, as if it were a bony prominence; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor move with any movements; and similarly, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you find it clearly when palpating; and this manner of dislocation is not easily reducible when new, or when the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the ministers lift the patient's hand upwards, then place their palms under the armpit, and dislocate the joint with force upwards to its place; and the ministers lift the hand and extend it upwards, then place it there; it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said with the hands a few days after, it must be that the patient is bathed in warm water; and the attendant apply soothing and assuaging remedies, such as decoction of althea and fenugreek and marigold in water, and apply them; then cover the patient's back, and place a woollen cloth evenly, neither too soft nor too hard, under the armpit; then place the patient's foot on the cloth, and lift the shoulder blade properly, and pull the hand of the patient upwards; and another minister hold the patient's head downwards so that it does not move downwards; this shoulder will now return, and if you wish to reset it in this manner: ensure that a person larger than the patient is present; place them facing the side, and insert the shoulder under the armpit of the larger person, then lift the larger person's arm upwards, so that the patient's body hangs by the arm; and another minister pull the hand of the patient downwards towards the abdomen.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, he may add something heavy to him, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the dislocation is also reset in another manner: and it is so that one sticks a long poker into the ground, where the head of the shoulder should be as round as a pike, neither too large nor too small; then it is placed under the patient, but he should have a cushion under, and the patient should be stretched lengthwise from another direction firmly; and the joint will return to its place quickly. And if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, do this cure: take a poker of two arm's length in height and four fingers in width, which has a head round enough to enter perfectly under the armpit, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then bind above the head of the bone with a cloth, so that the bone does not swell for the patient, then place under the patient; and extend your arm above the long bone, and bind the auxiliary above the bone, and the arm to the head of the hand, then place the arm on the ladder of a large ladder, and let the hand hang downward, and leave the body hanging from another part: the joint will now recover gradually.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is dry, in whatever manner it may be, you must place under the pillow a pad of wool even, then apply the plaster prepared with flour of mill, with incense and egg yolk, over the whole shoulder and around, then remove the pad from under the pillow as appropriate, and turn the bandage over the plaster, and embrace the hand at its neck, and let the hand remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it must be eaten little, so that the limb is strengthened, for it will heal faster; and thereafter eat more after five or seven days, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is dislocated due to moisture or for another reason, it must be treated with three punctures of the fire cautery as described in the chapter on fire cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it dislocates after seven days, and the joint does not hold and cannot lift the arm upward, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint never returned to its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocations that are around the buttocks, and the breasts, or behind, are caused by impulse and extension of hands; and they are treated until they are healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes cracks in the limb, and delays due to movement, the patient uses baths many times until those cracks heal and return to their original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated at points, and returns to those points; and it is dislocated from all sides, especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not replied to, for it can be seen clearly and felt clearly; and it is dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the diseased part with the healthy one, you must clearly see it.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And the joint is fixed, and cannot bend the arm or touch its shoulder in any way.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must first reset it as abscesses heal and come to an end, for if abscesses heal and come to an end, it would be grievous to bring them back; and by chance, they cannot always be fully reset, especially when it is in the deepest part. Such dislocations are worse than others, and cause more pain, and by chance, they may even lead to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is such that when it can be reset in this manner, you extend its hand with both your hands; and its arms are spread out, and the hands positioned according to the edge of the cut around, above, and below, and place the joint at its proper position or at the root of its palm until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his face and fixes the root of the palm with the knife which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it will not return to its place, give strong extension; and two ministers extend the arm, and tie it with ministers, so that it does not move in extension; then turn the arm in every direction, then wrap it in a double long and wide cloth; and when you join the joint to his hand, apply an eye for softening the joint, then form the joint, until it returns; and when it is in its place, put on a dry plaster with egg yolk, and bind it firmly, and hang the arm at the neck of the patient, and let it be for some days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly set in its place, loosen the ligament, and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not fit well, reapply the plaster and the ligament, and leave it for some days, until it is firmly placed; then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if it feels fractured after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, then bathe and gently rub it, pressing until it is alleviated; or you may place a fatty sheep tallow on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and apply hot water therapy; and when it sweats, thoroughly rub the joint, then reapply the tallow, and again apply hot water therapy; and do this two or three times until it is healed; and if you see, place warm moist sheep's dung heated with butter, and apply it; it will return to its proper position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand is severe, and the return is light, more than other joints. Therefore, one must reset it to its place quickly, as soon as it becomes dislocated, just as the shoulder swells or an abscess forms hotly.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the resetting is such that you place the injured hand on a table, and extend the fingers of the hand. Then, hold the palm so it aligns with the joint, and keep pressing until it returns to its proper position. You must ensure it is properly set; then, place the back of the injured hand on the table for extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, place the patient's back of the hand on the table, and the helper place his hand on that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, that is well. If not, apply a plaster to ease the abscess and let him be thus until it begins again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after several days, the joint will remain crooked; and it does not harm the patient as long as the hand is soft and cannot grasp anything at all: then know that the nerve is severed or the artery; there is no other means but to apply a fire cautery near the case, and by chance nothing else works.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put the plaster that we have said on it, then bind and let it be 5 days, then unbind and leave thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot move well, and there is any stiffness, apply warm liquid gelatin and rub until it heals.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated in any direction, sometimes at the back of the palm or the palm's center; then straighten the finger, and hold the dislocation with your thumb until it returns to place. Then support the end of the finger, and bend it toward the part where it is disjointed; and let it be 2 days, and then keep it straight for that day; and bind it as we have said, and unbind it each day, and allow it to move, and rebind it at night; and do this often until it is tight. If it is dislocated in the palm of the hand, do so as you did before until it heals. And similarly, if it is dislocated in any other part, do so until it heals.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the shoulder blade from the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder blade from the back or neck is dislocated, or there are multiple dislocations, there is no proper treatment, for death comes quickly to the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the evacuations come without consent, nor can they be held, and often the members become soft, or both hips or both arms. And often the shoulder blade changes into four parts; that which changes at the back is called "gilbositez": the treatment is to reward if gilbositez has come from childhood: there is no cure or healing for this.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or impacts or similar things, the ancient methods of treatment with grand words say they have no real benefit in all cases; but I have abbreviated them according to my intention, and formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the carbuncle that comes to the buttocks before, there is no cure; and so it is with that which comes directly into two sides, and one cannot cure it outside except the one that comes properly to the back, as I say; and it is that the patient extend his body on one side equally, and have an arrow beneath him, so that he does not blister; then stick a brand in the head in the ground, and another at the feet, and tie a rope under the armpits of the patient, and another at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and two ministers know the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, among the two brands; and their hands be well fastened, the brand as we have said, and the prisoners put their palms on the spine in form, until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return through this treatment, take a board of three fingers in length, and wedge it beneath the wall, and if the patient is on their side, place the head of the board beneath the wall, then put the middle of the board over the spine; and have the patient place their feet over the other head of the board, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you can, do this at a mill that turns by hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And you insert two pincers into the head of the patient's arm from one side, and towards their feet on the other side, placing a palm-width piece of spice between each pair of pincers; and in each pincer, place a hole where the mill turns, ensuring the pincers are firmly fixed in the ground so they do not move. Between each pair of pincers, place a turning pincer where the joint turns, with smaller pincers of a palm-width between them to turn the mill. Then tie one rope among the axles to the mill near the head, and the other rope to the other axle near their feet. Each minister turns their mill in opposite directions along the rope, while the master keeps the spine aligned as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when they are even, place a desiccative plaster with abundant egg, and then the stoppers, and then the string of three long pieces, that purpurgues the leukoma of the yellow bile and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a bandage as we have said, and use the patient for a subtle healing until they are healed; and if any matter comes at the end of the healing, then you must administer softening and soothing medicines with the string that we have mentioned earlier; and sometimes one administers a piece of flax, and sometimes the appearance in the rear spine of the back is seen, and one should think it is dislocation; and this is the bone that shows, therefore one must not have presumption: by chance it might bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of the dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	The joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder come from dislocations alone, not in the same way as other joints; and the hip joint is displaced according to four parts: inside and behind, in front and behind; more inside it leans towards, and less displaced in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of a dislocation inside is that when one aligns the injured leg with the healthy one, it appears longer, and the injured knee is more exposed than the healthy one. The injured knee cannot bend as far as the healthy one; this is due to the swelling from an abscess, because the head of the femur has moved out of place.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes to fail, is that this accident is contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him to whom they come before, is that his leg is well positioned; however, he cannot bend the knee without pain, and if one tries to make him walk, he cannot do so and retains his urine, and swells the veins, and when he goes, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him to whom it comes behind, is that he cannot extend his knee nor bend it, and this leg is more twisted than the other, and the veins are softened, and the head of the thigh is at the spot below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The treatment for this sign of dislocation is that you realign it if the dislocation is old, and it remains in its position, then no further treatment is needed; and it must not have any presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in that which concerns the fresh dislocation, and it is of four kinds of dislocation, so hasten that you turn the joint, and stretch it inside and outside, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and has need of no other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, you must prepare a strong minister, and stretch the leg strongly with two hands, or at the ligament that is tied above the knee; and another minister extend his hand over in such a manner that he places his hands under the patient's armpits, then tie a bandage around the thigh; and another hold the head of the patient; and they stretch up and down all at once, so that the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common for the four similarities, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not so, it is necessary to treat its similarity. If the dislocation is in the shoulder blade, you must attend to the patient on his healthy side, then place the bandage at the root of the thigh, and below the angle, then set the bandage above the angle and towards the spine; then have another minister embrace the large part of the affected thigh and extend it firmly: it will now return to its place. This method of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot tighten it in this manner as we have said, it is necessary that you tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong cord above their two heels and knees, and let the affected leg be extended about two lengths more than the other; then hang it from the top of a stake, and suspend the long arms with the patient. Then command one minister to embrace the top of the thigh, and have another minister suspended along with the patient who firmly embraces the thigh, for the joint is now rapidly returning to place.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocations are displaced, the patient lies down, as we have said in that which has gilbositeit, and draw the thread above the diseased leg properly, and also on the calf; then place two sticks, one at the head and the other at the feet, then insert the stick between the thighs of the diseased person in the form; and plant moist cloths around, so that it does not blister the diseased person, then stretch each minister toward him, and the eyes place equally to his side the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	And if it returns, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	And if not, place it on the table and press it as we have said in the gilbositeit, and let the patient lie on the sound side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.
